queens favor and had so great an influence over her that whatever she asked was immediately granted she had a great deal of wit but of so dangerous a nature that those who sincerely espoused the queens interest began to lose their credit by her malicious insinuations which made them in a little time conceive as great an aversion for the sovereign as for the favorite  thus was the state of affairs when benavidez came to villa real where he staid some time before he could find an opportunity to speak with his sister because during the first days of mourning it is the custom in spain not to admit any person into the palace except the family but as soon as the queen could be seen he was introduced into her apartment where he found leonida and casilda it is impossible to express the different agitations he was in at the sight of leonida who might have discovered his secret thoughts had she perceived his disorder  after having satisfied the queen in some particulars relating to his travels he hastened to his sisters apartment but was agreeably surpised when passing through a gallery of paintings where casilda had designedly invited leonida to walk he met them and saluted leonida with much respect give me leave madam said he to acquit my self of the commission i received from the prince of carency who charged me to assure you that he will be soon here in order to conclude a marriage to which you are destined though unknown to each other it is an equal misfortune to us both replied leonida with a dejected air and the particulars you writ to casilda relating to the character of that prince have so tormented me that i have omited nothing ever since which i thought could persuade my father to change his resolution but he so strictly regards his word that hitherto my prayers and tears have had no power to move him benavidez fetched a deep sigh and after a moments silence the prince desired me madam said he to send your picture to him and i must confess it would be a trouble to me to see him receive that favor had he not a prospect of being happy in the possession of the original i cannot dispose of my picture interrupted leonida without my mothers leave therefore it depends on you to ask it of her but in my opinion it is entirely unnecessary the prince will see me too soon for his peace or mine i am not amiable enough to efface the objects which possess his heart but i will try by my obedience to deserve his esteem madam said benavidez since you consent to it i will tell madam velasco that it is the prince your lovers request speak to whom you please of it replied leonida with an air of contempt but do not call so fantastical a person my lover i can never like a man that falls in love with all he sees and even with those he never saw  as she had finished these words madam velasco who was going to the queens apartment entered the gallery she knew benavidez had been a great while with the prince of carency which made her suppose there was an intimate friendship between them and as her concern for a prince who was contracted to her daughter could not indifferently affect her she immediately enquired after his health and expressed a great impatience to see him in spain benavidez told her he had left rome and was going to the court of navarre to be at the solemnity of his brother the count of la marchs nuptials with the princess beatricia daughter to the king that the prince passionately wished for leonidas picture which he had promised to ask for him and therefore addressed her for that favor madam velasco was very much pleased at the zeal benavidez seemed to have for his friend and told him she would do any thing that might be agreeable to the prince that her daughter should sit for her picture and desired he would take care to send it to him benavidez found that his hopes as well as passion augmented and flattered himself that the plot he was framing would have its desired effect he left madam velasco and leonida to go with his sister into her apartment and after giving each other proofs of an entire affection i have something to say to you brother said she come into my closet she took him by the hand and sitting down could not help shedding a shower of tears you weep my dear casilda said he embracing her have you any thing to say to me concerning don henriquez ah brother said she he is the ungrateful object that troubles my peace and remembers no more the obligations he owes me i shall find some ease in relating to you all that has happened and as a disappointed passion is less discreet than a successful one i am going to inform you of what you know but very imperfectly  don henriquez was on board the fleet with the admiral his father when one day as the queen was hunting and we all attending her donna blancas horse started and not knowing how to manage him ran away with her several cavaliers rode after her who were invited to serve her either by inclination or interest she being perfectly handsome and daughter to leonora who was then the queens favorite as i am naturally politic enough i endeavored to reach her before the rest when i saw her from the rising ground i was on fall in a valley i rid as fast as possible to her assistance where i no sooner came but the first thing that struck my sight was a case set with diamonds which dropped out of her pocket when she was thrown off her horse i took it up and had no other reason for not returning it instantly but the curiosity of seeing what was in it donna blanca was in a swoon when the rest of the company came up they immediately gave her what they thought would restore her to her senses being stunned with the fall and as soon as she came to her self she perceived she had lost her picturecase which was sought for but in vain i took notice of all her motions and her uneasiness increased with the fear of not finding what was so dear to her this gave me the greater inclination to keep it with the only view to mortify her being one of the finest young ladies of the court and daughter to the favorite  as she had received no hurt she went up to the queen but appeared so melancholy that her mother expressed much concern i was impatient to be alone that i might see what was contained in the case but how can i tell you brother or at least in telling you ought i not to dye with shame i had but just cast my eyes on the picture which was enclosed when i found such motions in my heart as surpised me being what i never felt before i was charmed with the noble air and youth of a gentleman whose features were so admirably well drawn that i could no ways doubt but it very much resembled the person whom it was designed for i gazed at it with delight and though unknown to me i thought it was impossible to see any thing more lovely i did not consider at first how dangerous my curiosity might prove so employed some hours in admiring this fatal picture whose idea it was not in my power to deface it threw me into such reflections as generally succeed excessive transports oh unhappy casilda cried i what subtle poison has seized thy heart art thou so tired with thy liberty that thou must lose it this day i know not who this is that seems so charming i am well informed that he is in love and is beloved since donna blanca who is so beautiful is the guardian of his picture which she showed by her uneasiness to be very dear to her what hopes then can i have of any relief and to whom must i apply my self should not my birth and modesty be sufficient to impose silence on me what could i pronounce the word i love and pronounce it in favor of a man who knows not the value of so great a sacrifice no my eyes shall sooner be witness of my rivals victory and i will die before i expose my self to the shame which must needs succeed such a confession but said i a minute after is it possible that in such a little time love could have made so great a progress i am forced to lay a command on my self not to speak of my weakness and i have formed a rival without having a lover  i confess to you brother this caused so great a change in me that i began not to know my self i was continually thoughtful and solitude was the only thing i courted i feared to discover my pain or seek for means to know the author of it if i show this picture thought i donna blanca will be informed i have it and then i shall be obliged to return it she is beloved and in so great favor that i dare not declare my sentiments much less contend with so dangerous a rival  two months were over before i could hear any thing relating to this affair i sometimes enquired what young lords were absent among others they named don garcia don pedro d avilas and don frederick henriquez how could i know whether the man that possessed my thoughts was either of them i endeavored to be acquainted with their character but those who were so complaisant as to describe them to me instead of giving me some light in the matter left me more in the dark and in greater despair i made it also my business to discover whether donna blanca had not a known engagement which i was persuaded was the only thing could satisfy me but they told me she was too imperious to receive the addresses of any of the grandees i knew the contrary though i was not at liberty to declare it so that i languishd between small hopes and cruel fears donna blanca was taken ill of the smallpox at this time and there was a necessity for her leaving the court i cannot help confessing that i was extremely pleased at my rivals misfortune heavens cried i just heaven make her as ugly as possible that the passion of her lover may turn to a mortal aversion the thoughts of this gave me some ease though i looked upon my being in love with a person i did not know as the greatest unhappiness that could possibly attend me how wretched would be my fate said i to my self if this picture with which i am so charmed should only prove the painters fancy and that i should never see its original i reflected at last on which would give me the most uneasiness to see donna blanca adored by him i loved or never to have hopes of seeing the object of my passion these in my opinion were two cruel extremes for i could not determine my self on either and therefore concluded i was the most unfortunate person in the world  my mind was in this situation when in the queens apartment thinking of the odness of my adventure i went to the window from whence i saw two noblemen followed by many attendants the youngest of the two so perfectly resembled the picture that i did not at all doubt but he was the original already so dear to me in the first motions of my surprise i fetched such a shriek and threw open the sash with so much precipitation that every body took notice of it and though the queen did not seem to mind it the first lady of the bedchamber did and reprimanded me severely i recovered the disorder i was in as soon as possible and told her i was deceived by taking the young lord for my brother whom i impatiently expected the affair passed in this manner and i did all i could to suppress the agitation which might attend the first sight of a cavalier whose shadow had so much disturbed my peace  in spite of all the reflections i had made i was seized with such violent emotions when the admiral and his son entered the queens chamber for it was they that i had like to have swooned don frederick henriquez appeared so thoughtful that i was grieved to the soul i ought not to flatter my self said i that donna blanca is indifferent to him in his looks i read my misfortune he sympathizes with her in the condition she is in and thinks none here worth his notice oh barbarian cried i to my self you think of nothing but your mistress cannot you turn your eyes on me and see the deplorable state of wretched casilda but brother i am ashamed said she interrupting her self i am ashamed of unveiling my weakness to you and exposing to your censure thoughts so offensive to the modesty of my sex i shall only tell you that the queen came out of her closet and the ladies made a circle about her when the admiral gave her an account of her naval force i resolved at that instant on a thing that will appear to you no less bold than precipitate which was to write to don henriquez therefore without consulting reason or considering the consequence i took out my tablettes and addressed him in these terms  affairs wherein the heart is concerned ought not to be deferred i deplore the condition of yours give me an opportunity of speaking to you and you shall be indebted to me for your peace let secrecy be the proof of your gratitude at night i shall expect you on the terracewalk under the window by dian s statue i there shall acquaint you my lord with some circumstances in which you are particularly concerned   when i had finished my letter i was at a less how to convey it to don henriquez at last i resolved to trust the young count of oropez with it his post of being first querry to the queen gave him as you know an opportunity of entertaining us often he had a great deal of wit and having on several occasions observed his discretion i made a sign to him and he came to me i have assured one of the young ladies said i to him that you can keep a secret and hope you will answer my good opinion of you there is nothing in my power madam replied he that i would not do to convince you i am not undeserving your generous sentiments it is not my secret said i blushing i am going to entrust you with but that of my particular friend who has a mind to perplex don henriquez she has just writ on my tablettes i desire you will find an opportunity to make him read it and do not forget to return them to me i shall never neglect madam the least of your commands replied he smiling though i cannot say you have charged me with so obliging a commission as you would have me think one word more said i be assured i am not concerned in it but notwithstanding shall ever acknowledge the favor you do me in obliging my friend oropez left me immediately and acquitted himself of what i wished with great address while he was with don henriquez i was extremely uneasy at this imprudent step but was not long so for oropez came back with my tablettes where at the end of my letter i found this answer  i never could flatter my self that any person was interested in the concerns of my heart but now i am happier than i imagined your commands shall be exactly obeyed i assure you of secrecy and as for gratitude it is the least return i can make so much generosity   these words so agreeably flattered my imagination that i longed for night with the greatest impatience in the mean time i made a thousand reflections which gave me hopes and entertained me till the appointed hour the night was very dark and hearing some body approach the window i threw up the sash and asked in a low voice don henriquez is it you yes madam said he it is the man in the world who is most indebted to you but at the same time i cannot help saying that the advantage you have over me is too unequal since you know me and i am not only unacquainted with you but even a stranger to what induces you to favor me with this interview i will satisfy you presently said i in a trembling voice and that you may not suspect i sent for you hither on a frivolous subject know that i am casilda benavidez therefore my lord do not use any dissimulation but tell me upon honor whether you are still in love with donna blanca if you will not be sincere in this confession i have nothing farther to say to you don henriquez seemed very much surpised at the question and having paused a while made me this answer donna blanca is so charming that her chains are glorious and since you believe i am her captive i will not scruple to own it these words threw me into a very great confusion what do you love that perfidious creature replied i who has made a sacrifice of you and even disposed of your picture to convince your rival how indifferent you are to her with that i took a light which i had hid for fear of being discovered and obliging him to come nearer i showed him his picture and looked at him so tenderly that he might have read my thoughts don henriquez after having viewed it turned his eyes on me and i perceived the surprise was agreeable to him but as what i had told him was very unexpected he asked me how i came to know that he loved donna blanca and by what misfortune he had forfeited her esteem i can easily satisfy you both these questions replied i your absence having banished you from your mistresss heart don diego cuniga made his addresses to her and was favorably received his father you know is one of the first grandees and she being very ambitious easily conceived a passion for him of which she could not have given a greater proof than sacrificing your picture to him his vanity was satisfied but his love instead of increasing by the assurance he had of a return made him slight her and even discontinue seeing her which she resented so much that it had like to have been the cause of her death he endeavored to persuade me i was the occasion of it for that if he had not seen me donna blancas impression would never have been effaced but as i had no inclination to believe him and did not give him so obliging an audience as he used to receive to alter my disposition toward him he brought me your picture told me every thing that passed when she gave it to him and begged i would accept it as an evincement that he never more would renew his addresses to her  although i looked on him as an unthinking young gentleman i took the picture and i protest to you my only motive for so doing was to undecive you in relation to your ungrateful mistress for though i had no acquaintance with you i frequently heard so much in your praise that it gave me no small concern to see you thus betrayed by a perfidious woman and therefore i resolved to do all in my power to dissuade you from ever thinking of her more i will take your advice madam said he in a great passion and don diego cuniga shall find at his return from sevil that if i am not a dangerous rival i am at least a troublesome enemy but madam continued he with a milder voice i hope you will assist me in my revenge on donna blanca you have been pleased to acquaint me with her perfidiousness and i swear i am already disposed to have an aversion for her were you but concerned in my interest i should certainly be restored to my self which happy state i only desire that i may be the more able to lay my heart at your feet i dare assure you madam that constancy has ever been my virtue and i am so well acquainted with love that you will find in me a passion if possible equal to your beauty it is too late replied i smiling to answer a proposal which you would not have made me had you less reason to be piqud but as i am inclined to wish that your words were sincere it will be a pleasure to me when i find your conduct engages me to determine in your favor in the mean time be very secret in regard to what is past your compliance in this will be an easy way to establish you in my esteem  i did not give don henriquez time to make me an answer but parted from him with so much satisfaction that i would not have changed my destiny for that of a queen my mind was all that night employed on pleasing ideas donna blanca is sick and absent thought i and will not appear at court of a long time it is possible her sickness may deface her charms and a mistress who is suspected to be inconstant having lost that attractive will find it a hard matter to justify her self besides i have admirably well succeeded in my stratagem don henriquez is inclined to like me and thinks he has cause enough to break off with her what have i then to fear i shall have made the conquest of his heart before ever my rival can be able to come and dispute it with me  i appeared the day following at court in a rich dress which every one admired having a particular interest in adorning my self to the best advantage and i disposed every thing so well that don henriquez came and assured me he had no reason to complain of his mistresss proceedings and that he was so entirely pleased at the discovery i had made him that it lay wholly in my power to render him the most constant of lovers this declaration was attended with all the courtship that could be expected from a man passionately in love how great was my felicity in those days i was blessed with all that love and gallantry could inspire but oh brother i am ready to die when i call these things to mind and have nothing now remaining but mortal grief are you entirely disengaged said i sometimes to him and could you resist donna blanca should she endeavor to regain your heart you must needs suspect my sentiments replied he to question what i would do in such an occasion i take heaven to witness charming casilda that were she as constant as i could have wished her and more beautiful than ever she appeared to me i should no longer confess her power though his protestations transported me yet i had room to apprehend that when he saw my rival a discovery might be made in which i should prove very unhappy i secretly reproached my self with my perfidiousness and feared some punishment would attend it which was sufficient to make me uneasy therefore i pressed don henriquez to solicit his fathers consent to our marriage that they might afterward join in their request to the queen about it which being once granted i should have no longer reason to fear he represented to me the fantastical humor of the admiral but promised he would apply himself with the greatest care and address in order to prevail with him these assurances extremely flattered me and i was expecting the effects of them when one day the queen went to take the air in the forest of javalles attended by her ladies who were riding by her open chaise but we were hardly got to the height of a little hill when we discovered in the plain some men on horseback which we knew to be moors they were engaged with spaniards whom they charged so vigorously that we thought them in the greatest danger we saw at the same time a lady at the foot of the tree appearing to us in a swoon with several women about her who by their actions expressed much concern  the queen stopped at some distance and saw this engagement with great uneasiness but don henriquez who had followed us came up to her and desired leave to go and succor the spaniards which her majesty having assented to and commanded some of her guards to attend him he attacked the moors with so much bravery that the scene was changed in an instant and they being no longer able to oppose him were obliged to fly for safety all this while my fearful thoughts were employed on the dangers he was exposed to i was praying for his success though already conqueror and as i observed all his actions with a watchful eye i saw him approach the ladies who were still frightened though their enemies were fled  don henriquez had scarcely turned his eyes toward them when spurring his horse he rid full speed from the place but perhaps he considered that so great a slight to the lady who was donna blanca might displease the queen supposing she took notice of it therefore his politics or rather my inevitable misfortune forcing him to return he went up to her and alighting saluted her very coldly but what he said what so short and confused that in spite of her attention she could not comprehend it i owe you my liberty said she my lord for which i shall think my self eternally obliged to you though i am persuaded you knew not in whose cause you fought no madam answered he i was a stranger to whom i rendered this service i protest that had i known how far you were concerned i should have had occasion for all my generosity to support me in fighting for the most perfidious person in the world and for my part replied donna blanca with an air of pride i retract my obligation since you confess your self unworthy of being my deliverer she said no more because one of her women was near from whom i had this relation but called for her chaise and went to meet the queen don henriquez left her and came up first to give her majesty the particulars of what had passed and to let her know that it was donna blanca he had relieved who had like to have been carried off by the moors at this name i was thunderstruck and my imagination contrived a thousand ways to torment me representing all i had to fear from so fatal a rencounter can any misfortune be equal to mine said i donna blanca taken by the moors was going by her captivity to deliver me from all the alarms her return could be capable of giving me she is rescued from this danger and owes her safety to the arm of don henriquez i have now every thing to apprehend he is just come from her and i doubt has discovered my treachery i know not whether i deceive my self but his looks tell me he loves her still the thoughts of her being inconstant might have cured him but nothing can do it if he is once convinced of her innocence i shall appear a monster to him and become the object of his aversion heavens what shall i do if what i dread should happen whether don henriquez would not talk to me for fear of being taken notice of or that he had no mind to it i cannot tell but he did not speak to me all that day donna blanca who had not seen the queen since her recovery from the smallpox took that opportunity to kiss her hand i was inconsolable to find her as handsome as ever and her praise the subject of every ones discourse whilst i as silent as death was observing don henriquez who i thought did a violence to his inclination in not approaching her they appeared both in some confusion yet their eyes seemed to express more love than anger none but a rival could have known the cause of these different motions but oh nothing escaped my penetrating jealousy i read in their looks as i imagined my eternal ruin  the queen was returned to villa real and i in her apartment before i knew where i was or even which way i came i was lost in melancholy and thought it was very cruel in don henriquez not to show the least concern for me what said i is his passion come to this he who has rendered donna blanca so essential a service and knows i apprehend nothing more than a relapse does he thus neglect giving me assurances of the contrary i passed all that night in the greatest anxiety and though i found my self indisposed in the morning i rose early and went to the queens apartment fearing something might happen there prejudicial to my interest  donna blanca appeared at court that day finely dressed and so beautiful that all but leonida yielded to her don henriquez was just by me when my rival entered the chamber heavens madam said he how handsome she is what pity it is she is false why should her falsity affect you my lord replied i since at present she ought to be indifferent to you it is true madam answered he sighing but i only deplore the misfortune of those who wear her chains you are very charitable said i and the public is much indebted to you here such a crowd of various thoughts presented themselves to me that i was at a loss how to continue my discourse and don henriquez without enquiring into the cause of my silence had his eyes fixed on donna blanca what is this cried i you appear to me different from what you were yesterday do you repent of having changed your mind and are you still slave enough to love that perfidious creature dont you remember that she sacrificed you to a man of no merit which made me blush for her as much as i do now for you at this he interrupted me and said indeed casilda you must know me very little to frame such injurious suspicions there is not a man in the world who resents an ungenerous usage more than i and let me assure you that after i have loaded her with reproaches equal if possible to the offense i will not only show an indifferency for her but even despise her to such a degree that you shall have no reason to complain of my future conduct  he pronounced these last words so faintly that i was confounded what said i do you want to come to an eclaricissement with donna blanca you could do no more were she a pattern of tenderness and constancy i suppose added i you would have no value for such a mistress but give me leave to tell you my lord that if you speak to her i will never see you more he was surpised at these words and looked at me a great while endeavoring to penetrate into the cause of this resolution he called to mind what donna blanca had said to him which gave him suspicion enough to increase his curiosity and though he promised to comply with my commands he did it with so indifferent an air that i could no ways doubt of my misforfortune  i went from the queens apartment into my own and flung my self upon my bed half dead and drowned in tears soon after leonida came into my chamber who saw my concern and distraction which wanted very little of despair and sitting by me did all she could to soften my grief without knowing the cause of it but to disburden my mind of part of its depression i gave her an account of what had passed as she had never been in love and consequently unacquainted with what one in that state is capable of she could not help condemning my treachery to my rival oh leonida said i you little know the effects of a violent passion every thing is allowed to lovers when they are in pursuit of a heart say rather replied she that we often allow to our selves many things which are very blameable if i have committed a crime said i my punishment is near alas i was not mistaken don henriquez had found an opportunity to speak to donna blanca his impression was not quite effaced whatever reason she might have had to complain of his behavior they accused each other and by that means discovered the part i had acted i leave you to think brother whether they were not reconciled at my expense i was not long before i knew my fate for henriquez came and upbraided me with my perfidiousness i would have persuaded him he was still captivated by donna blanca and that by her artful insinuations she had prevailed and imposed on him but the ill opinion he had of me prevented his believing it as i knew his temper i thought i could not do better than confess the motive which had incited me to make him quarrel with his mistress judge the condition i was in dear brother when i owned that love was the occasion of my guilt and exposed my weakness which i was then sure would meet with a fatal return i sought for reasons to excuse my crime by painting my passion in the most lively colors and my tears convinced him of the truth of what i said he heard me without the least interruption but at last looked at me with attention and assuming an imperious air i think my self sufficiently revenged of your treachery said he since you love me and i have no thoughts of you but what are despising in finishing these words he left me the anger shame and grief which divided my soul had like to have immediately ended my unhappy life but leonida came to me at that time and used her endeavors to console me without the least success i was meditating the ruin of donna blanca and henriquez and felt in my self such a disposition for a desperate undertaking that nothing but the natural sweetness of my friends temper could moderate my rage my rival though victorious would not resolve to pardon me she complained to her mother who was weak enough to enter into her sentiments as a confident and ever since they have watched all opportunities for revenge i have by their means forfeited the queens favor and meet every day with so many subjects of grief as would deprive me of life could any thing be capable of it but the loss of the ungrateful henriquez i heard yesterday that leonora had prevailed with the queen to propose a match to the admiral between donna blanca and his son and that he had given his consent to it i shall soon see her triumph judge then  here casilda could no longer restrain her sighs and tears which obliged her to be silent benavidez who was extremely touched with her affliction told her he would fight don henriquez and neglected nothing which he thought could lessen her pain but as that which affects the heart is very different from any other so it requires more time for its cure we shall find notwithstanding in the sequel of casildas story despairing as she was that many years were not expired before she found consolation  benavidez gave his sister an account of what had passed between him and the prince of carency and told her he must needs have leonidas picture for he had thought of an expedient to make her have a great aversion for her lover but that he would not declare his passion to her till he was assured she had some confidence in him for which reason he begged casilda to solicit his interest who promised to act for him to the utmost of her power accordingly she desired madam velasco to let her daughter sit for her picture which in opposition to the young lady was immediately granted and given to benavidez who caused another to be drawn but with so awkward an air that none could see it without having a disdain for the original this was the picture he sent by an express to the prince with a letter at the same time telling him that that piece would show how charming the person was whom fate had decreed him since it was her perfect likeness and that he had entertained her with his merit but she hardly would have patience to hear any thing on that subject which convinced him her thoughts were employed on some other object  the prince who gave too much credit to benavidez was struck with such confusion at the sight of this picture and letter that he immediately wrote to him and without any caution confessed the cruelty of so unhappy an alliance and his aversion for leonida but as she had some reason to be persuaded that her picture would produce a contrary effect she often asked benavidez out of a motive of selflove whether he had heard from him and what was his opinion of her therefore as soon as he had received the princes answer which was writ in such terms as overjoyed him being that nothing more disobliging could be added he contrived that casilda should show it leonida with such an air of secrecy as if he were no ways consenting to it the thing was carried on as he had designed it leonida read the princes letter at which she was so offended that she immediately went and threw her self at her mothers feet and conjured her with tears to break off a marriage which would render her the most unfortunate creature in the world i will not pretend madam to disobey you in any thing said she but is it possible that you your self would occasion my ruin though i have but little experience in the sentiments one ought to have for a husband yet it appears to me that without mutual love nothing but continual torment can be expected for how can i value the man you have chosen for me since he has not only conceived an aversion for me but thinks me ugly and despises me cannot you change my fate madam oh rather let me never marry or if you are not pleased i should live with you send me to a monastry i will sooner embrace that state of life than be united to a prince for whom i have no inclination madam velasco moved at her daughters complaint took her several times in her arms and endeavored to console her in a most tender manner if it wholly depended on me my dearest child said she i would soon ease your mind but your father is my lord and we are both so far bound in duty to comply with his pleasure that i cannot promise you any thing till i know what are his intentions as she had ended these words don john of velasco entered the chamber the mother and daughter flung themselves at his feet and with prayers and tears conjured him to break off with the prince they showed him the letter he had written to benavidez but all would not do don john was determined to keep his word with him even at the expense of his daughters happiness he answered them that the contract was signed and nothing should ever make him revoke a thing he had concluded with the late count of la march so leonida withdrew in the greatest affliction and having informed casilda of her fathers sentiments told her she was resolved to retire into a monastry that will be no effectual relief to you replied casilda maliciously for a man who has so much power as don john will easily oblige his daughter to quit a place wherein she had thrown her self without his consent but my dear leonida your grief is so moving that i have already proposed means to give you some comfort my brother who is entirely devoted to your service and in whom you may faithfully confide has a fine house near carmona it is an agreeable retirement surrounded with spacious woods i will go and live with you there what my dear casilda interrupted leonida is your love for me so great as to quit the court i could make you a greater sacrifice replied casilda sighing you know the reasons i have to hate this fatal place the false henriquez will soon be married to donna blanca i shall have nothing before my eyes but what will increase my despair and in spite of my pride and reason i cannot cease loving that cruel man though he glories in my weakness absence is the only thing that can efface his idea let us go charming leonida continued she let us fly the man i love and him you hate my fate is more deplorable than yours replied leonida your absence will procure you some ease and no body will pursue you but as for my part i shall be pursued and perhaps discovered and brought back to my fathers house where i shall meet with very severe usage ah how little do you know the sad condition i am reduced to cried casilda do you think it a consolation to tell me that no body will pursue me that is the chief cause of my grievance i could wish the perfidious henriquez would abandon all and follow me heavens how transported should i be if you propose to enjoy a perfect tranquillity replied leonida do not harbor any wishes so contrary to your peace alas i know not what to wish said casilda then let us go solitude and absence may chance to give some ease to my mind young leonida who had but little experience and did not foresee the fatal consequences of such an undertaking consented to the dangerous proposals of her companion she embraced her a thousand times and confessed in a most tender manner her obligation for the considerable service she was going to render her they afterward agreed on a day and hour to execute their project and employed all their thoughts in taking such measures as could make it succeed  this was the state of affairs when they were informed that the count of la march was arrived at seville with a magnificent attendance and a body of eight hundred men to succor the infanta don fernand who was then at war with the moors the virtue and eminent qualities of this illustrious prince were soon published in spain and the prince of carency his brother had no small share in the general applause he had accompanied the count to seville from whence he intended to go to villa real in order to marry leonida but fortune was preparing long torments for him instead of those pleasures he would have tasted in the possession of a lady so charming and virtuous  the prince wrote a letter to benavidez to acquaint him with his departure from seville which he immediately communicated to leonida she now thought it time to be gone and without farther consideration trusted her self with casilda to the conduct of benavidez who over joyd and full of hopes omitted nothing that was necessary in this affair they left villa real and he accompanied them some part of the way but fearing his absence from the court at the time of their disappearing might give some suspicion of his having a hand in it he desired leonida and his sister to accept of one of his friends who should wait on them to their journeys end being a man whose fidelity was so well known to him that he ran no risque in trusting him with his mistress and sister  benavidez expressed much concern in parting from leonida who might have easily perceived it had not her thoughts been employed otherways he took his leave of them and they continued their journey with all the diligence and secrecy possible when they were arrived at benavidezs house where no body knew them they changed their names leonida called her self felicia and casilda took the name of beatricia saying they were sisters and of the house of leon  the gentleman who had accompanied them returned to villa real and gave an account to benavidez of their successful journey whilst the young ladies were taking the innocent pastime of an agreeable solitude  benavidez notwithstanding the impatience he had to see leonida appeared at court with a counterfeit air of gaiety but heavens in what affliction were don john of velasco and his lady when they perceived their daughter was gone they believed at first that she and casilda were retired to a monastry and benavidez seemed to believe the same saying that that was the only reason which prevented him from searching all spain in order to find his sister don john who had greater cause for uneasiness employed all means to discover the place where leonida might be but his enquiry being to no purpose he was almost in despair benavidez the mean while was proposing to himself no slender share of happiness in the success of an enterprise he had managed so artfully but the queen being then informed that some grandees of spain who were dissatisfied with the government were carrying on a traitorous design and had resolved to deliver up some considerable towns to the king of granada she ordered that benavidez who was governor of one of those places and had been impeached tho innocent should be taken up this unexpected blow threw him into a desperate condition he feared it had been discovered that leonida was at his house and that he was arrested on that account but when they told him that it was for high treason he thought himself too happy and seemed less moved for the loss of his life than the losing of leonida however his being prevented from going to see her increased his grief to such a degree that he could not conceal it from his guards which made them conclude him guilty  the prince of carency arrived at this time at villareal and did not know what to think of the many reports he heard the flight of leonida and casilda benavidezs imprisonment and the distracted condition of don john of velasco and his lady as well as his concern for a person to whom he was contracted and the necessity he was under of using his utmost endeavors to find her together with his indifferency for her all these united perfectly confounded him he made an ineffectual attempt to speak to benavidez who was so strictly guarded that he judged the affair he was accused of would meet with no favor if once convicted unless the queens goodness would prevail with her justice he heard that leonora was her favorite and having a strong inclination to be serviceable to his friend he made his court to this old lady who though as proud as great could not but conceive a particular esteem for the prince don john and his lady were so charmed with him that their satisfaction would have been completed had not his presence renewed all the grief which the loss of leonida occasioned so that nothing could moderate the affliction of these disconsolate parents  the prince of carency was presented to the queen who received him with a respect equal to his birth and merit donna leonora used to speak so often to her of his fine qualities that she soon perceived her favorite looked on him with an obliging eye and that he triumphed in her esteem over the other princes and grandees of the court he constrained himself as much as possible to oblige her being invited by no other motive than to serve benavidez oh had he known that he was working for the greatest of his enemies and one who was endeavoring his ruin he would have left him to his evil genius  one day as the queen was walking in the palacegardens attended by most of the court donna leonora affected to keep at some distance which the prince of carency perceiving he went and saluted her she received him very graciously and asked him if he would go with her into a green arbor that was not far after he had returned her compliment he led her to the place where being set down she spoke to him in this manner do you take this opportunity i give you my lord of entertaining me as a favor i seldom grant to any your youth wit and quality are sufficient motives to make you admired but as i have no inducements to create a passion be so kind as to tell me from whence proceeds the desire you have of conversing with me is it the effect of a sympathy that is frequently found between two hearts and for which no reason can be assigned the prince was very much surpised at what he heard but still had a mind to obtain her favor on the account of benavidez without intending to make any declaration that might distinguish a lover from a friend he looked at her some time as one astonished which entirely confounded leonora you ought madam said he to be convinced that you have highly obliged me in condescending to this interview which is an honor i have this long time wished for but if you will give me leave to improve this occasion let it be in behalf of the unfortunate benavidez i know the queen has so just an opinion of your good sense that she will readily assent to any thing you are pleased to promote grant him your protection it is the greatest favor i can ask your petition is not very great replied leonora in an angry tone when you employ for another the opportunity you ought to embrace for your self is it possible my lord that you can think of your friends interest and neglect your own oh i see too well that i am deceived there can be no passion where there appears so much indifferency this embarassd the prince more than ever any thing had done yet he tried to conquer himself and taking her by the hand you know very little madam said he the language of my eyes when you form so ill a judgment of my sentiments as to doubt of my passion your charms are the only subject of my contemplation and the fear of offending you was the cause of my silence this obliging confidence my lord replied she equally flatters my vanity and love for i could not think my self so happy in your favor i am infinitely pleased at the confession you have made me and since you would have me serve benavidez i promise you to do it effectually whether he be innocent or guilty he shall be set at liberty the prince made his retributions to her in so grateful a manner that she was perfectly charmed with him but as he was tired with this disagreeable conversation he impatiently rose up and took his leave  when he was alone he abandoned himself to those reflections which were most painful to him heaven just heaven cried he what am i reserved for i find my self entangled in an amor with the ugliest of women and who is the only one that ever gave me a favorable audience oh i love my unknown at nicopolis and olympias memory is still dear to me leonida prevented by some fatality has chosen rather to fly her fathers house than yield to his commands now must i to serve my friend counterfeit a passion for this favorite who is an object fitter to inspire aversion than a more obliging sentiment  though he reproached the cruelty of his fate yet he did not omit paying his devoirs every day to leonora whose passion rose to that violence at last that she determined to marry him which was the thing in the world he least thought of she sent to him and desired he would come to her which having obeyed my lord said she if in the profession you have made me there is more truth than complaisance and that you are touched as much as you would persuade me you cannot give me a greater proof of it than by uniting your destiny with mine i will not trouble you with a detail of my birth and fortune all spain can inform you of both but shall content my self with assuring you that you will find in me so good a friend in becoming your wife  my wife have you such a thought cried the prince interrupting her here he was silent but perceiving his mistake he endeavored to recover it and assuming a tender air such an alliance madam said he would infinitely please me if i were not engaged to leonida and you know it is not in my power to retract my promise no cruel as you are i know nothing interrupted leonora in a furious manner i saw your surprise and horror at a proposal you are not worthy of you have not only deceived me but have also deceived your self know sir that in this kingdom you must not dare to offend a person of my quality unpunished especially one who has as much power as the queen benavidez shall be my first victim and take care perfidious as you are that you be not the second in finishing these words she gave him a menacing look went into her closet and shut the door with great violence leaving the astonished prince in her chamber  he immediately went to madam velascos and without any reserve acquainted her with all that had passed you may be well assured madam said he that were i not even contracted to leonida i would sooner choose to dye than marry a woman who by her cruelties is become odious to all spain i know her birth and fortune are equally great but i despise them both therefore give me your advice madam and tell me what measures i must take to deliver my self from this monster without exposing the life of benavidez that is a harder task than you imagine replied madam velasco the violent temper of this woman has already sacrificed many and i tremble for you the queen loves her to such a degree that she will blindly condescend to all her desires alas my lord why are you in spain or why are you not the husband of leonida with this she burst out into a flood of tears you weep madam said he and i have reason to believe you are concerned for me do you think this affair will have any other consequence than my being obliged to quit villa real i am no subject of spain neither is a man of my rank to be insulted without revenge and i am assured that if leonora sees me no more she will soon forget me then prepare to depart my dear son replied madam velasco embracing him tenderly i will take my daughter with me into france if she is living and nothing shall alter the resolution i have taken to make her eternally yours  though nothing could be more obliging than the assurances madam velasco gave the prince yet he did not extremely wish for the performance he was in hopes that either leonida would not be found or that her aversion for him would continue in which case the marriage of course must needs break off and he would be no longer under the obligation of executing his fathers commands he immediately took leave of don john of velasco being resolved to go away the same night in order to join the count of la march his brother who was waiting at seville for the infanta don fernand to march against the moors  he retired early to his apartment and gave orders that all things should be ready for his journey but leonora who had spies over the princes actions was soon acquainted with his sudden resolution and seeing she had no means left to prevail with him ran and threw her self at the queens feet conjuring her with tears in her eyes to take pity of her weakness the prince of carency is parting madam said she he abandons me and i shall be the wretchedest creature in the world without your majesty is pleased to protect me the hopes of being his wife flattered by his assiduity and faithless protestations made so deep an impression on me that it was not in my power to decline a passion which would have united our destinies but the traitor has deceived me and i am going to lose him for ever unless you give immediate orders to have him seized what pretense could i have to act in that manner replied the queen with that complaisance which was usual to her he is contracted to leonida and don john of velasco is in great power he has friends and relations in this court and should i undertake to break his daughters contract in favor of you it would be doing him the greatest injustice besides with what authority could i do it i have no power over that young prince dont you know he is related to the king of france and that a man of his quality is not to be dealt with like other people then consider that the count of la march his brother is actually at seville and is soninlaw to the king of navarre all these things are to be weighed with deliberation ah madam replied leonora i do not intend to expose your majesty when i entreat you to detain the prince you have a good pretense to do it without my appearing any ways concerned there is an intimate friendship between him and benavidez and would it not be sufficient to make the world understand that the prince has a hand in the rebellion your authority dispenses you from giving an account of your actions and who dares inquire into your conduct the prayers and tears of this old favorite prevailed at last with the queen and she consented that a captain of the guards should go immediately and put the prince under arrest which was no sooner executed but the queen had him brought before her and having ordered every body to withdraw spoke to him in these terms what my lord said she could one have thought you capable of betraying us and that under the notion of a friend you were privately conspiring with those who intended to deliver up some towns of this kingdom to the barbarians dont pretend prince to say any thing in your defense for nothing can justify you i am too well informed of your intreagues so prepare your self to undergo the punishment you deserve your eminent birth will not protect you without my favor and if i grant you your life it shall at least be at the expense of your liberty donna leonora loves you my lord and has already interceded for grace if you will marry her i may in regard to her forget the pernicious designs you had formed against this kingdom  the prince heard with all the respect imaginable what the queen had to say then answered her with a noble and undaunted air my heart is incapable said he of forming so mean a design as that which your majesty lays to my charge and i have too much interest in justifying myself to consent that you should forget my crime in consideration of leonora no madam i refuse the mercy you offer me and demand nothing but justice which i have no cause to fear be it ever so severe go then prince said the queen you shall be strictly guarded and severely punished if guilty  he was conducted from thence to the same castle where benavidez was prisoner and confined several days with orders that no body should be admitted to him however this affair could not be carried on with so much secrecy but that don john of velasco was informed how ill they used the prince for whom he had so great a value he addressed himself to the queen about it in very warm terms and even threatened her with the king of frances resentment but she was resolved to venture at all and show no favor to him unless he married leonora  this imperious favorite who was the only person that had leave to see the prince came one night into his chamber richly adorned with jewels but so frightful as to her person that he could hardly prevail with himself to look at her nothing shall be impossible to me said she my lovely prince taking him by the hand i have every thing in my power and if you will marry me i promise to deliver you out of this horrible prison but if you are too proud and despise me be assured you shall pass the rest of your days here or end your life in a more tragic manner ha continued she perceiving in his countenance a great deal of anger mixed with disdain do you conceive less horror for the block than for my person i am not young i confess yet such as you see me i can make the felicity of the greatest princes in spain who daily offer me their sighs and vows which with mine i sacrifice to you see my my dear prince see what a shameful part you make me act i blush in confessing my weakness and your obligation to me ought to be the greater i who make all the court tremble am here before you like a victim uncertain of life or death waiting its doom say then will you decide my fate you are the only man that can make me happy and without you i am for ever wretched whilst leonora was speaking the prince of carency felt so violent an aversion for her that he could hardly command his passion but having overcome it a little he said with a very indifferent air are you not yet satisfied with what you make me suffer and will you for ever persecute me with a passion to which i can make no return i declare that in my thoughts the misfortune of being beloved by you is one of the greatest that could happen to me and since my sincerity offends you pursue your rage and let your vengeance fall on a man who can reproach himself with no other crime but that of having given you room for some time to believe he could like you after these words he was silent and whatever she could say to him he would not make her any answer  she ran out of his chamber like a fury threatening him with speedy death and from thence went directly to see benavidez who was very uneasy as one may well conceive having been disappointed in his design relating to leonida and not knowing whether she was still at his house or whether since his confinement her father had not found her out and married her to the prince of carency besides he could not tell but the crime he was accused of though innocent might cost him his life  these reflections were tormenting him when he saw leonora coming into his chamber he could not imagine the cause of so unexpected a favor and just as he was going to make his retributions to her she began in these terms benavidez said she with a voice that expressed the motions of her soul your life or death now depends on the best of your friends you are impeached and believed guilty the prince of carency who loves you entirely is actually a prisoner with you in this castle and i am willing to let you know that i have conceived a particular esteem for that prince you shall have leave to see him and be sure you use your utmost endeavors to persuade him to marry me in which case i answer for your liberty but otherwise you will have cause to fear both for him and your self farewell remember now that your interest and mine must be the same after having spoke to him in this manner she gave him no time to make any answer but went away with great precipitation  benavidez who before was despairing could not hear this news without being extremely pleased he resolved to use his utmost address in persuading the prince and as he knew the influence he had over him he flattered himself with easily overcoming all difficulties what a happiness will it be cried he if he yields to leonoras desires i shall then be sure of my charming leonida and this favorite whom i shall oblige will in gratitude employ her credit to make her mine i find it is not as yet known where she is my house has this treasure still in its possession and as soon as i obtain my liberty i will go and visit her in her retirement after having employed his thoughts on so agreeable a change of fortune he could not help reproaching himself with the treacherous part he had acted toward his friend and leonida no said he i shall never enjoy a real felicity since i must be obliged to deceive two persons who so entirely deserve my affection and will be inconsolable when they come to know one another to find their destiny changed by my perfidiousness these reflections gave him some concern but as his love transcended his friendship he resolved to arm himself against all remorse  whilst he expected with great impatience to speak with the prince of carency don john of velasco was using all his endeavors to get him out of prison he at last bribed one of the guards who having brought ropes and a file helped to cut the bars of his window and the night being very dark they both escaped on horses that were waiting for them  but this could not be done so secretly as not to alarm some of the guards who heard a noise in the princes apartment which they entered and perceiving his flight went immediately to give notice of it to leonora this news made her furious she ordered several horsemen who were all devoted to her interest to pursue him and was so confounded that without knowing what she said she commanded them to take different ways and told em that in case they overtook him and could not prevail with him to return they should kill him but after they had left her and the first effects of her passion were over she reflected on the cruel commands she had given and did not at all doubt but they would be too well executed by those villains what cried she am i going to be the murderer of a man for whom i would willingly lay down my life and do i convey the poinyard to his breast oh unjust fate why are you not contented with taking from me the object i love without making me the author of his death being thus prepossessed with dismal thoughts she was no more mistress of her self she sent immediately to countermand her inhuman orders but alas it was too late they had killed the prince in spite of his brave resistance which was so great that he would not have been overcome but by a vast superiority  leonora was saluted with this news at villareal which she received as one who already expected it and had no other thought but that of dying the prayers and tears of the queen were of no force she tore her hair and wounded her face and her extreme grief soon forwarded her death which made some atonement for the barbarity she had just caused to be acted on one of the finest princes in the world  don john of velasco and his lady were inconsolable for his loss reproaching themselves for not giving him a sufficient guard they regretted him as if he had been their own child and loaded with imprecations the memory of leonora benavidez not being so strictly guarded as before was soon informed of the princes death but his love triumphed over his gratitude which made him perfectly insensible of the misfortune of a person who had loved him so entirely  whilst these things were passing at court leonida and casilda under the names of felicia and beatricia were strangely alarmed in their solitude the gentleman who had left them safe there acquainted them with benavidezs being made a prisoner of state and accused of having a correspondence with the moors casilda at this news was resolved to go back to villareal in order to intetcede for her brother and do him what service she was capable of but leonida who feared to remain there alone represented to her that as leonora was not her friend and that through her means she had already lost the queens favor her presence instead of mending her brothers affairs would make them worse that besides she would have the mortification of seeing henriquez married to donna blanca which would only renew her grief these arguments would not have prevailed with casilda had she not apprehended that in leaving leonida who in the mean time might return to her fathers house benavidez would lose all the fruits of her artificial management which consideration prevented her journey  leonida and casilda used often to walk in a forest near their house and one evening as they were sitting by the side of a rivulet a horse ran by in a full gallop which frightened them very much seeing no body on his back they quitted the place hastily and as they were in their way toward the castle their surprise was much greater when they perceived two men lying on the ground wounded and covered with blood such a sight was very frightful to these young ladies who believing they were dead durst not approach them but ran home and called some of their servants with whom they immediately came back in order to give assistance to these two gentlemen if happily it were not too late  the ladies now having some attendance with them came up to these unknown cavaliers and found that one of them was already dead and the other still breathing leonida who had hitherto seen all mankind with indifferency seemed to have something more than compassion for the misfortune of this stranger whom one might judge by his noble air and dress to be of the first quality and as casilda appeared to be equally concerned leonida did not so much wonder at the effects it produced in her  oh what pity would it be cried leonida looking at casilda should this stranger die but what hopes can one have of his life it is possible he is now expiring in saying this she sprinkled water on his face and laid his head on her knees whilst casilda caused a sort of carriage to be made with the branches of a tree at last fetching a sigh he opened his eyes and perceiving leonida made an effort to speak to her but his spirits being wasted he fell into a swoon which gave them reason to believe his life was in danger  leonida and casilda whom i must now call felicia and beatricia when the carriage was finished ordered their servants to lay the stranger on it and thus they conveyed him to their house in great silence being perplexed with such a multitude of thoughts as would not admit of any interruption as soon as they were there they sent to carmona for a surgeon who after having probed his wounds told them they were not mortal this agreeable news changed the scene of sorrow into that of joy felicia went to his bedside and by this time he had recovered his speech which he employed in returning thanks for her generosity i can no longer deplore said he in a feeble voice the dismal adventure that had happened to me since it gives me an opportunity of knowing the most deserving person in the world but i fear madam my being in your house may incommode you which extremely lessens the satisfaction i should have to be where you are in saying these words he looked at her with so much admiration and pleasure that had she understood the language of his eyes she would have easily guessed at the motions of his heart do not be uneasy sir replied she you shall want for no assistance nor have reason to apprehend we see you here with displeasure you are now in a condition wherein silence and rest are equally necessary which reason induces me to leave you with that she retired and left beatricia behind her who as soon as felicia was gone approached the bed and said to him though may sister has assured you how desirous we are to be serviceable to you yet i must repeat the same and conjure you sir to have no other thought but that of recovering your health it will be no easy matter madam replied the prince to recover in a place where the objects i see may prove more dangerous to me than the wounds i have received beatricia who did not doubt but these words were addressed to her seemed not to comprehend their meaning but taking leave of him went to felicias apartment and asked her what the stranger had said to her she without dissembling gave her an account of their conversation which very much pleased beatricia i must confess said she he expressed himself more obligingly to me than he did to you these words gave some uneasiness to felicia without knowing from whence it proceeded  beatricia who was in a different disposition of mind proposed to her self that the only means to banish don henriquez from her heart was to yield it to another whatever trouble a new inclination may give me thought she it never can be equal to the pain i endure the man i love is now in the arms of donna blanca and all my hopes on that side are vanished but in placing my affection on some other object it may be kindly returned i had cause enough to apprehend that felicia would appear more beautiful than me in the eyes of this lovely stranger but his words have convinced me of the contrary and i am resolved to be favorable to him whatever may be the event love is a pleasing torment  the prince of carency continued ill some time and during his illness received daily instances of the generosity of these ladies particularly felicias obliging behavior to him on all occasions made him desirous to express his gratitude he began to think his preservation was chiefly owing to her tender care and by degrees fell desperately in love which threw into the following reflections how difficult a task will it be to make an impression on that unpracticed heart her modest looks and the blushes which cover her cheeks every time i cast my eyes on her evince how little she his acquainted with love and dare i flatter my self with succeeding in such an attempt no i must not hope for so great a favor from fortune i was beloved at nicopolis by a person i never knew i no sooner became captive to the charms of a lady at genoa but death snatched the dear object from me and lately as i arrived at villareal with a resolution to marry leonida i was informed of her flight and aversion to me alas my unkind stars were not satisfied to afflict me with all these misfortunes they have sent me a greater one leonoras passion for me her desperate rage caused me to be treated in this barbarous manner and her cruelty would still threaten my days with the greatest dangers were she informed that i had escaped and was now in this place but oh how can i resolve to leave felicia who is already more dear to me than the life i would endeavor to preserve all i can do in this distressed state is to change my name i am inclined to believe that as i was taken for the count of la vagne at genoa i may pass for the same here where i am not known if it be my good fortune to render my sentiments agreeable to this lovely charmer i shall never wish for a greater blessing i do not doubt but she has an affection for her sister therefore i must address my self to her and obtain favor if possible by her means the prince used often to entertain himself after this manner betwixt hope and fear  beatricia one morning rose earlier than felicia and went to see the prince who was awake and had rested very ill all night as soon as he saw her enter the chamber he thanked her for so obliging a care and told her he hoped she had reposed much better than he had done i must confess sir said she i have felt some uneasiness which i must lay to your charge since it proceeds from the curiosity i have to know who you are and the uncertainty i am in of being satisfied on that subject you judge very unfavourably of my gratitude madam replied the prince if you think me capable of not obeying your commands i am of genoa and of the house of fiesque my title is the count of la vagne i have been some years in my travels and as i was riding through the neighboring forest in my way to seville i was assaulted by robbers i did my endeavor to resist them but their number overpowered me and left me madam in the condition you saw me i know your family my lord replied beatricia and could have judged in seeing you that your extraction was illustrious the count of la vagne for now i must give that title to the prince of carency interrupted her to enquire after felicia but with a kind of impatience which did not very much please beatricia who in a cold manner made answer she had not as yet seen her as she was speaking the surgeon came in to the dress princes wounds so she thought fit to retire she went directly from thence to felicias apartment who was just rising what said she to beatricia dressed already how comes it sister you are up so early i can give you no other reason replied she only i was ashamed to lie a bed so fine a morning but will you believe i have been to visit the stranger and that i know his name and country you may as well say interrupted felicica that you know also the secrets of his heart no replied beatricia smiling i am very sincere and can assure you our conversation ended with his acquainting me that he is of genoa and is called the count of la vagne as you are to visit him next perhaps you may learn something more i have not so much curiosity as you imagine replied felicia and i fancy i shall trouble him but very little with my presence accordingly she did not go into the princes chamber till late in the evening being then informed he was very ill for his uneasiness at not seeing her all that day and the pain occasioned by his wounds had thrown him into a violent fever as soon as she approached his bed he looked at her with much tenderness and said i flattered my self more than i ought to have done madam in thinking the condition i am in had moved your pity since i find at present nothing touched you but the sad aspect of a dying man pierced with wounds and lying in a sea of blood you abandon me charming felicia and take no care to preserve the life of an unhappy wretch who is indebted to you alone for the small share he has left of it i would not incommode you with a visit my lord replied felicia my sister having told me this morning that in the state you are in nothing was more necessary than repose no no madam said he interrupting her you have not thought on me donna beatricia did not hinder you from coming to see me your eyes convince me of the truth and you only wish my recovery to banish me your presence for ever he said this with an air so moving that she could not help showing in her looks more affection than indifferency you have been here so little a while replied she that i hardly have had time to consult my inclinations yet give me leave to assure you that i find nothing in them to your prejudice and should very much regret my having known you if i thought in leaving this place you would entirely forget me she expressed these last words blushing and with some fear which charmed the prince who was going to make his retributions when beatricia entered the chamber in some disorder one of my women my lord said she who is just returned from walking in the forest found this picture in the same place where we first saw you i suppose it is yours and the person it represents is too charming not to merit all your affection the prince told her it was true the picture had been recommended to his care and received it with a deep sigh it was that which olympia doria had presented to him this gave much uneasiness to felicia who could not help desiring to see it but had hardly turned her eyes on it when her mind was filled with trouble which to conceal she retired to her closet where being alone i thought said she i had only casilda to fear but alas my fate is much more severe for certainly the person he loves is the most beautiful creature in the world and his passion is returned since she has given him her picture if he should cease to love her on my account it would be a perfidiousness that might give me room to fear in my turn a resembling destiny and if he is constant to her what can i hope she yielded her self up to these sad reflections and leaving them for others more tormenting oh continued she could any thing be more fatal than this last adventure i flew from the prince of carency because my parents would have me marry contrary to my inclination i thought my self safe in this forest where i only apprehended to meet with wild beasts but these fierce animals have done me no harm it is a stranger a dying man that has deprived me of my peace and made me acquainted with sentiments i thought leonidas heart incapable of receiving a shower of tears attended these words and she resolved never more to see this dangerous cavalier for which reason she feigned an indisposition and confined her self to her bed but could not help enquiring after the count who was now extremely ill his fever was very much increased by his not seeing felicia and his anxious reflections so tormented him that he thought of nothing but death  he was in evident danger when beatricia entered felicias chamber all in tears there are no hopes left sister cried she the unhappy count is dying if you have a mind to see him before he expires you have no time to lose felicia was not prepared for this disagreeable news which had like to have thrown her into a swoon but being a little recovered she repented the obstinate resolution she had made to see him no more she thought now she was going to lose him for ever and that such a loss would make her the most unfortunate person in the world ye powers above cried she going toward his apartment give me the count of la vagne were he never to love me should he even hate me let him live  she ran into his chamber whilst he was in a fainting fit his eyes were shut and he had neither voice nor pulse she approached him trembling and raising his head laid it on her bosom bathed his face with tears and at that instant was more to be deplored than him she lamented at last he fetched a deep sigh and opening his eyes was transported to find his dear felicia near him and so touched at his illness he looked languishing at her and making an effort to speak ah divine felicia said he is it you that gives me assistance and are you come to save me from death you need no longer fear for a life i cannot lose since its preservation is become your concern my lord replied she low enough to be heard only by him believe me your life is very dear to me and i wish nothing more than its continuance if you knew what you have made me suffer you  here beatricia interrupted them by her presence so they could not pursue their discourse but these few words produced such wonderful effects in the count that he daily recovered  how much were these lovers to be pitied not knowing each other chance had contrived to make them meet yet it was their unhappy destiny not to enjoy a blessing for which they would have sacrificed every thing such is the misfortune of some persons who purchase the most innocent pleasures at the expense of a thousand torments felicia accompanied by her sister went often to see the count who observed the care she took never to be alone with him but he could not desire beatricia to give him an opportunity of entertaining felicia for though of all mankind he had the least vanity yet he perceived by her looks and expressions that she had some favorable thoughts of him and consequently an improper person for a confidant but one evening hearing she was gone into the forest without her sister he caused himself to be dressed and though he had hardly strength enough to walk yet went to felicias apartment  she could not help being very much surprised when she saw the count who fell at her feet without having power to speak one word he took her hand and kissed it with such transports as expressed the motions of his soul felicias disorder was not inferior to his they looked at one another as if they had met after a long absence at last the count broke silence you have inspired me madam said he with a passion so transcendent that you must needs have perceived it in all my actions and i must confess i thought you took some pity on me but i have too much cause to believe the contrary since your looks express the utmost indifference oh judge how uneasy i am at this cruel uncertainty i now come to know my fate and conjure you adorable felicia to tell me what i must expect my love is such that nothing can ever make it change and were i sovereign of the universe i would lay it at your feet here he was silent and felicia replied with as much grace as modesty my concern was so great whilst you were speaking my lord that i did not consider you were on your knees i beg you will rise if you are desirous i should say any thing to you he obeyed her commands but feared to cast his eyes on her being
