like a man who expected to hear the sentence of his death we are both in a disorder said she which we might have avoided had you not spoke to me of your passion i must confess my lord to my shame that the same inclination which engaged you to entertain me has prevailed with me to hear you what more can i say of my weakness continued she blushing i discovered part of your sentiments and endeavored in vain to conceal mine i had never loved any thing before any my stars have decreed you should become agreeable to me yet do not think to take any advantage from so sincere a confession since i declare my mind this time with a resolution never to speak to you more but without having a desire to penetrate into the cause i cannot help telling you the fear i am in of being made a sacrifice to another whom perhaps you might love better than me oh madam cried the count in a rapture judge better of a man whom you have just loaded with your favors and do not suspect ingratitude from a heart that bears your image be assured a person who sighs for you can never think of any other object what have not i to fear replied she from the lady whose picture you so much esteem that shall never give you the least trouble said the amorous count presenting it to her here it is keep it as an evincement of my fidelity felicia was touched at so great a proof of his passion and expressed much satisfaction in receiving it then desired him to retire apprehending that his being up so long might do him a prejudice and whatever violence he did his inclinations he could not refuse obeying her  as soon as he was gone she reflected on all that had passed what leonida said she are you not content with hearing a declaration which you ought to have declined but also have owned to a stranger that you could love him you who are engaged to the prince of carency can you be so easily captivated and weak enough to confess your affection for another you have already shown your jealousy which is a certain proof of a violent passion what judgment will the count form from such a behavior you are going to lose his heart and become a disgrace to your sex oh unfortunate creature what must you do to atone for a fault which seems of so high a nature these thoughts gave her the deepest concern and her face was bathed with tears when beatricia returned but she took so much care to hide them that they were not perceived  the count being retired to his chamber passed his time the most agreeably in the world when he called to mind felicias generosity but could hardly flatter himself with the success he wished for oh love said he will you at last change my pain into pleasure and repair the ills you have done me amiable felicia has heard me and protested i was not indifferent to her heavens let us be for ever united that our good or ill fortune may equally affect us day began to appear before he could close his eyes he rose and went to see felicia who was alone in her closet reflecting on that which had racked her imagination all night she received the count with much civility but appeared so melancholy that he knew not what to think of so great an alteration what is my crime madam said he have i done any think to incur your displeasure you seem unwilling to turn your eyes on me are you concerned for having given me room to think myself the happiest of men and do you already regret the obliging terms you employed yesterday to banish my alarms alas continued he are you resolved to cast me at once into despair by so cruel a change no my lord replied she looking at him with an air that might convince him of the contrary i have used ineffectual means to conquer those sentiments i discovered to you i wish i could see you with indifference but i find it is not in my power do not then be uneasy i alone ought to be so the count transported with love and gratitude took felicias hand and kissed it with all the marks of passion and respect that could be expressed on such an occasion beatricia being informed they were together entered suddenly the chamber they were in and surprised them just as the count was kissing felicias hand how strangely was she amazed at seeing this she changed color several times and her eyes were animated with an uncommon fire which they immediately perceived though she endeavored to conceal her disorder  their conversation turned on a general subject and from that hour she used all possible means to prevent their entertaining one another in private these proceedings extremely perplexed the count divine felicia said he to her one have let you sooner into the secret had i found a favorable opportunity oh madam how obilging is this declaration replied the count and what reproaches do i owe myself for not having acquainted you contracted oh heavens to what misfortunes am i doomed do not afflict your self my lord replied she i am yet mistress of my destiny can you think i would receive your addresses if i had an inclination subject that induced her to send for him he asked her obligingly what were her commands to which she answered in these terms your health my lord is so perfectly recovered that i fear we shall lose you endeavored in vain to discover whether my sister or i have the precedence in you affections perhaps this question may show my indiscretion but i believe you a man of too much honor to leave me in an chamber with his arms crossed taking so little notice of her discourse that he neither looked at her nor made any answer but like a man in a violent passion was leaving the apartment without knowing what he did or where to direct his course  casilda who could not bear the thoughts of losing the prince had no longer reason in her words or actions but ran and stopped him with her face drowned in tears will you go barbarian said she what will you fly me and abandon a woman that adores you to follow perfidious leonida leave her with my brother despise her and to complete your revenge even forget her since by her behavior she has rendered her self unworthy of your love my quality is equal to hers and what i have superior to her is my constancy but what do i see oh heavens cried she looking at him with what ingratitude am i rewarded you leave me to expose your self to the greatest dangers you  she was going to continue her discourse when the prince interrupted her what would you have me do madam said he can i love any thing but leonida and were i capable of a change could it be in favor of the sister of benavidez ah do you deprive me even of hope which is not denied the most unfortunate replied she shedding a shower of tears where fury had no less a share than love but inhuman as you are dont think to live in peace with your cruelty i will find means to torment you and make you repent the little regard you have to my sufferings  the prince did not stay to make any answer to casilda whom he left in her chamber without either strength to follow him or power to speak a word but was meditating on several violent designs being divided between love jealousy and despair  after this scene it is not to be imagined the prince would remain in benavidezs house he resolved by a strict enquiry to discover the road benavidez had taken with this design he set out but could not help complaining of the adversity of his fortune can i ever flatter my self said he with the possession of a heart that has so inhumanly betrayed me what motive could induce leonida to act in so deceitful a manner was it only to sacrifice me to benavidez no i cannot harbor such injurious thoughts of one who appeared so modest and virtuous then calling to mind that she had told him she was engaged why cruel creature said he as if he were speaking to her why did not you entirely confide in me you are engaged it is true since i am the man to whom you are contracted we should have known each other and perhaps you might have loved me but instead of acting sincerely you have carried your perfidiousness to an extremity you listened to my transcendent passion and flattered me with a return only to make my despair proportionable  had his distraction been of a more moderate nature it is probable he would have apprehended farther consequences from the fury and resentment of leonora for as yet he was not informed of her death besides he had no mind to go to seville for fear of seeing the count of la march his brother to whom he would be obliged to relate his adventure with leonida and the error she had been guilty of which he could not resolve being of a generous temper and incapable of saying any thing to the prejudice of a lady he loved so entirely  these obstacles at another time would have embarassd the prince but in this conjuncture they did not in the least affect fairness of his complexion and color of his hair he carried in his countenance such marks of melancholy that no body could see him without concern the governor of that place was soon acquainted with his arrival and as he had received orders from court not to let any stranger pass that way without examination hearing he was a person of quality and a foreigner out of a compliment he paid a visit to the prince who received him with so much politeness and grandeur that after a short conversation and many offers of service the governor invited him to accept of an apartment in the castle  the prince returned his civility in a most obliging manner and desired to be excused because his affairs would not permit him to stay above one night at carmona but the other unwilling to be denied repeated his importunities and with much difficulty persuaded him to comply with his request  a noble entertainment was prepared in the castle for the prince who could not suppress his violent chagrin which the governor perceived but would not enquire into the cause he understood by his discourse that his design was to go to jaen and as he had a son who commanded a company in the citadel of that place and whose name was don gabriel dagular he told the prince very obligingly that if he approved of it he would write to him in order to acquaint him with his arrival there and added that if it were in his sons power to serve him he was satisfied he would neglect no opportunity of expressing his readiness  this free and gallant behavior of the governor engaged the prince to accept his offer with the acquainting don john of velasco with what had passed that he might act on his side for the recovery of leonida never was surprise greater than that which his letters caused at court for don john and his lady were persuaded the prince had been killed by leonoras assassins one may imagine how great was their joy when they heard heaven had preserved him yet it could no ways alleviate their inexpressible grief for the loss of their daughter they immediately thought of means to get her away from jaen where they believed she was but whilst the prince is on his journey thither let us see disengage herself were in vain she cried out and implored heaven and earth for succor she called the count of la vagne to her assistance but her cries and tears had no power he led her through uncommon ways over mountains and rocks where the echoes answering her complaints rather augmented her sorrow than lessened it  whoever you be said she to benavidez you are the most unjust of mortals his passion for you and of the favorable reception you gave him what were all my pains and cares designed for this stranger and did i expose myself for no other reason but to procure him an disposing of my destiny you may afterward dispute your title to me with the count and deserve by your services that precedence which you apprehend i give him you have one advantage he has not which is my being already under some obligations to you and so far i acknowledge my gratitude therefore i would not have you forfeit the esteem due to so peculiar a merit but dont think you shall ever prevail with me by force or by a disrespectful behavior your present conduct is a sufficient motive to render you odious to me yet upon condition you will obey me i am willing to forget your offense and all the indifferency imaginable your words bear more policy than good nature and your heart speaks for my rival besides do you think me credulous enough to believe your anger can be so easily appeased no i ought not to run the hazard of losing a treasure i have already in my possession therefore madam for my passions sake pardon my not complying with your request resolve to be mine since by that means you can render me the happiest of mankind i will go with you to any part of the world you shall be mistress of your destiny and mine then i will obey you for ever  ah barbarian cried leonida in nations they came up to them and though there was a great inequality of force yet the captain would not surrender without fighting benavidez seconded him in his defense with all the courage imaginable lend him men and money in order to dethrone my father who then possessed the crown by his birthright and the laws of the land accordingly he not only succeeded in the enterprise but even deprived him struck felicia with consternation for whilst she was at sea she had some hopes that either a tempest would arise and cast them upon the coast of spain or that the spanish fleet which was then abroad would retake em but she was too well assured that being once landed at sallee she could not any more expect to be relieved  abelhamar on his side thought death less terrible than parting with this young lady whom he would soon be obliged to yield up to the sultaness and as he had not much time to remain with her he employed those hours in representing his passion to her in the softest language love and respect could inspire but she received his addresses with so much coldness that he began to despair of meeting with an obliging return  they were now arrived at sallee and as abelhamar could not resolve to go himself and present felicia to the queen of fez he told the admiral he was indisposed therefore desired he would excuse him to her majesty for not waiting on her he approached felicia at the same time and said it is you madam that hinders me from making my court to day for i cannot attend you to a place where you go with so much reluctance but be assured that in spite of your indifferency i shall not omit any thing to deliver you from your confinement you are too generous my lord replied she in endeavoring to contribute to my satisfaction which will be purchased very dear if it should hereafter give you the least chagrin  abelhamar retired exceeding melancholy and soon after felicia inea and the rest of the slaves were set on shore by the admirals command in order to be sent to the queen alas my dear inea said felicia looking at her with a dejected air we see our selves going into captivity and till now the civil treatment of abelhamar prevented us from feeling the full weight of our misfortunes this prince now leaves us and the fine palace we see is to be our prison at these words she could not restrain the course of her tears and inea kept her company in this dismal scene till they alighted at the first court of the castle from whence they were immediately carried to the queen  they found her seated on a carpet of gold beautified with diversity of colors and round her were several embroidered cushions enriched with pearl she was dressed in a turkish habit of silver brocade flowered with crimson and buttoned with diamonds and emeralds her girdle which was set with precious stones girded a little poigniard to her side part of her hair was tucked under a muzlin veil stripped with gold and the rest hung in tresses down her neck her eyes which were large and black though languishing shined with irresistible luster but in her mein was painted so much pride and haughtiness that it robbed her of part of her charms and rendered her awful to all that approached her  leonida attended by the women who were taken with her came and flung her self at the queens feet who thought her a surprising beauty she chose her and inea to be of her chamber and gave the rest to the admiral to dispose of as he pleased the queen knew leonida was a spaniard by her dress therefore speaking to her in that language asked her name and to what part of the world she was going when they took her to which she answered her name was felicia that a gentleman had run away with her who told her he intended to carry her to morocco but that he had been killed in the engagement and she thought her self too happy in her misfortunes to fall into the hands of so great a queen she finished these words with so weak an accent that celima easily perceived she was under a great affliction she extremely pitied the youth of this lady whose noble air persuaded her she was of eminent birth be under no concern felicia said she to her i shall extend my goodness to you there are greater troubles than those you are to undergo in this palace you must not judge of felicity by appearances and i know not after enquiring into your condition and that of some sovereigns i have heard of but yours is more happy for i believe added she your heart has preferred its liberty being uncommon for one at your age to receive an impression of love leonida made no reply but looking on the ground changed color and fetched a deep sigh celima who only spoke to her in this manner to discover the motions of her heart observing her disorder perceived she was touched with a secret passion but did not take any farther notice of it  a little after the governess of the slaves ordered felicia and inea to follow her to that part of the palace assigned for their use where she made em change their clothes and as they were to wait on the queen she gave them very rich stuffs for their dress they generally went bareheaded with their hair falling negligently on their shoulders and as a mark of servitude wore golden bracelets and chains on their arms when they attended the queen to any place they had large white veils of an extraordinary fine stuff which covered their head and part of their face  felicia appeared as beautiful in this new apparel as in that she had just put off and her actions were accompanied with so much grace that nothing seemed strange to her they carried her into a room where they were teaching the slaves to sing and play upon instruments which surpised her extremely not expecting to see so great a number of handsome creatures as if celima had the privilege of choosing them out of all the courts in the universe these captives showed no less admiration in seeing felicia they all came up to salute her and amongst them she observed a young lady whose air was so majestic and charming that she took a particular delight in looking at her but what increased her attention was the fancy she had to have seen her somewhere before and that she was not unknown to her they expressed an extraordinary civility to each other and as there is generally a greater sympathy between unfortunate persons than others these two fair captives mutually contracted a particular friendship  from thence felicia in her new dress was carried to the queen but made no stay in her apartment soon after abelhamar forgetting he had desired the admiral to make his excuses to celima for not paying his court to her that night ran impatiently to the palace and seemed extremely uneasy when he perceived felicia was not with her he did not presume to mention any thing concerning her but the queen saluted him in these terms you have brought me a lovely spaniard whom you shall see presently in her slaves dress i am persuaded you will not think her less beautiful than before and i must tell you i have learnt since your departure that she who was taken in the island of sardinia is the daughter of brancaleon doria her name is olympia and  here she is continued the queen seeing her enter the apartment she will inform you of something particularly surprising celima commanded her to entertain the prince with her story which she obeyed and felicia coming in at the same time approached olympia who began the ensuing relation  a young count extremely handsome and of a merit so shining that he was universally admired fell in love with me i made him no disobliging return thinking my father would be very well satisfied to give me to a person of his quality and one who had highly distinguished himself in the world his consent my lord was the only thing wanting to make us happy but alas we little foresaw the difficulties that opposed our desires  my father displeased with this noblemans family looked on him and all his relations as enemies however for a long time his politic reasons obliged him to conceal his true sentiments which he discovered when my marriage was proposed to him it was then we knew with mortal displeasure that time only could relieve us we both labored under all the vexation that such a disappointment was capable of giving us and as our affection daily increased we could not deny our selves the satisfaction of private interviews my father was acquainted with our proceedings which being opposite to his inclinations made him so angry that he told me in the greatest passion he would revenge my disobedience to him on the object i loved these menaces caused me to tremble for this young lord whom i conjured to absent for some time and soon after a glorious occasion invited him to go abroad bagazet had conquered a great part of the levant and the king of hungary endeavoring to beat him our of it applied himself for succor to most of the princes of europe who readily sent him all possible assistance though i considered this to be a long and tedious journey and even apprehended all the dangers the count might be exposed to yet through the necessity of his absence i seconded the desire he had of going to missia  we exchanged vows of eternal constancy to each other and the grief we felt at parting i thought would have cost us our lives the event of the campaign was very unhappy the christian troops were defeated and the count taken prisoner which news i heard with a concern not to be described i sent him money to pay his ransom and was expecting his return with the last impatience when i received an account of his death it is hard my lord to imagine how cruelly such a loss affected me i could no longer restrain my sorrow i persecuted my father with reproaches and would not permit either my relations or friends to see me i thought life it self insupportable and begged of heaven to shorten its date that i might be eased of the torment i then endured  this was my melancholy condition when slumbering one night my mind filled with my misfortunes i suddenly awaked and saw a person near me whom at first i took for the shade of my deceased lover such an apparition would have terribly frightened me had my passion been less violent i found afterward by his discourse that far from being with a phantom i had cause to believe he was the same lovely man so dear to me at this sight i abandoned my self to all the joy that could attend such a surprise and showed to this cavalier all possible marks of affection he was cruel enough not to undeceive me and i was not sensible of my error till the day following when by chance my father brought him into a grotto where i had retired to indulge my self with the pleasing thoughts of the counts being restored to life  i was then informed this gentleman whom i had taken for him had never seen me before which sensibly touched me i was so ashamed of this mistake that my affliction had like to have put a period to my days my father was extremely moved at my condition and as i knew his sentiments i did not doubt but he would oblige me in any thing i desired therefore embracing the occasion i conjured him in most pressing terms to give out that i was dead and permit me to go to my mother who was then in sardignia which he readily assented to i had not far from cagliary an aunt who was abbess of a famous monastry that lay in a wilderness near the seaside where i intended to end my deplorable life concealed from the sight of any object that might renew my sufferings  my father notwithstanding the chagrin this separation gave him disposed every thing for my departure and the news of my death was spread abroad without any ones thinking it supposed i immediately left genoa and my voyage had nothing remarkable in it for i soon arrived in sardignia where my mother received me and without deliberation consented to what i so much wished she carried me to her sister who was the depository of my secrets and having changed my name i led a life so retired that without being of the number of the dead i could not be reckoned amongst the living but i used often to be alarmed with letters from my father pressing me to quit my solitude in order to return home which made me apprehend he would use his authority to compel me to it therefore i went and flung my self at my aunts feet and conjured her to give me the nuns veil that having once made vows my relations might lose the hopes of my returning again into the world  she at first opposed my request believing she ought not to make such a step without the advice of my friends but at last my prayers and tears prevailed on her she desired the bishop of cagliary to perform the ceremony and as it is the custom in that place for the person who takes the habit of a novice to go with a number of young ladies to hear the prelate in a little chapel by the seaside i went out dressed in a long gown brocaded with silver my hair hanging loose on my shoulders and my head crowned with flowers my companions were also dressed in white and in this manner we formed a procession along the shore  it is now said i my dear count that i am going to sacrifice to you the rest of an unhappy life which was destined to be yours were you sensible in the region where you are of what i do for you in this world you would rejoice to have inspired me with such sentiments i was lost in these thoughts when i heard a great noise the cries of my companions obliged me to look behind me where i saw several men following us with their swords drawn i endeavored to make my escape but two of them being come up to me carried me off with some of the young ladies and having forced us into a boat rowed immediately up to their ship where we were under sail before any one could come to our assistance  one may easily imagine that such a surprise terrified us extremely but it was nothing to the inexpressible grief which seized us when we found our selves in the hands of a corsair of algier neither our prayers nor tears had power to soften him all his thoughts were fixed on making the most of our captivity he soon lost sight of sardignia and after having taken other prizes steered his course toward sallee being sure to sell some of us to the queen who was pleased to choose me as you know my lord out of a motive of pity for i was so very melancholy that none could see me without compassion  it never came into my head to acquaint my father with my captivity nor did i wish the recovery of my liberty which i was going to offer as a sacrifice when the corsair took me it was equal to me to be shut up in the palace of sallee or in a monastry since i had no other desire than that of leaving the world and passing the remainder of an unfortunate life without any engagement  in this state were my affairs and i daily receiving new favors from the queen when a merchant of genoa who deals in jewels came to this court her majesty being desirous to see what valuable things he had to dispose of sent for him and i was near her when he entered the apartment he no sooner cast his eyes on me but seemed astonished for he did not doubt of my being dead as it was reported yet in seeing me he had cause enough to believe i was brancaleon dorias daughter since he had spoken to me too often at my fathers house not to know me again and as he immediately perceived i knew him it so confirmed his opinion that he desired leave to speak with me which he obtained of the queen is it possible madam you should thus neglect writing to your friends who so infinitely love you and are lamenting your death at genoa whilst you are living and a slave at sallee who bemoans me said i with a melancholy accent do you believe that after the fatal destiny of a person who was dearer to me than life i could find any relish for the world no as my passion was great so was my sorrow and no other motive induced me to spread abroad my pretended death only to retire into some solitude and there forever regret the loss of a man i so dearly loved in finishing these words i burst out in tears and the jeweller fixing his eyes on me with admiration you deserve a better fate madam said he and i esteem my self happy to have met with this opportunity of assuring you the gentleman you actually deplore did not perish as it was related he arrived at genoa a little after the report of your death at which he was so touched that his trouble is not to be described he admitted me to see him often but his grief would seldom allow him to speak and whenever he broke silence it was with your name he afterward fell dangerously ill and as soon as he recovered went to travel but he is now returned to genoa and i can give you testimonies madam of his eternal love  we were in a place pretty distant from the queen who could not hear our conversation but i was so transported at this news that without knowing what i did or considering why i ran and flung my self at her feet at first i was not able to speak my eyes gushed out with tears and i looked at her in so moving a manner that she asked me several times what was my request the merchant being a man of sense came up and explained the meaning of my disorder and as i had time to recover my self during their discourse ah madam said i to the queen i entreat your majesty to give me my liberty i am now willing to live and wish my self at genoa since my misfortunes are at an end no creature was more wretched than i and now none is more happy i protest to you madam i daily saw the light with pain having as i thought lost the only person that could make my felicity and desired death to terminate my miseries as it had done his i cannot call to mind all i said to the queen who was pleased to hear me with a great deal of condescension and being informed who i was as a particular proof of her esteem for my family she restored me to my liberty for which i returned her majesty repeated thanks i asked the jeweller a great many questions and desired he would procure me conveniences for my passage in the next ship that should sale for genoa but after having made more serious reflections i thought it prudent not to put my self into my fathers power till i had first consulted the count and taken measures with him to succeed in our mutual desires without running any risque of meeting with new obstacles  after these considerations i wrote to him by the same merchant who is returned to genoa in order to bring him here this is my lord what has passed during your absence which the queen commanded me to relate to you  abelhamar thanked her majesty and afterward olympia for whom he had always shown a particular value you have no reason now to complain madam said he to her hymen is going to reward you for all the pains love has made you suffer you will soon see the object of your affection and unite your destinies ah how happy is such a state in ending these words he sighed and looked languishingly at felicia who turned her eyes on the ground fearing they should meet his he also endeavored to speak to her but she carefully avoided his approach this proceeding so deeply affected the prince that he retired almost in despair the queen who was troubled with a secret uneasiness went into her closet to indulge her usual melancholy and the slaves repaired to their apartment  felicia finding inea in her chamber embraced her with as much pleasure as if she had not seen her of a long time we have said she illustrious companions in our servitude that fine creature they call olympia is daughter to the famous doria i have just now heard her story which she related to prince abelhamar oh heavens my dear inea how worthy of envy is her fate she will soon see her lover whose death was so surely believed that after his loss she determined to sacrifice the remainder of her life to solitude if you ever have felt a tender passion you may imagine how agreeable such a meeting will prove to them her eyes already shine with an unknown luster and express the motions of a satisfied mind alas continued she how different is her case and mine i conceive madam interrupted inea your uneasiness does not proceed entirely from your captivity were i permitted to say more i should judge your heart was concerned in the sighs and tears which sometimes you cannot restrain relieve your self in complaining madam and if you think me worthy of being your confident i dare assure you i shall never forfeit that honor by divulging your secret i am persuaded of your sincerity my dear replied felicia and think my self happy to have met with a person in whom i can confide but if i relate my melancholy story to you i hope you will oblige me with a recital of yours and believe what i desire does less proceed from my curiosity than the particular interest i have in all that concerns you i flatter my self with what you are pleased to say lovely felicia replied inea and to show how obedient i am to any thing you command i will now give you a relation of my misfortunes  the story of inea i am born of a noble family of andalusia where my father had a good estate and married a lady who brought him no fortune he was ever thought a gallant man and being bred up to the sea from his infancy the king gave him a ship of war he has left two daughters my eldest sisters name is mathilda who is very handsome we used to see but little company according to the custom of spain but my father having received into his house a young gentleman of a distinguished family in toledo whose name is don ramire of castro a secret sympathy disposed his heart and mine to receive impressions for each other i was pleased at his gentle air his wit and soft insinuating manner which engaged me unawares and we were not long acquainted before he declared i had inspired him with the tenderest passion  he thought himself happy in wearing my chains his fortune and merit gave him such advantages that he had no room to apprehend any of my friends would oppose his felicity and i was of the same opinion for though i resisted the infant inclination i had for him it proceeded only from the fear i had of its not being sincerely returned how unfortunate should i be said i to my self were my affection placed on a man who might receive it with indifference i ought before it is too late resolve to fly and deny my eyes the pleasure they take in seeing him the just diffidence i had of my own merit obliged me to be very reserved to don ramire and behave my self in a manner quite opposite to my sentiments which inclined him to believe i had conceived an aversion for him this thought did not only afflict him but made him so timorous that he had not power to speak to me i examined all his actions with great care and when we were together he appeared extremely pensive i attributed this to the weak impression i had made on him which created in me much uneasiness and i did the greatest violence to my self in not showing my concern but though our minds were prepossessed yet our eyes meeting sometimes could not help confessing the inward motion of our hearts ah too indifferent don ramire thought i if you are really touched in what manner would your looks express it since without being so they speak the soft language of love he told me afterward he had conceived the same idea of me and discovered in my eyes something which would have flattered him had i not given him too many instances of my insensibility  my sister passed some time in studying our looks and was endeavoring to know whether we had a passion for each other having her self a secret reason to be informed of the truth all the care she took served only to persuade her there was no love between us and that she might undertake what she pleased without apprehension don ramire appeared as agreeable in her eyes as he did in mine but the difference of his proceedings with her was very remarkable it came into his head first to acquire her friendship that afterward he might make her his confident and so by degrees engage her in his interest thus one may see how blind is love in some of his projects for there was very little probability that mathilda would act in such a character she was my mothers favorite as my eldest sisster had a right to be married before me therefore don ramire being the only person who then seemed desirous to make an alliance with our family it was thought but just she should have the precedence  i was not long before i discovered her intentions and my uneasiness met with so vast an addition that it had like to have thrown me into despair what said i complaining of my fate am i already jealous i who can hardly tell what it is to love and must i feel a thousand different pains which ought to be unknown to one of my age methinks i could approve his passion were he disposed to like me yet i have avoided him with the same caution i would have done the man i hate was ever conduct like mine my sister is taking advantage of my timidity she is beloved and in spite of that i still harbor such sentiments as ought to make me blush since they will render me the unhappiest creature in the world  don ramire whose perplexity of mind was not inferior to mine could no longer be silent and as mathilda gave him all opportunities of entertaining her one evening as they were walking together in one ally of the garden and i in another unknown to them and at too great a distance to hear what they were saying i perceived he was talking to her with a great deal of emotion at last i saw him fling himself at her feet and taking her hand kissed it so ardently that i no ways doubted but he had just declared his passion to her which meeting with an obliging reception occasioned those transports in him oh heavens what a sight was this to a person in my condition i would no longer observe them but went into an arbor at the end of the ally not having strength enough to support me nor power to resist the course of my grief  there i threw my self on the ground leaning my head on a bench and covering my face with my veil i shed a shower of tears oh how cruel is my destiny said i don ramire and mathilda love each other she has heard his declaration and given him a favorable audience for which he made his retributions to her on his knees and i can never flatter my self with the hopes of being dear to him here my sighs and tears made me perfectly ashamed and i was as mad at my own sensibility as at his indifferency but had i known what was passing between him and my sister i should have had as much reason to be pleased as i thought i had for the contrary  in fine madam after a conversation that turned on different subjects don ramire urged by the violence of his pain delivered his thoughts to her in the following manner charming mathilda i must entrust you with a secret on which depends the peace of my life be pleased to hear me and let me find in you those generous dispositions that may contribute to my future happiness as she believed he was going to disclose a secret to her wherein she was chiefly concerned she thought fit to keep him under such a restriction as not to allow him too much liberty you ought sir answered she to discover your pain to a person of more wit than me i have not experience enough to give you any advice and there are certain things i do not desire to know be assured madam interrupted he i have too great a respect for you to say any thing that could give you the least displeasure moreover you have nothing to fear since you are not interested in this affair i am only going to tell you i have a passion for inea whom i adore i hope my success from your good offices and conjure you to grant me your favor in this request in finishing these words he flung himself at her feet and his thoughts were so entirely taken up with what he was saying that he took no notice of the different emotions which appeared in her looks all that rage shame and excessive love could make one feel joined at once to torment her you love my sister said she after being some time silent and you choose me for your confident without considering that as i am the eldest my fortune must be settled before hers i am so offended at the injury you do me that were i more revengeful than i am i would instantly punish your indifferency go sir continued she speak to her your self i should render you but a very ill office with that she left him and no man was ever seen in a greater confusion he walked some time in the ally reflecting on what had passed and was now convinced mathilda having discovered her weakness to him would leave no art unpracticed to disappoint his passion for me  don ramire perplexed with these thoughts came into the arbor where i told you madam i had retired and was not a little surpised to find me there as for my part i knew not what resolution to take whether to go or stay when he put himself on his knees by me and entreating me to hear him adorable inea said he the condition i am reduced to does not permit me to be any longer silent i cannot doubt of your aversion since you not only debar me of your conversation but even turn your eyes from me i have used all possible means to decline a passion which i fear will displease you but as the torment i endure is little inferior to death whatever usage i am to receive from you hereafter only think i daily die for you  i could not imagine don ramire replied i you were so capable of deceit but your conduct convinces me of the truth you try in vain to persuade me this dissimulation is worse than the offense and i know what i am to depend on go sir i am resolved never to see you nor speak to you more ending these words i ran from him in spite of his endeavors to prevent me and left him with an air so full of pride and anger that he told me since he had like to have expired on the place his despair was so great that being retired to his chamber he was taken ill with a violent fever which obliged him to keep his bed  the mean while i went into my closer where being alone i abandoned my self to a thousand cruel reflections were i only to contend with mathilda thought i there would still be hopes of obtaining some advantage over her but the case now is such that should don ramire yield his heart to me methinks i would reject the offer he is a traitor who tells me he has sentiments for me which he has not he says the same to my sister and loves neither of us at least i have cause to complain since he chooses me for the subject of his raillery oh what fatality deludes me to love this perfidious man i fear he knows the affection i have for him which is a misfortune i cannot bear these thoughts forced a flood of tears from my eyes whilst i endeavored to banish him from my heart and i was thus depressed with sorrow when my mother sent for me i went down to her apartment and appeared so dejected that my sister who examined every motion of me did not doubt but i was come from don ramires chamber and that his illness was the occasion of my melancholy though at the same time i knew nothing of the matter nor would i enquire after him thinking he did not deserve so great a favor therefore i returned to my own chamber again without hearing his name once mentioned  mathilda persisting in her love for don ramire told my mother the conversation they had together in the garden and desired she would be favorable to her in laying her commands on me to use him with so much indifference as might destroy his hopes of ever attaining to my affection this my mother promised her and all she could wish on that subject the next day i heard the condition he was in who little thought i had the least concern for his illness though i must confess it gave me much uneasiness and compassion soon took place of my anger yet i would not go to see him whatever pain i suffered in denying my self that satisfaction  ah how great is my misfortune cried i not to have pride enough to suppress a passion which so immoderately disturbs my mind and yet have so much resentment as to deny my self the only pleasure this world can give me how is it possible i can be so cruel to a person whose idea is never absent from me and whose life i would purchase with my own  by this time his fever was so violent that the physicians were of opinion nothing but his youth could save him i was in my mothers apartment when they came to acquaint her with the danger he was in saying they believed him very near leaving the world at this news i was so seized with grief that all i could do was to reach my chamber where i fell in a swoon and continued so almost an hour  i had with me a young servant called tereza who loved me entirely and as she was no stranger to my affection for don ramire she helped me to conceal the despair i was in no cried i when i was a little recovered i cannot let him die spite of his ingratitude i find the preservation of my life depends on his heavens continued i bathed in tears shorten my days and give health to don ramire for alas without him what can i expect but unconceivable pain i protest to you madam i said a thousand distracted things the recital of which would tire you for sure no sorrow was ever equal to mine i was thus tormenting my self when my mother came into my chamber and her presence so surpised me that i had like to have related to her the subject of my grief she had just been with don ramire who conjured her in a most pressing manner to let me favor him with a visit adding that after so great a satisfaction he should contentedly die she told him any thing he desired should be granted then came to prepare me for this interview telling me how i should behave my self don ramire said she is so near death that what i am going to enjoin you i believe is unnecessary yet that i may have no cause to reproach my self i command you inea to show him all the indifferency possible in case he speaks to you of his passion i shall obey your orders with pleasure madam replied i though i am persuaded if he intended an alliance in this family he never had a thought of me you make an unseasonable declaration interrupted my mother in a severe tone for i know he loves you to distraction and it was very imprudent in him to choose your sister for a confident as being your eldest she ought first to be provided for besides it is my will pray tell don ramire so and that i had rather see you dead than his wife  my mother spoke to me with so much heat that i could not dispute the truth of what she said i presently comprehended her meaning and instead of a traitor as i thought him before i now found he was a man of honor and the constantest of lovers this no ways softened my pain for though i was overjoyed to know his passion was sincere yet on the other hand i saw my self at the point of losing a person i then esteemed worthy the sentiments i had for him and my alarms continually persuaded me nothing could mitigate so real a misfortune the impatience i had to see him would not permit me to say much to my mother i left her and took tereza with me to don ramires apartment which i had hardly entered and approached his bed when he turned himself toward me and reaching out his hand said in a weak voice come madam come and receive the last breath of a man who never sighed for any one but you though your injustice accused my heart with deceit the state you see me in ought to convince you there never was a passion more perfect it is for you i die adorable inea continued he pressing my hand it is you alone who is the cause and since it was my fate not to deserve your esteem i think my self happy not to survive your aversion in finishing these words he looked at me with eyes drowned in tears and fell into a deep silence which i did not presently interrupt being either in disorder or pleased to hear him mention a passion i began to believe and was willing to approve at last i spoke to him cease to reproach me don ramire said i cease to complain and think only of recovering i am unfortunate enough already and did not want this last stroke to complete my ruin must i lay aside the modesty of my sex and in spite of shame confess i love you oh consider what a sacrifice i make you when i own those sentiments i have so long endeavored to conceal i thought you had an inclination for my sister which gave me much uneasiness all your civilities to her i used to attribute to love and what very much increased my torment was the action you did some days ago when you flung your self on your knees before her in the garden i concluded you were entertaining her with your passion which made me retire to the arbor where you found me in order to indulge my grief that was the cause of my upbraiding you but now sir you may be satisfied for i have punished my self severely and you are sufficiently revenged in finishing these words i burst out in tears and this gentleman who before could searcely speak cried aloud with transports of excessive joy ah charming inea why was my happiness so long unknown to me i was just going with my despair to end my life but since you have delivered me from the arms of death i am resolved to live and live to serve you alone here i interrupted him to acquaint him with my mothers intentions which he protested he never would comply with i represented to him the necessity there was to affect an inclination for mathilda in order to carry on our amor the more successfully he told me his honor would not suffer him to act such a part and that he thought it more prudent to speak directly to my father concerning our marriage but as i knew my mothers jealous humor i was satisfied such a conduct would highly offend her and that no scheme would succeed so well as a feigned passion for my sister which opinion i at last persuaded him to approve  i cannot deny you any thing madam said he since my life is yours dispose of my destiny as you please i am devoted to your commands in short don ramire promised me to make his addresses to my sister in such a manner as might incline her to believe he designed to marry her as soon as i left his chamber i went to my mother and told her what he said on that point which pleased her extremely and as for my sister nothing could equal the joy she expressed at so agreeable a change  we used every day to visit don ramire during his illness and whenever i was alone with mathilda i constrained my self to exaggerate the affection he had for her which i really repeated so often that sometimes i was afraid i spoke the truth thus we managed affairs till he recovered and my family looked upon him as mathildas votary about this time the governor of porto real whose daughter had been newly married gave an entertainment with a ball at night to all the nobility of that place we were invited to this assembly which was much greater than any we had ever appeared at before don ramire who was to be of the party expressed some uneasiness at my going thither fearing my charms as he told me would create him many rivals indeed though i had no extraordinary conceit of my self i could not condemn his jealousy but rather approved it and thought i had reason to return him the same compliment we said a great deal on that subject till at last i took it into my head not to go there at all and was meditating on some stratagem to favor my design when my mother sent to let me know she was ready and only waited for me i immediately went to her but first made don ramire promise me whatever happened he would not leave the ball till he saw my mother and sister home again  we all went together to the governors don ramire gave his hand to my mother who was followed by my sister and as for my part just as i stepped out of the coach i designedly fell down and pretended i had spraind my foot so that i could not appear at the ball my mother displeased at this accident which she did not know to be a counterfeit sent me home and don ramire stayed with them very much surpised at what i had done being sensible it was a sacrifice i made him he had not resolution enough to stay by mathilda during all the entertainment but took an opportunity whilst she was dancing to go and place himself in a corner of the room and there wrote to this effect on his tablets  what torment does your absence give me adorable inea here you leave me exposed to the smiles of a woman i hate how do you think it possible for me to be complaisant to your sister when you are not by as soon as you were gone my thoughts like your shadow followed you alas this moment absent from you who is more unhappy than i and how fortunate should i think my self were i paying homage to your beauteous eyes   mathilda who was naturally uneasy not seeing don ramire by her looked every where for him and at last perceived him writing on his tablets she went and took him out to dance the sarao which you know madam was invented by the moors every cavalier leads his lady with one hand and carries a torch in the other my sister as she was dancing found it easy enough to take his tablets away unknown to him the dance being ended she went aside in order to examine them you may easily judge at reading what was wrote in em how enraged she was to find her self thus betrayed and the preference given to me having so good an opinion of her own merit as to believe it would have insured her from this misfortune  nothing could be equal to the violent passion she was in yet during the ball she endeavored to conceal it and what helped her most to dissemble was that to do her justice as she is very amiable don sanche of gusman son to the governor who was a fine gentleman but extremely vain addressed himself particularly to her and she thought she could not have a better opportunity to cure her passion and be revenged of don ramire than giving a favorable reception to this cavalier therefore she immediately gave him to understand my mother would be willing he should visit us although we are not fond of company said she yet sir your distinguished birth and merit entitle you to a privilege others cannot pretend to this invitation highly pleased him inasmuch as he had already declared his passion for my sister and could not well expect a return unless he were admitted to pay his devoirs to her  mathilda prepared my mother to receive him but did not mention the adventure of the tablets she only told her that as she was not very sure of don ramires heart a rival might give him some jealousy and induce him to conclude a marriage he daily seemed to decline while she was studying means to satisfy her revenge don ramire acquainted me with the loss of his tablets which he feared were fallen into the hands of my sister though i take little notice of her behavior toward me said he i observe within these few days she treats me with an affected civility i cannot well penetrate into the cause nor should be any ways uneasy about it only i apprehend she is informed of what we had agreed should be kept secret if you will give me leave continued he to declare my passion to your father we shall soon know what to depend on  i must confess madam the only motive i had to make a mystery of it was the pleasure of being secretly beloved by a man whom i esteemed so worthy my affection therefore i desired he would stay some time longer before he discovered his sentiments  consider don ramire said i that our condition is not so unhappy as you imagine we live together in the same house and in spite of the jealous eyes which continually observe us we see one another every day and our love is mutual  such as these were our daily conversations when we perceived by don sanches assiduous courtship to my sister that his passion for her had received a new addition we thought she treated him with so much distinction as persuaded us he would soon be happy in her favor which extremely overjoyed us for we waited nothing else to perfect our felicity how blessed will be my days said don ramire to me when without opposition i shall possess those excellencies i now adore ah dear inea does your heart sympathize with mine and may i hope to find in you those endearments which none but tender lovers can truly relish if once i am so fortunate as to obtain that wish continued he no thought of any other happiness for sure there can be none shall ever dwell in this bosom my vows shall be dedicated to you alone and the height of my ambition will only be to merit your love  alas madam you may imagine these obliging assurances from a man i so entirely loved made the days pass like hours but will you believe that while we were expecting the conclusion of my sisters marriage with don sanche her jealousy increased to such a degree that it would not give her a moments peace she was more taken up with the thoughts of revenge than with the care of pleasing a person who was proposing to her so advantageous an alliance i heard that one day don sanche having desired leave to speak to his father about it she suddenly changed color and her eyes expressed a more than ordinary grief i can no longer be silent said she to him in a cause wherein you are interested since you confess a passion for me and seem willing to unite your destiny with mine let me tell you sir you must first destroy the hopes of a rival to whom i am already engaged don ramire has obtained the consent of my family and impatiently expects an answer from his to terminate every thing before i saw you i was not aversed to him but alas i cannot now think of my fate without horror i do not doubt but your love and courage united will release me from this engagement since nothing except my inclination for you could induce me to decline it here her malicious tears interrupted her discourse and by this stratagem don sanche was easily persuaded to undertake any desperate thing against don ramire he assured her he would soon make him renounce his pretensions to her if he had assurance enough to oppose him in a place where his authority was great and in an affair where his heart was so particularly concerned adding to these words all that love could inspire  this made mathilda believe don ramire would rather yield her up than engage in her quarrel or that if he answered the challenge out of a point of honor he would have a potent enemy to contend with she must have been very revengeful to enter into a sentiment so opposite to those of her sex for she imprudently exposed at once two persons who were very dear to her don sanche impatient to come to a decision with don ramire writ to him that night in terms which showed an insupportable pride he thus addressed him  the passion i have for mathilda will not admit of a rival i am informed you are mine though it little concerns me you know who i am and that you will be disappointed in contending with me therefore i advise you to be secret in this affair and generously yield a pretension you cannot dispute without rashness   don ramire was highly provoked at readind this haughty billet and though he knew it was a plot of my sisters yet he would not let me into his resolutions fearing i might oppose em but immediately returned don sanche an answer in these terms  the indifference i have for mathilda could not have engaged me to dispute her heart with any one but your self it is sufficient you admire her for me to oppose your pretensions and in return to your liberty with me i advise you never to see her more unless you intend with your life to satisfy my resentment   as don ramire believed so violent a beginning would have a suitable consequence he went the next day to a place where he thought he might meet him as he effectually did don sanche no sooner perceived him but came up and said in a low voice without the least affectation well sir are you disposed to measure your sword with mine i am disposed to punish your insolence replied don ramire and shall expect you on the strand by the seaside where no body may prevent us they separated on this and don ramire went to the appointed place  he was hardly there when he saw don sanche coming up to him with menacing looks they both immediately drew and made several passes at each other don ramire parryd those of his enemy and soon put him in some disorder till at last he gave him a mortal wound which hardly left him life enough to confess the author of his fate as for don ramire he returned home with so much serenity in his countenance that it was to be admired he did not even think of taking the least care of his safety and seemed as if some secret charm detained him alas i am persuaded that fatal charm was my self he spoke to me with a freedom i could not attribute to any thing but the greatness of his soul and i had no room to suspect the misfortune which had just happened to him when of a sudden the governor and his guards surrounded my fathers house and snatched him from my arms in spite of all i could do to oppose em  those moments i cannot call to mind without the greatest concern the governor who was perfectly distracted as well as inconsolable for the loss of his only son came himself on purpose to sacrifice don ramire to his resentment i do not at all doubt but as he was seconded by a strong guard he would have killed my lover before my face had not i prevented him by standing between em and to save him exposed my self to all the danger for though i am naturally so timorous that even the sight of a drawn sword strikes me with terror yet i assure you madam on that occasion i behaved my self with so much resolution that i am convinced to be brave it is sufficient to be in love  don ramire who saw with the utmost despair the danger which threatened me was like a lion defending himself against a company of eager huntsmen he wounded some and avoided the fury of others but alas his courage and the little assistance i could afford him did not hinder them from seizing and carrying him immediately to prison  i thought at that time my soul would have departed from its habitation my blood turned so cold in my veins i would have followed don ramire and shared his misfortunes had not my mother and sister prevented me mathilda more like a fury than a reasonable creature loaded me with imprecations and reproaches the death of don ramire said she shall revenge me as well as the person whose fate i deplore the traitor shall be a sacrifice to the governors just resentment and my heart can receive no real pleasure till the day comes that he is to lose his life the violence of my grief would not permit me to make any answer my eyes said enough and i have well experienced that excessive affliction makes every thing but its cause indifferent to us  who can represent the torture i lay in all that night as soon as it was day i sent to some of don ramires friends desiring they would acquaint me with what they knew concerning his fate i was then informed he had been examined and the partial judgment of the court had already condemned him the governor being resolved not to show him the least favor but as there was a form to be observed in the trial they had permitted an acquaintance of his whose name was don tiello to plead in defense of his life  far from sinking under this misfortune i received new strength from its extremity it is no time now to shed tears cried i the safety of my lover is what i must think on teresa continued i you were ever faithful to me and are the only person in whom i can confide go run and buy me a suit of mens clothes for i am resolved to see don ramire i can pretend i am son to don tiello who sends me to inform him of what is passing in his affair and by that means i shall be admitted to enter the prison where we may take measures together for his escape ah madam take care what you do replied she if you are known what will become of you i am not in a condition said i that will permit me to apprehend any thing we must endeavor to snatch don ramire from the governors revenge and when he is safe i shall have time enough to think on what relates to me in ending these words i obliged her to get me the clothes which i immediately put on and fancied in that dress i might very well pass for a young cavalier  night being come i ordered teresa to take the key of my chamber and give out i was ill in bed then went out in this disguise protected by none but my guardian angels if by misfortune said i don tiello who has generously offered to defend don ramire should be with him or perhaps come in whilst i am there what must i do and how shall i extricate my self from such a difficulty love said i oh love for whom i suffer unconceivable torments be favorable to me this time you see my deep concern for the danger which threatens my lover i have little hopes and every thing to fear unless his safety becomes your care  when i was arrived at this fatal prison i hardly had strength to support me my spirits were feeble and i found my self in much disorder the first person i spoke to was the jaylors daughter i told her i was don tiellos son friend to don ramire and was come to inform him of the state of his affairs at these words she pressed my hand like a person in some concern and said ah sir the unhappy gentleman is lost if you do not take speedy measures to save him i know more of that matter than you continued she and perhaps interest my self as much the place we were in was so dark that i could not see her face though i had a great curiosity to know the person who expressed her self so feelingly but i said in a trembling voice pray tell me what you have heard concerning him all the judges replied she are devoted to the governor and don ramire will be condemned without appeal i have endeavored in vain to find an opportunity of speaking to to him but never could see him since he was brought here covered with blood and dust and in that dismal condition he appeared to me the handsomest man i had ever seen alas how fatal was that sight to me i was so touched with his misfortune that all my thoughts ever since have been employed on his safety and i am happy enough to have found an expedient which cannot fail  here she was silent but after a little pause assumed her discourse and since you are his friend continued she i ought not to conceal from you the disposition i have for him i must confess i love him and my affection is raised to such a degree that i am resolved to deliver him from hence if in giving him his life he will dedicate the remainder of it to me and render my fate inseparable from his tell him how near the danger is since he will not have common mercy shown him and that if he can purchase his life on these terms i am ready to serve him i know he is a man of quality and the vast disproportion there is between us but the condition i hope will make me acceptable to him i shall for his sake expose my family to the governors resentment who will believe my father contrived his escape and perhaps punish him accordingly how often have i said to my self laurea unfortunate laurea cease attempting a happiness that meets with such difficulties what has my passion for a stranger power enough to make me forsake my parents alas sir i have disputed with my self till i am no longer mistress of my reason i could sacrifice every thing for him he is dearer to me than life and the danger he is in affects me beyond imagination assure him from me that my heart never received an impression before i am young and though not beautiful may pass for agreeable oh how happy should i think my self if he did but like me and could his passion proceed more from inclination than gratitude i should die transported yet said she to me as you are particularly acquainted with him pray tell me whether he is not already engaged for in fine as i do every thing for him i also expect he will make me an equal return therefore go to him i shall wait your answer here in order to undertake something in his favor  though my heart was so contracted with grief that i could hardly answer her after she had ceased speaking i said to her madam your design in preserving a gentleman so deserving of life is truly generous i am persuaded he will not be ungrateful and shall let you know his sentiments when i return she left me immediately to tell her father i was don tiellos son who desired to see don ramire he made no difficulty but conducted me to the place where this unhappy gentleman was shut up alas madam where shall i find words to express the anguish and trouble i felt at that instant what am i going to do and what advice shall i give him said i must i deliver him up to my rival no i cannot bear the thought of it he shall never know the passion she has for him then reproaching my self for coming to such a resolution what continued i would i thus see him perish and deliver him up to the fury of his enemies oh sure i cannot be guilty of so much cruelty for rather than let him die he shall be hers i will with my own hand give him to her and since i am destined to be a sacrifice my peace and liberty shall be the ransom of his preservation  thus madam i came to the chamber where don ramire was confined and being let in the doors were shut again he was so extremely thoughtful that he hardly turned his eyes toward me till i spoke to him what makes you so dispirited sir said i where is that courage which ever supported you the tone of my voice made me known to him and opening his arms oh my angel cried he the only dear object of my vows is it you i see here in this frightful prison are you come to share my pains at these words he took hold of my hand and kissed it with transports of the greatest passion i sat down by him and was some time before i could recover my speech so many dismal thoughts conspired to increase my despair at last i made an effort and said if you knew my dear don ramire what is contriving against you my presence would not give you all this joy they are working your ruin and you cannot possibly avoid the misfortune you are threatened with but by marrying laurea the jaylors daughter who is in love with you and will do her utmost to save you the dress i am in deceived her and she has confessed her passion for you she charged me to inform you of it and requires your answer assuring me at the same time you will have nothing to fear if once you consent to her wishes i conjure you then by all our affection to embrace this important occasion marry her since there is no other remedy left i had rather deplore the loss of your heart than that of your life o fatal resolution added i must i even lose the hopes of ever being yours but alas what do i say it is no time now to reflect i cannot balance your interest with mine you must live sir though you live for another whilst unhappy inea retired to some remote solitary place will be dead to you and to the rest of the world  don ramire heard me with surprise and made me this reply do you think madam i shall not always prefer death to an inglorious life and that i am capable of making you the sacrifice no unfortunate as i am love and resolution are my companions and nothing shall ever make me change here i could not restrain my tears which he perceived and said cease weeping my dear inea why will you add to my calamities oh rather conceal your trouble since it is in vain to advise me to such an alliance must i speak to you no more of it replied i sighing are you then resolved on your death and mine and will your love and courage be of no other help to you than to let you fall a victim to an incensed parent whose only son you have destroyed at least strive to save your self promise every thing to laurea and perform what you please you know me very little madam interrupted he if you believe i can be so perfidious this young creature will depend on my assurances and i cannot resolve to deceive her heavens what shall we do then cried i your tender scruples are very ill timed do you consider how near you are the danger which threatens you and that your fate is almost inevitable i beg of you i conjure you to comply with laurea though you are dearer to me than life alas if i saw the least ray of hope do you think i would desire you to act so contrary to my peace oh my dear my eternal love continued i dont sacrifice your self to our mutual affection but yield to my last and earnest request  a deluge of tears followed these words and my spirits were so faint that i could hardly continue my discourse ah how fatal will your pity be to me cried he your trouble pierces my heart dont be so dejected charming inea heaven will take care of us yes said i heaven would take care of us indeed if you did but second its inspirations has not providence sent you laurea oh name her not replied he i conjure you by all the powers of love never to mention her more you are resolved to perish then said i i would live for you answered he but if it be not possible i will at least die constant and be satisfied with giving you the last proof of my fidelity here in a deep silence he embraced my knees and moistened my hands with his tears which gave a new course to mine my breast was filled with grief and in this sad moment a thought came into my head which i fancied might be executed without much difficulty  dont be against all the ways there are left to preserve your life said i but swear by your passion for me that you will strictly follow the advice i am going to give you it is unnecessary you should engage me by oath to obey you replied he you know i am devoted to your commands and though i could not consent to deceive laurea you must not judge from thence of what i am capable of doing for you well said i you shall have nothing to say to her i will be with you about this time to morrow and we must exchange clothes you shall go out in mine and immediately repair to don tiello who will have notice of it there are vessels going out a cruising and as you have relations at the court of morocco you may find an opportunity of going to a place where you will be out of the power of your enemies what madam cried he and leave you here a prisoner in my room exposed to the fury of your relations and the governors resentment must you be sacrified for my liberty no i had rather die before your face i am not base enough to resolve on any such thing i see very well said i to him in an angry tone that i must use all my authority to make you obey me since you compel me to it sir i command you to prepare your self to go off in the manner i told you i protest if you continue to be obstinate i never will see you more i retract the promise i made you of being yours and dispense you of all your vows to me so that now being free we may dispose as we please of our destinies  never was man in a greater confusion than poor don ramire when he heard me utter these words he flung himself at my feet and looked like one distracted are you then resolved madam to hate me and make another man happy said he what crime have i committed to deserve so many misfortunes i only refuse to fly this prison because i would not leave you here sure this proof of my passion cannot be so cruel an offense why will you add one torment to another i must be absolutely obeyed replied i since in leaving me here i run no risque laurea will get me out and it is with her i shall take measures for that purpose therefore if you love me do not oppose my setting you free alas madam dispose of me as you please said he in a dejected manner i am wholly yours and never would have disputed your power were it not for the fear i was in of exposing you to inevitable dangers i am now satisfied answered i for be assured don ramire if i loved you less i should not have been so displeased with your refusal at these words he passionately kissed my hand and with tender regret we separated  the jailer being told by a soldier of the guard that i wanted to have the door opened came and conducted me out but i was uneasy not seeing laurea who having veiled her self was standing in a dark passage near the outward gate where on a sudden i heard her say hold sir pray let me know what news from the person you have just seen he acknowledges your generosity with the highest gratitude madam said i and will make you mistress of his fate being resolved to live only for you i fear you flatter me replied she for i am easily deceived but if you do heaven will punish you both no said i do not suspect his honor nor mine you shall never have reason to repent your generous sentiments but when will you set him free as soon as possible answered she my father and the soldiers who guard him eat together i intend to put opium in their wine and when they are asleep steal the keys so let him out but what will become of us afterward continued laurea you shall embark together said i and rejoice at your good fortune far from portoreal thus i left her and she seemed highly pleased at the assurances i gave her  i was going toward home when i thought it very necessary don tiello should be informed of what had passed therefore i went to him and told him i had used his name to be admitted into the prison which i hoped he would approve that i had been trying means for my friends escape and as i did not doubt of succeeding we had agreed he should come to him as soon as he was free being persuaded he would be so generous as to take care of his safety till he had found a ship to carry him to morocco the circumstance is very lucky said he for my brother lies now in the road and only waits a fair wind to sail for that coast be assured i shall neglect no opportunity of serving him after this answer i desired him not to go the next day to the prison because i was to be there and should pass for his son so left him without being known and my mind was more composed than it had been ever since don ramires fatal confinement  by this time i was come home where i found teresa waiting for me i related to her all that had passed but when i recollected i had advised don ramire to lay his liberty at laureas feet i thought i could never have been capable of acting so contrary to my sentiments what could i do teresa said i for were he as weak as i have been and had fear made him inconstant by this time i should see him no longer mine and on the other side had i not used this stratagem in a few days he would be no more in the world  i found some ease in entertaining her after this manner most part of the night and representing to her his extraordinary passion and constancy his design of going to morocco and mine of meeting him there i ought not to distrust said i the promise he has given me since he declared he rather would choose death than be contracted to his deliverer and if i can get my jewels which are in my mothers keeping nothing shall prevent my making this voyage teresa told me it was easy enough to get into her closet and if i would carry her with me she would take upon her to get em though she should hazard her life for it her affection to my service so sensibly touched me that i embraced her and promised never to forsake her you must go out with me to morrow night continued i disguised in mens clothes for fear my relations perceiving my flight and the loss of the jewels should seize you as don tiello is a man of honor and in our prisoners interest i will meet him before i go to the prison and tell him my resolution of staying in don ramires place i shall desire him at the same to protect you and
