procure us a ship to follow him but madam replied she what will you do with laurea whom you intend to deceive under the notion of your being don ramire she will follow your fortune and if she discovers who you are may give you a great deal of trouble this requiring some reflection every thing i had to fear presented it self to my imagination all that night and tormented me a thousand different ways  the next morning i pretended i was extremely indisposed to prevent my mothers suspecting i had any design and as soon as it was dusk of evening teresa disguised entered my mothers closet and took the jewels as we had proposed it then i went directly to the prison where laurea was expecting me without any light i told her i was resolved to expose my life for her and don ramires service assuring her i would carry them to a ship which would soon put em out of the power of their enemies my fate is in your hands replied she and provided i am with him i love carry me where you please i am now endeavoring his liberty and do not doubt but i shall succeed in what i undertake i returned her thanks in the name of don ramire then hiding my self with my cloak went to the jailer whom i complimented in few words and desired the favor of seeing don ramire as from my father you shall see him this night and no more said he to me in a rough manner for orders are given that none but don tiello should be admitted and if the governor knew i suffer you to speak to him he would make me repent it this unexpected reception stunned me alas thought i if we do not improve this opportunity we are all undone  don ramire as soon as i entered his chamber received me in his arms and saluted me with so much tenderness in his words and actions that it showed at once his love and gratitude come my dear said i let us make good use of this precious moment put on my clothes immediately and give me yours cover your face after the same manner i did mine and if you meet laurea as you go out tell her don ramire depends entirely on her friendship teresa in whom i conside is dressed in mens clothes and waits at the end of a street to go along with you to don tiellos who is ready to receive you as for my part i shall stay here till laurea comes to relieve me alas my charming inea replied he how shall i resolve to forsake you no my only dear i cannot submit to a command so desperate if i must perish or lose you i readily prefer the first ah cruel man said i shall we then dispute for ever and will you act both your own destruction and mine how can you be so obstinate i beg you dear don ramire i conjure you by all the love you ever professed to me and the proofs i have given you of a return not to deny me this favor i fear every thing on your account but have little to fear on my own obey me this instant and make no reply  thus madam i at last persuaded him though not without much difficulty and having divested my self of my clothes i made him put em on the disguise seemed favorable to him and i was flattering my self with a successful event when the hour of parting drew near our sighs and tears were the interpreters of our excessive grief is it possible i have resolution enough said don ramire to act a part so contrary to the sentiments of my soul oh think that in obeying you this day i give you the greatest testimony of an inviolable passion i regard it as a proof of your constancy replied i which will have its reward our fortune may receive a happy change then we shall triumph over our ill stars i even feel a secret satisfaction in my present misfortune since it gives me an opportunity of showing how much i love you in what a different state is my bleeding heart cried he can i ever be more unhappy than to leave you in this frightful place and live some days without you but continued he be assured my body only will be separated from you my thoughts shall ever attend you receive my vows divine inea and let this ring be the pledge of my love heaven ordain we may be so united as never to be parted more i accept your hand replied i here receive mine and may the superior powers be witness of our promises adieu my dear continued i embracing him and bathing his face with my tears farewell my angel said he pressing me in his arms it grieves my very soul to leave you  don ramire in this manner was conducted out and as soon as i had lost sight of him all my fears for him and my own conduct came hurrying to my mind i know not madam how it was possible i could bear with the anxiety of my thoughts all that was dismal and full of terror entered my imagination whilst i was uncertain of his fate but by the time i thought he might be out of danger my afflicted mind received some relief  as i had passed but a very indifferent night i lay all the next day on the bed which made the jailer believe i was sick therefore whenever he came into my chamber he would not interrupt me but leaving what was necessary by me retired i continued in this situation till the evening when i was agreeably surpised with a visit from don tiello who brought me a letter and informed me of don ramires being happily embarked he highly commended the resolution i had shown in staying in his place with the hazard of my life to preserve his but after he had been some time with me he discovered i was not what i appeared to be the tone of my voice my complexion and particularly the emotion i was in when i spoke of don ramire with the joy i expressed at receiving his letter and my tears every thing confirmed his suspicions yet for fear of offending me he would not mention any thing of the matter protesting only he would do all that depended on him to serve me and that i could not confide in a person who would make a more generous return after some discourses of this nature he took leave of me wishing i might meet a recompense proportionable to so great and perfect a friendship i passed the rest of my night in reading over and over don ramires letter which was the only consolation i had the five days i was prisoner it was writ in these terms  i have left you my dear inea in so frightful a place and with such melancholy circumstances that you may easily imagine the condition i am in is not less deplorable than yours i must confess i was just on the point of returning to you but the apprehension i was under of displeasing you prevented my giving such a proof of my love oh ought i not to be ashamed you should have surpassed me in generosity and that i could be weak enough to suffer it yet do not interpret this to the prejudice of one who only consented to fly that he might preserve himself yours and since our good fortune equally depends on my life i shall take care of it as an offering no longer mine but consecrated to you come then speedily my angel and let us by our union taste immortal pleasures my leaving this place is deferred no longer than the finishing this letter i am going and shall expect you with impatience proportionable to the happiness of our next meeting adieu my soul adieu my only dear we shall have no reason i hope to complain hereafter of fortune since our passion surpasses every thing that has ever been known in the world   i must tell you madam i had taken teresa with me to the prison by which means i made her acquainted with laurea who supposed her to be a young gentleman and our intimate friend as they used often to meet in a place they had appointed for that purpose laurea could not help saying one day to her that she was very uneasy concerning what she should act in favor of don ramire and that she had a mind to leave him in confinement for what can i hope from him continued she i may depend on a great deal of chagrin on account of my father who will be prosecuted for his escape i shall be the occasion of the ruin of my family and how do i know but i may be lost with them it is true i am promised every thing from don ramire yet my birth is so inferior to his that nothing less than an extraordinary passion could induce him to condescend to our alliance besides he has never seen me and when we are once embarked together instead of loving me perhaps he may hate me oh i think my self already abandoned by him and set ashore on some desert island where death will be the recompense of all my pains teresa trembled at what she heard this young creature say knowing i could only make my escape by her means so omitted nothing to bring her back to her first intentions generous laurea said she i am persuaded if you knew the person you propose to serve as well as i do you would never change your resolution he has all the sentiments of a man of honor and i am sure his passion for you will be eternal the chimeras you frame to your self have not the least foundation i therefore conjure you to be constant in so important a cause which will undoubtedly contribute to your good fortune as well as his laurea ashamed of having shown so much inequality of temper made some excuses then resolved again on her first design i am willing to believe you said she and to convince you of the truth be here exactly at two after midnight i will bring don ramire to you every thing is ready for his escape and you may take measures for our departure teresa extremely overjoyed at these words left her immediately and went to don tiello to tell him don ramires friend whom he had seen in prison would be that night set free and desired he would prepare a sloop for their going off but continued she how shall we disengage our selves from laurea who will do us all the prejudice in her power if once she perceives we have betrayed her when she comes aboard said he and finds it is not don ramires concern she will be too happy to return home without discovering any thing for fear they should charge her with having an hand in his escape and if some unforeseen accident does not happen i am persuaded we shall manage this affair to our satisfaction  as i could not tell what hour laurea had appointed to set me at liberty i began to be very much tired with my confinement but in the dead of night i was relieved of my uneasiness when i heard my door open softly and saw the jaylors daughter being wrapped in my cloak i advanced toward her with my face almost hid for fear she should discover i was not don ramire i embraced her with the greatest marks of a violent passion but said little to her on the score of my gratitude she was in such disorder her self that i believe it would have been hard for her to perceive the deceit had she even seen my face in one hand she had a dark lanthorn and in the other a bunch of keys so without saying any thing to me she made me a sign to follow her which i did and we passed all the soldiers who were fast asleep as she had contrived it by putting opium in their wine thus we left the place without the least obstacle but as soon as we were in the street she took hold of my arm as if she were afraid i should fly her clingd to me so close that i was hardly able to walk  don tiello and teresa were waiting for me in the place they had appointed from whence we went together to the seaside where we found the boat belonging to the ship which was to carry me to morocco the night was very dark and laurea made me a thousand caresses i could but very ill return being in pain to know what would become of this young creature after she had discovered the plot we were not long a making up to the vessel and as soon as we came on board don tiello carried us into the captains cabin but madam how shall i tell you the surprise i was in when i found this captain to be my father who was no less astonished to see teresa and me after all the enquiry that had been made about us throughout the whole city don tiello knowing he professed a great friendship for don ramire had trusted him with the secret and declared i was that unhappy gentlemans mistress who had resolved to follow his fortune into morocco in mans disguise he started back three or four steps and not being master of the first effects of his passion was going to draw his sword when i flung my self at his feet oh sir said i forgive me remember you are my father and vouchsafe to hear before you punish me i embraced his knees and wet his hand with my tears though he entirely loved me yet in this occasion he showed his resentment by making me many reproaches and at last bid me say what i could to justify my self  i knew my only remedy was to confess the truth which i did in so feeling a manner that it moved his compassion he was very well acquainted with don ramires merit and had been thoroughly concerned for his imprisonment but being informed of his escape he expressed an entire satisfaction my father left us to go into another cabin with don tiello who was very much his friend i see said he you are surpised as well as me at what has happened you were certainly a stranger to ineas flight and did not think it was her you had put into my hands i protest to you replied don tiello i am under a consternation which i cannot express i cannot say i have committed a fault for perhaps it may turn to advantage that the affair has passed after this manner but if you will make me perfectly easy i beg you will grant me your daughters pardon whatever reasons you have to be displeased with her you see she is contracted to don ramire who is a man of birth and fortune and in my opinion you cannot dispose of her better than uniting her destiny to his i agree with you replied my father but his proceedings to obtain inea without my consent highly offend me i received him into my house as a particular friend and would have willingly given my eldest daughter to him was it nor a very ill return he made to so much civility when he engaged this young creature to disguise her self and follow him like a madwoman if you remember what inea has related to us replied don tiello she is alone culpable yet of all crimes those which love makes us commit are most excuseable and especially in a young person who has so little experience forgive her then i conjure you added he and you will confer an obligation on me which i shall ever acknowledge my father who was already disposed to favor me embracing don tiello said to him i am considerably indebted to you for entering so generously into the interest of my family and will forget ineas crime since you desire it if don ramire has a real passion for her i shall rejoice at the match and as a proof of my satisfaction i will carry her to morrocco in order to complete their happiness  this conversation ended in my favor as you see madam which i little expected for i was in the cabin so extremely afflicted that i may say no sorrow could be equal to mine what will become of me said i to teresa i am for ever unfortunate i loose my liberty in the very moment i thought my self mistress of my destiny and i am now in the power of a father who will have no mercy of me alas poor don ramire i must never see him more he will certainly think i am dead or inconstant and either of the two will drive him into despair i shall be delivered up to my mother and sisters severities which is a misfortune i can never endure  whilst i was speaking laurea looked at me with the eyes of a fury dont you deserve the fate you have met with said she nay even more than what seems to threaten you you have deceived me perfidious as you are and improved my weakness in favor of your lover i have just delivered up my family to the governors resentment but dont think to escape me you shall be my victim as i am yours in pronouncing these words she flung her self upon me and i do not doubt but would have stifled me had not teresa come to my assistance as well as my father and don tiello who hearing a noise ran and freed me from this mad creatures rage i stood in want of their help for i did not resist her prefering death to an unhappy life  don tiello saw very well to what a condition my grief had reduced me and neglected nothing to ease my troubled mind he begged i would no longer afflict my self i have prevailed with your father madam said he and he has promised me to carry you to morocco i had not patience to hear any more but upon these assurances went and flung my self at my fathers feet and embracing his knees expressed my gratitude he told me with a great deal of goodness that as it was don tiellos request he forgave me and consented i should marry don ramire at these words laurea cried aloud and made such complaints as would move any one with pity i knew by my self what she suffered alas said i to teresa were my case like hers how wretched should i be she loves don ramire and was flattered with the hopes of passing the rest of her days with him but now those agreeable thoughts are all destroyed she loves him less than you imagine replied teresa and if i had not done my utmost to make her pursue her first intentions i very much doubt the performance of what she promised you here teresa related to us what had passed between them as i have already informed you madam and don tiello told laurea the best thing she could do was to return to portoreal before day that her father might not know of her having a hand in the matter so he took his leave of us and carrying her with him into the boat they both went ashore  i had but just time to change my clothes when you came on board and your trouble madam interrupted the pleasure i began to taste at the thoughts of seeing don ramire who as yet has not heard of my misfortune he will leave morocco perhaps in hopes of finding me at portoreal his passion may make him forget the danger which threatens him at that place and i know not whether i shall ever see him more i have also lost teresa who was so true to me this poor creature was snatched from me by one of the officers in the admirals ship my prayers could not prevent her being carried off by this barbarian and i assure you madam had it not been for you i should have sunk under the load of innumerable calamities    here inea endeavored to hide her tears but could not restrain their course felicia embraced her and used many tender expressions to soften her sorrow alas my dear said she i my self am very unfortunate and did you know the cruel torments i endure you would own you are not alone to be pitied but i consider it is time for you to retire i have kept you up too long i am sensible madam replied inea i have tired your patience with the recital of my adventures but that is a fault which attends all unhappy lovers since the only consolation they have left em is that of lamenting their fate you do me injustice replied felicia if you have so disobliging a thought i am extremely pleased with your compliance and to convince you thereof i will to morrow in return confide the secrets of my life to you in finishing these words she embraced her again and inea went to her bed  phoebus had no sooner graced the watery plain but young inea impatient to hear felicias adventures rose and saluted her with a pleasant morning i wish my dear said felicia to her i had not closed my eyes all night for i have had a frightful dream concerning a person i very much esteem he appeared to me in the greatest dangers engaged with the moors and vanquished oh how my soul is alarmed your mind is so possessed with dismal ideas replied inea that you must not be surpised if they affect you in your sleep yet madam dreams are not to be taken notice of alas said felicia they would make no impression on me at any other time but what have i not to fear at present being far from my country and from a friend whose absence is the chief cause of my uneasiness though i own to you abelhamars passion for me is no small addition to my woes since i must be continually on my guard against the pursuits of a prince who has so much power in this court unhappy creature that i am were not my misfortunes great enough why must the few charms i have left serve only to render them the more insupportable dont add to your affliction madam said inea the prince has too much respect for you to use his authority in opposition to your inclinations and you may easily imagine as soon as your relations are informed of your destiny they will employ all their interest to relieve you i should be in the wrong to doubt their affection for me replied felicia weeping though in their opinion my behavior merits no favor oh that i rather owed my liberty to the man whose presence now would make me happy i find you are in love madam said inea interrupting her i confess it replied felicia blushing and since you have given me so great a proof of your confidence i promise you mine and will inform you of my weakness  felicia began immediately to relate her story from the time her father had contracted her to the prince of carency but her discourse was often interrupted with tears which the thoughts of her misfortunes extorted from her i am not only concerned said she at my being separated from the count of la vagne but inconsolable when i think how casilda betrayed me after having chose her for my friend and loved her sincerely i condemn her replied inea and wonder how any one could be so perfidious especially to a person who no ways deserved such inhuman usage  they were talking in this manner when the governess of the slaves came and bid em dress themselves in order to wait on the queen to the mosquez where they were obliged to attend though christians felicia during the ceremony of those infidels took such care to hide self in her veil that although abelhamar sought her with a great deal of attention he could not distinguish her from the rest of her companions he did not doubt but this affectation was designed which so sensibly grieved him that he retired to his apartment and wrote the ensuing letter  what crime have i committed lovely felicia to deserve your aversion you fly me and even deny me the satisfaction of seeing your beauteous face can you be offended at a passion your charms have created what violence have i not done my self to suppress my transports rather than incur your displeasure oh treat me with less severity my love is worthy a more obliging return since i am seeking means to procure your liberty which i hope to effect in spite of the queens opposition   celima being returned from the mosquez ordered that some of the slaves should come and work by her felicia was of the number and as abelhamar was watching an opportunity to give her this letter he approached her and slipped it into her lap which he thought she had perceived and would have taken care to hide it but it happened otherwise for the queen who was informed of the princes sentiments for felicia seeing him put a paper into her work found means to take it so was convinced of the truth and extremely pleased this young spaniard made no return to abelhamars passion the queen had a secret aversion to him though his only crime was that of being lawful heir to the crown she was in possession of which was a sufficient motive to make him disagreeable to her  that evening celima took a walk in the palace gardens and as she had a mind to speak with felicia she called her as it were to lean on her arm and advanced toward a terracewalk from whence one could discover the seaside with a most delightful prospect there she sat down and looking at felicia with a graceful air though you have not been with me long said she i have a particular kindness for you and am willing to tell you that if you have a mind to merit my affection you must entirely banish abelhamar from your heart i am informed of his sentiments and know part of yours but it is to be feared that a young creature as you are having no other engagement and being flattered with the hopes he gives you might sacrifice your virtues to your ambition yet i cannot believe you would consent to be his mistress for that is all you must expect from a man who certainly never will marry you i do not know madam answered felicia with a great deal of modesty who could speak to you of the princes sentiments but if your majesty is informed of mine you are convinced i have received his offers in such a manner as ought to destroy all the hopes my misfortunes might have given him the condition i am in madam continued she has not made any dishonorable impression on my heart and i bless heaven to find your majesty so opposed to a thing which i could not think on without the greatest horror for in my opinion it is more glorious to die than live a life destitute of virtue  what said the queen would you sooner choose death than be mistress to abelhamar who would not as well as i madam replied felicia and what other thought could enter into ones head this resolution is my only comfort since i know it to be an effectual way to deliver me from an infamous passion but if you have a lover in spain said the queen do you consider that in dying at sallee you never will see him more suppose there were any one for whom i had an inclination replied felicia i should be the more ready to die as being the strongest evincement i could give him of my constancy for if it were my misfortune not to live for him i never would for any other ha felicia said the queen smiling what do you tell me is it possible that cupid has already summoned a heart so young but alas there is no age free from his empire in one moment the fatal dart is lancd ending these words she sighed and remained some time in a deep silence  all the ladies who attended the queen were standing at such a distance from the place where she was sat that she could speak to felicia without being heard here said she taking the princes letter from her bosom see what abelhamar has wrote to you i believe you are virtuous therefore cannot suspect your conduct when you see him take no notice of my knowing his sentiments but advise him not to persevere in his design for instead of procuring your liberty as he promises perhaps he may lose his own for the rest of his days this she pronounced with a melancholy accent then rose and returned to the palace  felicia overjoyed at what the queen had said to her joined inea whom she desired to stay with her in the garden and they both went and sat down in the same place which celima had just quitted notwithstanding all the misfortunes that afflict me said felicia to her companion i have cause to bless heaven for the disposition the queen is in she forbids me receiving the princes addresses think my dear how willing i am to obey her and whether she had need to use her authority on this occasion i congratulate you answered inea since it adds to your comfort but i cannot conceive out of what motive she opposes a thing which ought to be indifferent to her unless she has her self taken an affection for him i am apt to believe said felicia her thoughts are employed on some object and that her heart is not entirely free from love for when she asked me whether i had any engagement i perceived she grew of a sudden so pensive that it was some time before she could recover her self yet i cannot think she likes the young prince for as she is mistress of her destiny i suppose she might make him her husband if it were her pleasure i rather believe she intends to keep him under an absolute submission to her will can she be so little acquainted with the motions of a heart interrupted inea to imagine abelhamars sentiments will receive laws from a sovereign whom he has some reason to hate as for my part i know it would be impossible for me either to love or not love by command i might so far prevail with my self as to be silent or to counterfeit an indifference and yet i cannot tell whether i should act that part so well as to please those who would lay such a duty on me i shall not dispute with you on that subject replied felicia but between us i esteem it a great happiness that my inclination is so ready to comply with the queens commands  as she had finished her discourse she perceived a man near her whom by the light of the moon she knew to be abelhamar which not a little surpised her she rose in order to run from him but he took hold of her and said do not fly me thus cruel felicia i am unfortunate enough to have heard your conversation with celima and could wish my self dead rather than give you the displeasure of seeing me once more at your feet here he was silent but after some time continued in this manner what did i think one whom i looked on a divinity would approve of the unjust queens barbarity and reduce me to the last despair by an inhumane usage take care ungrateful felicia how you behave your self toward me i am not here among strangers and celima who would fain dispose of my heart as she does of my crown may find fortune is not always constant and that usurpers have ever cause to fear my lord replied felicia i perceive you heard what the queen said relating to you i must not concern my self in affairs of state and since you know my sentiments i shall make no diffiulty in confessing them it is true i was sensibly pleased to receive a command so positive and conformable to my inclination for i cannot love an enemy to my country and religion why have i treated you like an enemy answered the prince what advantage did i take of my victory was it a crime to love and serve you i am sensible of all you acted for me interrupted felicia and my gratitude is equal to your favors accept of it then my lord as the only return i can make and it is even more than the queen will consent to  the prince falling into a violent passion leaned himself against a ballister of marble pillars which boarded the terracewalk and looking at felicia with despair in his countenance i swear said he by our great mahomet and by my love that if i dont enjoy you i will put the kingdom of fez into desolation pull down from the throne the unworthy princess who sits on it and burn this magnificent palace to ashes you shall see felicia what such a lover as i can do when he finds himself despised your eyes shall cause more confusion amongst us than any revolution ever did oh heavens my lord cried felicia can any thing be more dreadful than such designs what for an unfortunate slave as i am would you disturb the peace of this nation are not my woes great enough already must you attempt to force me away from the queen after i have declared to you that i will resolve on death sooner than consent to your desires my lord since i must confess it i am in love with one in spain and i will as willingly give my life as marry any other absence it self shall never lessen my affection for him i know the way to be constant and preserve my heart for one who  no i can hear you no longer said the prince interrupting her you endeavor to distract me with the cruelest things you can imagine but in time i will be revenged on you the queen and that dangerous rival finishing these words he left felicia  her affliction was so great that she had hardly reached the palace when she was seized with a violent fever which continued all that night the governess of the slaves went next morning to acquaint the queen of it who sent olympia doria to stay by her as soon as felicia saw her enter the chamber she said to her with a languishing air the condition i am in madam will only give you uneasiness and the company of so unfortunate a creature as i can be no ways agreeable to you i cannot tell whether it be a pleasure to you to see me answered olympia but i know very well nothing can give me a greater satisfaction than being with you and though i am in expectation of the only happiness that can bless my days yet in quitting this palace i cannot help regretting the absence of my charming felicia how obliging you are my dearest companion replied she but alas i shall have the greatest cause to regret when i see you no more what consolation would it be me were i going with you to genoa i have some reasons to wish it i will not presume to ask em said olympia fearing you should think my curiosity too great but if you will tell me why you are so desirous of going that voyage i shall take it as a mighty favor i will grant your request replied felicia as soon as my health permits me and shall desire you also to was in  the mean while felicia and inea entertained each other with their grief whenever they found an opportunity of being alone should i inform the queen of abelhamars menaces said felicia to her friend she would take such measures as might secure the peace and tranquillity of her kingdom and by sending me for spain deliver me from his violence but continued she after a moments pause what reproaches should not i deserve supposing this young prince was only urged by his passion to speak as he did without having any thoughts of executing so rash a design and that upon my information he should be arrested then his disgrace and perhaps the loss of his life would be owing to me what an ungrateful return should i make to the obliging sentiments he conceived for me from the beginning of my misfortune inea approved very much her prudent considerations and represented to her how willingly the queen would embrace that pretense to make a sacrifice of abelhamar whose passion she only opposed with a design to provoke him to use her with disrespect which would consequently bring him to inevitable punishment and were it otherways it would not stand with reason that the queen should concern her self with any thing so much below her as a slave felicia was of ineas opinion and thought there was so much probability in what she said that she chose rather to be silent in the matter than make a discovery which might be the cause of greater disorders so implored the assistance of heaven for her deliverance as for inea she had already writ the particulars of her voyage to her dear don ramire and was impatiently waiting his answer  abelhamar whose passion was grown desperate retired from the queens palace to his own and there confined himself with his faithful mula cease garden distracted and melancholy i perceived at a distance celima followed by her women and to avoid paying my court to her i retired to a grotto under the terracewalk which i had just entered when the queen leaning on felicias arm came and seated her self in a place where i could distinctly hear all they said no mula it is not possible to express the intolerable aversion she has to me and with what disdain she speaks of me she has given reiterated commands to that lovely captive to fly and hate me who ungrateful as she is not only received em with pleasure but even promised celima more than she required of her and it was not long before i felt the effect of it for as soon as the queen was gone back to the palace and i could find an opportunity to speak to this young slave she confirmed with a most rigorous air what i had already heard and moreover told me she was in love with one in spain and that nothing in the world should ever make her change in a word i find there is no time to be lost i must immediately adhere to the king of tituans proposals that prince extremely resents celimas refusal a slighted passion demands revenge and he looks on me as one who is capable of assisting him before i had seen felicia i would not favor his designs thinking the queen might choose me to reign with her now i see my error she not only hates me but even opposes my happiness wherever i seek it  if i may be permitted to give you my advice my lord replied mula i am of opinion you should speak to celima before you enter into the king of tituans interest and try whether you cannot bring her into a more favorable disposition for you it is probable she may make some serious reflection and for her own sake not provoke you to act any thing desperate i am willing to make that one step more said the prince though ever so nice but as i believe the queen has a design to take me up let us be prepared for the worst if i am put in arrest do you go to tunis tell ismael the number of friends i have in this court and manage affairs so as by his assistance and theirs i may obtain my liberty possess my love and be revenged  it was late before abelhamar had ended his conversation which prevented him from going the next morning to the queens apartment and the first thing he heard was felicias illness this news caused him to be extremely uneasy he soon forgot all other projects and fixed his chiefest thoughts on seeking means to see the person he loved which met with some opposition celima having given orders he should not be admitted into her chamber and as for the governess of the slaves he could not flatter himself with the hopes of gaining her being an old woman entirely devoted to the queens will so that he was almost despairing of success in his enterprise but what is not love capable of it conquers all difficulties  the prince being young and handsome resolved to disguise himself in womans clothes in order to be presented to the queen by a captain of a ship with whom he was particularly acquainted he was a perfect master of the spanish tongue and did not doubt but he might easily pass for one of that nation he told his design to mula who used his endeavors to divert him from an attempt which might prove fatal to him but his arguments were of little weight where love had so great an influence he ordered immediately his physician to be called and bid him give out every where he was dangerously ill of a fever and that it was convenient he should see no company this news being talked of at court the seacaptain brought him to the palace among several other slaves which he had lately taken the queen took a particular notice of abelhamar and asked him some questions which might have puzzled him had not his wit been prevailing and his replies so ingenious that they did not give her the least suspicion of a disguise the governess of the slaves having asked his name he told her he was called eugenia and that he was a native of the kingdom of castile the queen ordered she should be conducted to felicia who perhaps might know her and be much pleased to see one of her country  abelhamar was sent in this manner to felicia who was in bed very much indisposed he no sooner entered her chamber but seeing her in this condition he turned pale and seemed so dejected that it would have pitied any one that was present at this interview as felicia and inea believed this new slaves affliction proceeded from her late misfortune they were no ways surpised at the disorder she was in but endeavored by their kind expressions to soften the rigor of her unhappy state  the amorous prince thus continued with his dear felicia and the oftener he saw her the greater were the effects of her charms which at last so potently influenced him that he could not resolve to quit the palace esteeming himself too happy in the company of his adorable mistress he had so many perfections that it would have been easy for him to make the conquest of the queens handsomest slaves had he made the least pursuit toward it but his heart was entirely filled with felicias idea and all his thoughts were employed on the only care of pleasing her  she also very much contributed by her innocent caresses to detain him their humors agreed so well that she desired as a favor they would let eugenia stay with her during her illness there is a secret charm in your conversation said she sometimes to her which gives me a much greater pleasure than any i can find in that of my other companions it is the effect of my love for you beauteous felicia that inspires you with this sympathy replied the passionate prince and how blessed should i be were i as dear to you as you are to me but continued he if you will give me leave to tell you my thoughts i believe you are indifferent whether beloved or not alas how great would be my felicity answered felicia with a melancholy tone were i such as you represent me you little know my sentiments they give me more uneasiness than my unfortunate captivity what madam said the pretended eugenia is it possible that after having wholly resigned my self to you you would make any thing a secret to me if your heart is touched with a tender passion will it not be a comfort to you to make me your confident what shall i say to you replied felicia i can only tell you my weakness and confess an engagement which is so dear to me that it fills my soul at once with a thousand different motions these words cruelly affected the prince who could not utter one syllable but turning pale he fixed his eyes on her and continued some time in this posture as astonished at what she said though she had already declared her sentiments to him in the garden at last he endeavored to speak and with a languishing accent said i should not be surpised so perfect a creature as you were adored yet felicia i flattered my self that far from having lost your liberty you were free from any passion this opinion pleased me extremely for although we are of one sex i must tell you i take delight in gaining the affections of a young unpracticed heart who is unacquainted with sentiments so destructive to our peace this made me conceive a particular friendship for you but i understand your disdain for some is equal to your weakness for others oh what shame and disorder do you cause in me replied felicia covering her face with her handkerchief i expected in telling you my secret you would have pitied and consold me alas do you upbraid me eugenia your severity will compel me hereafter to fear and fly you the unhappy prince at these words flung himself on his knees and taking her hand kissed and bathed it with tears his speech was suppressed with sighs which would have been sufficient to discover him were it not that felicia had a strong opinion of his being of her own sex and did not in the least take notice of his passionate expressions  inea entered the chamber whilst they were in this silent and melancholy condition what is the cause of this sorrow said she is this the way eugenia you entertain our dear sick lady you have without doubt said something to her which renews the remembrance of her past misfortunes i have said nothing to felicia interrupted the prince immediately but what was agreeable to her therefore do not accuse me i would undergo any pain my self rather than aggravate hers alas inea said felicia here cruel eugenia has been reproaching me with sentiments i have for a person whom she her self would love were she as well acquainted with him as i am no replied eugenia i am convinced of the contrary i even have an invincible aversion to this unknown who perfidiously robs me of your heart which is a crime not to be forgiven this is no subject to create a dispute between you and i said felicia the affection we have for a lover or a friend is of so different a nature that the one does no prejudice to the other give me leave to tell you cried the young prince that when a heart is touched with a powerful passion it is incapable of receiving any other impression then you dont believe i love you eugenia interrupted felicia i know not what to believe replied the prince but what i am assured of is no creature can be in greater despair as he ended these words olympia entered the chamber  it is given out in the palace said she that prince abelhamar having counterfeited a sickness is gone away secretly in order to assist ismael king of tunis who intends to declare war against the queen which news has so much alarmed her that she has given orders to search his apartment in spite of what his physician says to oppose his being seen and if it be possible to penetrate into the queens sentiments by her uneasiness she is in a great apprehension concerning the consequence of this sudden departure the queens thoughts and mine are as different as our interest replied felicia she is concerned at the princes being gone and i am overjoyed at it abelhamar who had not interrupted olympias discourse could not help looking earnestly at felicia that prince is very unfortunate said he that his absence should give you so much pleasure i perceive the love and respect he has for you meet with a very unkind return what is become of that complaisance you showed us at first my dear eugenia replied felicia you equally blame me for having an inclination and for not having one i think it would not be reasonable for me to have any other sentiments for abelhamar and i am even assured that if i liked him you your self would condemn me try madam continued eugenia strive to love the prince were it only to be revenged and to punish me for my capriciousness i promise you before it be long i will render his passion very disagreeable to you i shall not give you that trouble replied felicia my constancy might then be brought in question it is dangerous to make such trials these words sensibly affected abelhamar whose passionate looks expressed such emotions that is was surprising felicia inea and olympia suspected nothing extraordinary under the disguise  but what advantage did the young prince receive from this stratagem he saw felicia and daily discovered some transcendent charms which inflamed him the more and increased his despair when he reflected on the sentiments she had for him for his passion was not only violent but so nice that he would not have been satisfied with the possession of her person without that of her heart and as he knew he had no share in her affection it threw him sometimes into such a deep melancholy as could not be concealed besides the queen being informed of abelhamars counterfeit sickness his going off and part of his designs gave orders that those officers who served him and could give her further light into the affair might be taken up and examined she was also raising troops repairing the fortifications of the town and taking all measures necessary to secure her self against the insults of an enemy whom she thought already with the king of tunis though every day in her chamber and sometimes lying at her beds feet thus the amourous prince elected his felicity in a confinement where he was exposed to a danger he did not apprehend and good fortune was so favorable to him till then that his disguise did not give the least cause of suspicion  felicias illness though extremely violent did not continue long her youth and good constitution contributed very much to her speedy recovery and gave her strength enough to walk in the palace gardens the court at that time was so attentive on the preparations of war that the slaves were not so strictly watched as usual one day felicia olympia inea and our counterfeit eugenia taking the air had turned their steps toward a pleasant terracewalk which afforded a most agreeable prospect but the weather changing there suddenly rose a high wind succeeded by terrible thunder and hail which obliged them to run for shelter into a little summer house that had a view on the ocean  felicia and inea were looking out of a window and had been some time observing the sea which furiously came and broke against the rocks making a horrid noise when they perceived a ship in the greatest danger she had lost all her masts and thus tossed from wave to wave was waiting the fatal moment these young ladies were moved with compassion at such a sight and concerned for those who were on board they implored the assistance of heaven and whilst they were making vows for their safety the wind decided their destiny for the ship was driven ashore and there entirely wrecked it was a most dismal scene to see how these unfortunate wretches strove to save themselves but their efforts were fruitless they all perished excepting one who was happy enough to reach a little rock which lay at a small distance from the shore  the storm being allayed some fishermen who had seen the shipwreck took their boat and rowed toward the rock where they found the man i mentioned in a swoon and as cold as death they took him and brought him ashore where they immediately lighted a fire and gave him all the help they were capable of  these things happened so near the summer house where our young captives were retired that they could easily see the condition this stranger was in but how great was felicia and olympias disorder when they knew him to be the count of la vagne they would have expressed their satisfaction were it not for the fear they were in of his being dead it is he cried olympia in her first transports it is certainly himself felicia on the other side pressing inea and eugenias hands could no more be mistress of her moderation oh heavens said she to them my dearest companions there is the man whose absence has given me so much displeasure he appears now just as he did when i found him in the forest of carmona where he had been attacked by robbers the picture of death was painted on his face i was then in a condition to assist him but now alas i am forced to see him perish without being at liberty to give him any help  whilst she was thus speaking to inea and the disguised prince olympia left em and ran to a door adjacent to the seaside which she caused to be opened without any difficulty and in a small time reached the place where the count was lying as soon as felicia perceived the concern and care she expressed in assisting him she knew not what to think i am well persuaded said she they are both natives of genoa and perhaps relations but methinks her affection is very great since she weeps as well as i and embraces him in such a passionate manner  the mean while abelhamar enraged and jealous was acting the greatest violence on himself in not discovering to her who he was that he might resolve on the immediate sacrifice of this dangerous rival ineas thoughts were also confused and she was hardly able to speak a word the more she considered olympias tender concern for the count of la vagne and the secret consolation she seemed to derive from his presence the more she sighed and sent her wishes to her faithful don ramire in a word it is not to be conceived how tormented they all were by different causes of uneasiness but how was lovely felicias mind employed all this while and what were her inward motions when she saw the count recovered from his swoon who appeared in transports of inexpressible joy at the sight of olympia he kissed her hand and fixed his eyes on here is as if fortune had snatched him from the arms of death only to lead him into perfect felicity am i then betrayed cried felicia in a faint voice and can i believe what i see is the count of la vagne in love with olympia you ought not in the least to doubt it answered eugenia who was very willing to confirm her suspicions and if you flattered your self with being beloved you are mistaken in the heart of that traitor any one may see by his actions that he has a passion for olympia do not have so rash an opinion of him interrupted inea it is probable he has some particular reasons for acting as he does perhaps the count is informed of prince abelhamars passion for felicia and as he is come in order to ransom his mistress he thought it convenient to conceal his true sentiments the better to succeed in his designs what pleasure you take in being deceived cried eugenia who could not bear to hear her express her self in this manner have you already forgot that abelhamar is suspected to be with the king of tunis and consequently there are no measures to be observed with him but the count knows nothing of it interrupted felicia and i am inclined to believe inea has interpreted the sentiments of his heart how great is our weakness when we love said the prince we scarcely can credit our own eyes we are so inclined to embrace any thing which flatters our wishes indeed eugenia replied felicia you always represent things in the falsest colors what have i done to invite you to take such delight in tormenting me the prince who perceived she was displeased said no more to her but resolved in himself to make the force of his revenge fall on this happy rival  olympia sent to acquaint the queen that the count of la vagne was cast on the shore but had escaped death and begged leave to pay his respects to her majesty celima who was exceeding melancholy and apprehensive of the consequences of abelhamars revolt declined seeing this stranger not to let him be witness of her affliction but sent back to olympia to tell her she might bring him to the palace where she should have an apartment prepared for him in one of the remote pavilions having given orders that he should be received with a distinction equal to his birth to this she added how willing she should be to admit him were she not indispensibly obliged to attend some affairs of the highest moment she gave orders also that they should supply him with all necessaries and several slaves immediately brought him variety of rich garments that he might please his fancy whilst olympia went to return the queen thanks for her favors the count was conducted through the gardens to the palace  felicia inea and eugenia were walking in an alley which had a view on the seaside when the count of la vagne came up pretty near to them felicia perceiving him her heart fluttered and she grew so faint in an instant that had not inea supported her on one side and the disguised prince on the other she would not have been able to stand but the count who had no cause to remark her motions though in favor of himself passed by the ladies and only saluted them with much respect without taking any particular notice of felicia  as soon as he was gone far enough from her not to be heard oh heaven cried she is it possible he can be so much master of his temper as not to show some tenderness in his eyes he looks as if he had never seen me what means this indifference inea are these his transports oh what must i think of his passion madam replied inea is not his coming hither to fetch you away a sufficient motive to convince you of his fidelity inea only deceives you interrupted the prince for i have seen many persons in love and can assure you that although they were in a continual restraint and obliged to be on their guard in the presence of jealous observers yet their passion discovered it self in their eyes and actions why continued he addressing himself to inea do you really think the count of la vagne was overjoyed to see felicia he did not so much as change color nor even fix his eyes on hers no no his passion is not so violent as you imagine and if you continue speaking in his favor you only do it with an intent to sooth our friends pain dont torment me in this manner cruel creature cried felicia am i not unfortunate enough already why will you persist in saying such vexatious things to me have you resolved on my death i take heaven to witness replied the prince sighing that i have no such intention you would certainly judge more favorably of my sentiments were they well known to you  felicia fearing it would be taken notice of at the palace that she had been so long abroad returned speedily to her chamber which she no sooner entered but wrote to the count in the following terms  i have now some reason to flatter my self that heaven will soon put a period to my misfortunes since love and generosity have invited you here to your felicia s deliverance how shall i express my joy my affection and my gratitude and when shall i be at liberty to entertain you with my tender sentiments alas what violence did not i do my self in seeing you so near me without speaking to you but how was it possible you could pass by me with such an air of indifference i must confess it very much affected me and if i may tell you my thoughts i almost suspected your fidelity i began to fear you had devoted all your transports to olympia this extremely augmented my uneasiness being an effect of my delicacy which you must pardon let me know how i am to behave my self hereafter in this court and dont neglect any thing to procure us a speedy departure i hope fortune will influence the interest of our hearts and crown our sufferings with eternal felicity   this letter could not be conveyed to the count without some difficulty felicia bid inea read it and conjured her to find means to have it immediately delivered into his hands i cannot think on any way replied inea but to carry it my self your self cried felicia how will you venture to do it leave that to me madam answered inea i will run any risque to serve you this is very generous my dear companion said felicia then thanked her for so obliging an offer and desired her since she was willing to render her so considerable a service not to defer it  olympia was now in the queens apartment and the count in his but being extremely impatient to see his lovely mistress he stepped into the garden in expectation of meeting her it was a fine moonlight night and as he was walking with his thoughts wholly employed on the happiness he promised himself in the possession of a lady for whom he had so transcendent a passion young inea wraped in her white vail accosted him and said read this letter my lord it comes from a person who ought to be dear to you the count opened it and was surpised not to know the writing after having read it over and over without conceiving the meaning it came into his head that it was a jest olympia had imagined to divert her self so said to inea i desire you will tell the beauteous lady from whom i receive this favor that i intend my self to be bearer of the answer  as inea was going back she perceived a woman at a distance covered with her vail who was coming toward her and fearing she should be known by her she passed on the other side of the pallisadoes and went into the long walk where she found felicia who taking her under the arm said to her in a low voice you will think me very impatient to know what the count has said to you but that is not the only reason which brought me hither i was looking out of my chamberwindow waiting your return when i saw a woman cross the garden with great diligence and go as it were toward the counts pavilion i must confess my dear inea it gave me much uneasiness and i made all possible haste to follow her as far as i could distinguish she appeared to me to be olympia and i believe it is her oh inea how my heart aches and in what torment is my mind for fear of losing the object of my love judge more favorably of the count said inea interrupting her he read your letter with an extreme attention and addressing me in very obliging terms assured me he would answer it personally it is very well continued felicia but let us go on without making a noise we may perhaps discover where that person is going whom i mentioned to you in finishing these words they walked on hiding themselves behind the pallisadoes and hearing some body talk in an arbor which was at the end of the alley they drew near  the count of la vagne and olympia were conversing together in this place it is impossible madam said he to his mistress for me to express the despair i was in when i heard of your death and the circumstances which preceded it they so entirely affected me that even life began to be odious to me and never was mortal in a more desolate condition but how transported was i at the unexpected change of fortune when the jeweller who had seen you in the queens apartment informed me that the same beauteous olympia whose loss i was deploring was actually living and at sallee judge  i well conceive my dear count said she interrupting him what might employ your thoughts in two such different occasions as our affection is mutual we sympathize in all the pleasure and torment which derives from our good or bad fortune you may imagine after what i suffered for your supposed death how excessive was my joy when i heard of your safety i have told you already said the count that your illustrious father has given his consent to our happy union receiving my proposals with such extraordinary marks of friendship that i must confess i should have suspected so uncommon a favor were it not that my long sufferings give me a title to so great a reward yes continued he most divine olympia you are now to be mine and i for ever yours as they were speaking in this manner a doleful voice interrupted them which repeating these words i am dying gave em to understand that some person very near the arbor was taken ill this induced them to discontinue their conversation though ever so delightful in order to assist the lady who was complaining so dismally  they looked on every side without perceiving any one but hearing some noise behind the pallisadoes they approached and saw inea holding in her arms felicia in a swoon ah my lord dont come near cried inea weeping your presence would become fatal to felicia and you madam continued she speaking to olympia i beg as a favor she may not see you what aversion can she have to us replied they both at the same time we do not know her and it would be strange she should hate us without cause this is not a proper time to explain matters answered inea all the assistance i desire of you is to run to the palace and send us some help  olympia without making any reply though extremely astonished at what she heard went to give notice to eugenia and some other of the slaves of the condition felicia was in and the mean while the count staid by her no said he to inea i cannot go from you till you have unriddled this secret to me was it not you that just now gave me a letter which i do not understand the meaning of one would think by your air and words that i had disobliged this fair lady but alas how could i have done any thing either to deserve her anger or your reproaches it is impossible replied inea to dissemble better and conceal with more confidence the horridest perfidiousness that man could ever act against a lady of birth and merit dont expect my lord that i will explain things to you which you know better than i the count of la vagne could not have helped laughing at so odd and obscure an answer had not the condition felicia was in inspired him with great compassion and finding inea seemed displeased at his remaining there he resolved to retire  by this time several slaves were come to felicias help and among others eugenia or the disguised prince who seeing her in a swoon expressed his affliction in terms so passionate that his counterfeit was soon discovered unfortunate eugenia cried he in a doleful accent thou art going to be deprived of the only object of thy love felicia my dear felicia to what a sad state are you reduced divinest creature if i lose you my death shall succeed yours since i cannot live without you whilst he was talking in this manner inea and her companions were throwing water on felicias face but as their assistance could not recover her they carried her to her chamber the prince as you may imagine surpassed the rest in attending his sick mistress as soon as she was lain in bed he sat by her and forgetting himself his excessive grief forced from him such expressions as were not becoming his female disguise  the governess of the slaves who watchfully observed every thing took notice of his words and examining earnestly eugenias features discovered prince abelhamars resemblance she ran immediately and related what had passed to the queen who was not a little surpised at this unexpected adventure it was late at night therefore she would not call a council fearing it might alarm the people who were already under great apprehensions from the king of tuniss landing so deferred till next day taking any resolution against the prince  he little knew the danger which threatened him all his thoughts were then employed on the state felicia was in nor could he reflect on any thing more tormenting she scarcely recovered her speech but lamented being restored to a life which at that time all things rendered burdensome to her inea apprehending that the violence of her affliction would force her into such complaints as ought to be concealed told her companions who were present that it was convenient felicia should be left to take a little rest and that eugenia and she would stay by her the others hearing this immediately retired  felicia after they were gone gave an entire course to her excessive grief see inea cried she see what calamities i labor under i am remote from my country out of favor with my family become a slave and betrayed by a man who appeared to me deserving of every thing he is now in love with another it is olympia he is come to deliver this lover whom she impatiently expected and received with so much joy is the same on whom i bestowed my tender care when in a most dangerous condition and my solitude afforded him a refuge from the fury of his enemies he conceived a passion for me engaged me by a thousand promises to make a return and vowed his love should be eternal but heavens how perfidious has he proved i remember now as an evincement he sacrificed olympias picture to me which persuaded me i had seen her resemblance before oh what a sad object am i of fortunes capriciousness here she was silent a long time alas what have i done said she again to deserve at so tender an age such a series of misfortunes yesterday i was deploring the absence of the man i loved this day i lament the loss of his heart her sighs and tears interrupted her several times whilst she was speaking and at last she could say no more the prince flattering himself with some small hopes took this time to speak to her if you were in a a condition to taste the pleasure of revenge said he you would be soon satisfied my arm should second your resentment for it is no longer in my power charming felicia to conceal what my excessive passion for you has made me undertake see at your feet wretched abelhamar your slave here i remain in this palace for your sake although i know that were the queen informed of it my life would atone for my crime compare this proof of my love with that of my unworthy rivals whom you prefer and then you will own your self the most unjust person in the world  oh heavens cried felicia can i believe my eyes what new fatality does attend me you here my lord and an enemy to the queen have you been my confident and caressed me by so many days without my perceiving the deceit alas where shall i go for refuge what must the queen think of me will she not have sufficient reason to suspect my virtue can any one imagine that without my consent you would have made so rash an attempt ah nothing but death can relieve me from my misfortune abelhamars disorder was so great that he did not say much in his justification and as for inea who was present at this scene she could not deny them her compassion she endeavored to excuse him and said to felicia the true respect the prince has for you madam ought in some measure to appease you since no body knows of his being disguised your honor which is dearer to him than his life and the inevitable danger that threatens him if the queen should be informed of what has passed will engage him to keep secret an affair of this importance you are very little acquainted with mankind interrupted felicia who glory in relating their adventures and never love so sincerely as to make any thing a secret well my lord continued she addressing herself to the prince you have made your last efforts to augment my miseries i should have died esteemed by those who know me but at present shall deserve their contempt you may go now to the count of la vagne and tell him that since he has sacrificed me to olympia i have quitted him for you and contrived this criminal disguise to favor your admittance know me better madam replied abelhamar were not my passion for you transcendent i should never deviate from the rules of honor and what i owe you no my felicia you shall never find me guilty of acting any thing that may incur your displeasure yet i cannot help saying you ought no longer to deplore the loss of a man so unworthy your esteem who without dispute has deceived you for it is impossible if he once loved you he could ever love another divine felicia be convinced of the power of your charms and think that i who feel their effects can never change the present situation of affairs gives me hopes of a happy turn in my fortune i may ascend the throne on which my ancestors were seated but oh felicia what pleasure can it afford me to possess a crown without you i entreat you now to grant a request you cannot reasonably refuse me which is to forget your perfidious lover and receive the vows of the most passionate and most constant of mankind if you compare my sentiments with his you will do justice to my sincere passion you shall be delivered from your captivity and shall give laws to the queen whose chains you now wear ah my lord cried felicia in a dejected tone i desire nothing but death therefore give me leave to complain and do not interrupt my grief with proposals which i cannot accept i have not power to forget the traitor who thus neglects me i love him still spite of all the reasons i have to hate him and should i be doomed to sink under my grievous woes or even live to despise the author of my present pain do not think that a crown could invite me ever to believe perfidious man again  abelhamar heard her with an unconceivable anguish and had not strength to make a reply but looked at her with the greatest concern and his sighs interpreted the tormenting motions of his soul felicia was not in a condition to observe the despair this young prince was reduced to but renewed her complaints and nothing could restrain the course of her tears what are you doing madam said inea to her is it possible that a person so charming should regret the loss of a man who even disowns you and abandons you to go away with olympia is it thus he ungratefully repays the obliging sentiments you have for him call revenge to your aid madam forget a man who forsakes you and let your disdain be the reward of his falsity it is easy my dear replied felicia to give advice on such an occasion i would do the same to you were you in my case and i in yours but do you think it is in our power to act as we please when love has once rendered himself master of our inclinations ah cruel rival what torment do you give me and you perfidious count shall not i see you punished for your ingratitude employ my arm madam interrupted the prince and with your consent i will revenge you of your perjured lover i would sooner prince whom i dare not admit at this time of night into my chamber my peace and honor depend on your compliance think of the danger you expose your self to for a person who can make you no return that is the only misfortune i fear interrupted abelhamar every thing else might be easily surmounted retire my lord replied felicia i am extremely uneasy at your being here the prince perceiving it was in vain to resist withdrew but not without assuring her that although he were to suffer innumerable torments through her indifferency yet his passion should ever be the same  olympia doria all that evening had not found an opportunity to speak to the count of la vagne which made her pass the rest of that night in such an agitation of mind as troubled the joy she ought to have received at so uncertain of my destiny you are not the same you were yesterday what have i done to deserve from you so cold a reception i have not resolution enough to be silent replied olympia though it was my another time she should have been very glad to see him olympia having returned her acknowledgments in a most respectful manner went into the slaves apartment where she chose the ladies i mentioned and to acquaint her with her departure but at the name of olympia and the news of her going away she fetched a shriek and made such complaints as would have inspired the hardest heart with pity olympia hearing this would not aggravate her pain by her presence and though she passionately wished to entertain felicia that she might know from her whether the count of la vagne was sincere in what he had told her yet she was no ways willing to satisfy her self at the expense of so amiable a person  the count was expecting olympia with impatience when she came to tell him the favors she had received from the queen who ordered some of her officers to accompany them to the ship the mean while felicia oppressed with sorrow continued lamenting with inea i have no hopes left said she to her my fate is decreed the ungrateful count of la vagne is now going off and i shall lose him for ever he flies me and carries with him the object of his love the barbarian could see me dying without being touched nay he even denied me his pity and the deplorable condition that perfidious man has reduced me to has not cost him a sigh ah leave me and let me die with grief and shame dont indulge your affliction madam interrupted inea think only that he who leaves you is unworthy of the tears you shed reflect on his ingratitude and it will be an effectual way to forget him you are deceived if you believe it said felicia sighing when one is inspired with a passion the loss of its object wholly employs our thoughts i protest to you with some confusion that all the good qualities i knew in that inconstant lover appear to me now with greater luster though i can no longer doubt of his infidelity or my misfortune and to let you see more of my weakness i have a pressing desire to write to him in hopes my reproaches might move him what madam interrupted inea could you receive his devoirs again after such an injurious proceeding alas replied felicia what are not we capable of acting to recall a heart whose possession is dear to us then dont add to my pain i too well comprehend what you think and blush to see my honor concerned but consider i am an unhappy distracted creature my dear i conjure you in the name of your faithful don ramire to find some person that will deliver a letter to the count of la vagne you cannot confer a greater obligation on me inea who was very willing to serve felicia left her immediately in order to make an attempt but soon after she returned and told her it was impossible to send any body to the port that the queen had either received news of ismaels approach or that something extraordinary was passing at court since she had commanded the guards of her palace to be doubled and the gates to be shut that none might be admitted without her order  then i must lose all hopes cried unfortunate felicia for i can neither stop him nor follow him just heaven revenge me on that perjured man punish his perfidiousness punish the cause of this last misfortune may the angry waves swallow them up and let me hear the news of their loss soon after that of their departure but alas am i capable of forming wishes so contrary to my inclination no i have loved the count too well ever to hate him then let him live and be happy all my fury ought to be turned against my self for i deserve the miseries i now linger in had i instead of leaving my fathers house submitted to his commands i should not at present have the cruel mortification of reproaching my self with an imprudent conduct which i never shall be able to justify to the world while felicia is thus deploring the cruelty of her fortune we must return to the prince of carency  casilda had maliciously persuaded him that benavidez was gone with leonida to jaen where he would be sure as she said of the governors protection a man must certainly have as much valor as love to attempt any thing against a person who was protected by the governor of so considerable a place but the violence of his passion and extremity of his despair together would not permit him to reflect even on the greatest of dangers  wherever he passed people observed something extraordinary in him and though his eyes expressed much grief his noble mein carried marks of the highest distinction he made the strictest enquiry after felicia of leon whom sometimes he called leonida of velasco but when he described her to those he applied to he was so lavish in her praise that they easily discovered he was her lover  notwithstanding all his care and diligence his pursuit was in vain for she had not passed that way nor could any one give him the least intelligence concerning her he began to be very uneasy and hurrying from one thought to another his mind was filled with his past misfortunes till he came to jaen where he arrived exceeding melancholy he looked on the citadel of that town as a place where his life and disasters were to be terminated here said he here i expect to see the ungrateful beauty i adore and before her eyes i will attack the ungenerous man who next her self had the first place in my heart what a strange destiny is this cried he my mistress and my friend equally betray me and to satisfy my resentment i must destroy the one to wound the other it is probable they are this fatal hour contriving my ruin and giving each other fresh assurances of eternal love but my death must confirm their felicity for whilst i am living they have a cruel enemy who will endeavor to defeat their projects and ever trouble the happiness they propose  at his arrival he had a mind to go directly to the citadel for as i told you before he had accepted of a letter from the governor of carmona to his son don gabriel d aguillar by whose interest he was sure of an easy entrance into the place but he thought it was better first to send to him and the mean time inform himself of what passed there as he was going through the town he met a french chevalier of the house of boucicault his name was alphonso a person of an obliging temper who came to seville with the count of la march what do i see is it you my lord cried he coming up to the prince with a great deal of joy and respect are you living whom we so much lamented with the prince your brother believing you were assassinated near carmona as it was reported in spain and for which we were meditating a proportionable revenge i should have been happy my dear alphonso said the prince had my enemys designs been effected but i am reserved for greater calamities yet i desire my name may be kept secret for important reasons which engage me to conceal it and you can be very serviceable to me i am in love and betrayed and must revenge my self on my rival and my mistress oh how i shall load felicia with my just reproaches she is now in the citadel with him what you say is true my lord interrupted alphonso i know it from don gabriel d aguillar who is one of my particular friends felicia is confined against her will in an apartment where she sees no body but by the means of the spanish captain i have already mentioned one night without being perceived i saw her sadly deploring her fate oh my lord how young and handsome she is i must confess i extremely pity her  do you pity her said the prince with a deep sigh have you any compassion for her ah you are little acquainted with her perfidiousness but tell me what means that manner of confinement did not you see her come here with don fernand benavidez the governors nephew no replied alphonso the person you name has not appeared here since my arrival for as i am every day at the citadel i should probably have seen him yet if he be there he certainly keeps himself concealed ah the traitor cried the prince he is only hid for felicias sake and without doubt has desired a guard to protect him from my resentment the villain has sufficient reason to fear me it is dangerous to insult a desperate man who does not value his life this thought made the prince fly into so violent a passion that alphonso begged of him to retire from the place where they were standing for fear they might be observed  the prince said to him if you will prevent my committing any extravagancies you must second the desire i have of seeing benavidez and felicia i have a letter for don gabriel daguillar who i am glad to hear is your friend you will oblige me
