extremely in sending instantly to him that we may take necessary measures for that purpose alphonso promised the prince every thing that depended on him even at the hazard of his life then left him to execute his orders  whatever enquiry alphonso and don gabriel made before they came to the prince they could learn nothing satisfactory those to whom they applied concerning don fernand benavidez told em they believed he was at villareal but that he was not nephew to don alonzo fajardo and that no body had seen him at jaen where hardly any one knew him when they brought this account to the prince he could not believe em since felicia is in the citadel interrupted he it is a certain consequence benavidez is not far do you only contrive that i enter her apartment it is likely he will come there when every body is retired don gabriel told him he should be obeyed then went to receive orders from the governor who named him for felicias guard at night he came back to the prince to conduct him and alphonso to the citadel  now can any mortal imagine the trouble this amorous prince was in when he thought he was sure to see the object he still adored he resolved his rival should perish though he himself were to fall with him which violent reflection made him sigh deeply especially when he considered that this same felicia was leonida of velasco to whom he was so strictly engaged that his honor would not suffer any other to carry her off  he was in this confusion of thought where love and revenge were equally concerned when don gabriel conducted him through several courts till at last he brought him to the tower where felicia was concealed in a low apartment the windows were barred with irongrates and the weather being excessive hot she had obtained leave to walk on the leads of the tower for the air the prince took that opportunity to enter a closet which was only shut with a glass door and there hid himself behind the window curtain from whence he could see all that passed he was not there long before the lights were taken away and he heard two persons creep into the closet they spoke very low and the night being dark he could not distinguish whether they were men or women soon after they went out of the closet where the prince thought himself alone but the lights being brought in again he saw several women who were preparing a bath they hung a canopy of rosecolourd satin embroidered with silver over a large black marble vessel which they filled with water and flowers mixed with the finest perfumes  every thing being ready a lady came in to whom the rest of the women showed much respect but he could not see her face her head being covered with a fine veil this was felicia who having undressed her self to a thin nightgown ordered all her women to retire excepting zaida then called for her lute saying music only can sooth my dear afflictions ah zaida zaida could he for whom i suffer hear these verses how pleased should i be soon after she sung the ensuing words with so sweet a voice that none could hear her without being enchanted  why should virtue thus torment me oh unkind and cruel law or why should fantastic duty strike my tender heart with awe   love take pity of my anguish to my soft distress be kind never let the fair one languish when to tenderness inclined she repeated the last stanza several times and fetched now and then deep sighs which showed her heart was possessed with a mighty passion as well as excessive grief the prince all this while perceived it was not the voice of his unconstant felicia or at least was surpised that the small distance which was between them should cause so great an alteration in her tone as not to know it again do not afflict your self madam said zaida great passions are ever influenced by fortune he whom you love is at present informed of what you suffer do you think he will attempt nothing to evince you of his affection felicia made no reply but ordered her to shut her chamber door and went into the bath how entirely do i love you cruel leonida said the amorous prince to himself but oh ungrateful woman ought not i to be ashamed of my weakness for let me look upon you as a person to whom i am contracted or as a mistress i love to distraction you have equally deceived me under the titles of carency and la vagne ah perfidious creature you are now proposing to surmount all difficulties in order to marry benavidez could there be a complaint more passionate than that which you just now uttered but continued he what must i believe are her designs traversed here i see her a prisoner in a place where she thought to find a sanctuary she even regrets the absence of her lover and every thing seems to disappoint their expectations  such were the princes reflections and in spite of his resentment love still triumphed in his heart but in what surprise was he when zaida opening the door of another closet he drew the curtain and saw a man going with precipitation to the bathing vessel where he put himself on his knees and spoke so low that his voice could not reach the prince who only heard felicia cry aloud is it you my dear lover then she swooned away  the prince of carency seeing this could no longer refrain but without thinking on the consequence of the scene he was going to open ran out of the closet like a madman and had he been capable of taking any base advantage it was in his power to run him he took for benavidez through the body before the other could even put himself in a posture of defense for felicias swoon had such an extraordinary effect upon him that he did not see the prince who was just at his back till hearing some body threatening him with a furious tone he rose and drew his sword but the prince seeing his face immediately dropped the point of his knowing him to be don alonzo eldest son to the infanta don fernand he had seen him at seville when he was there with his brother the count of la march and the fine qualities of this young prince had engaged the prince of carency to have a great esteem for him he cast his eyes on her whom he took for leonida and knew her to be dona felicia d ayala daughter to the great chancellor of castille who was highly distiguishd by his birth and renowned for the histories of don pedro and don henriquez kings of spain which he had written this grandee being dead felicia was brought up with the two princesses daughters to the infanta don fernand don alonzo who saw her often conceived so great a passion for her that every one suspected he would marry her privately and to prevent so unequal a match whilst don alonzo was one day a hunting the infanta his father had ordered that felicia should be secretly conveyed to jean where she was to be carefully guarded all the women who attended her were at the infantas devotion and by the death of the chancellor her father she was delivered up entirely to the persecutions of those who envied her as for zaida she was a slave whom felicia had made a christian and one they did not mistrust not reflecting she had been presented to her by don alonso this young prince at his return to seville was in a despairing condition when he heard his mistress was gone and though he learned but very confusedly the manner of her being carried off and confined in a strong place yet invited by his passion he day and night used his utmost endeavor to recover her having at last discovered his dear felicias concealment and found means to write to zaida who answered his letter the affair was so well managed that without felicias knowledge he got into her apartment  the prince of carency perceiving his error in order to repair it presented don alonso with his sword the point toward his own breast punish an unhappy man said he whom you will oblige in taking away his life by my words you may judge of the concern i am in for having disturbed this charming interview which to obtain it is probable my lord you have exposed your self to some danger but be assured i suffer more than you through this mistake i do not resent it in the least my lord replied don alonzo embracing him and if you will promise to keep this secret you shall ever find me a grateful friend the prince of carency gave him his word he would never take the least notice of what had happened and without staying till felicia was come to her self he left the chamber in so deep a despair that he could scarcely speak to gabriel d aguilar who was at the door of the first room with alphonso and this last attended him to don gabriels apartment who was obliged to remain in his post  the prince having an opportunity of yielding himself up to his just sorrow called to mind all his misfortunes from his first appearing in the world to that moment on whatever side he turned his eyes he saw so little hopes of an intermission that every thing became indifferent to him and he did not even wish himself a better fortune all his thoughts were fixed on being revenged of benavidez which he fancied was the only satisfaction he could receive but as it appeared almost impossible it extremely added to his grief oh alphonso said he can any disappointment be equal to this i was in hopes to punish a traitor and recover my mistress but that fatal name of felicia has again deceived me what unaccountable circumstances have attended my life fate has singled me amongst all mankind to be unfortunate where must i go to find the treasure i have lost alas my leonida is not here and i discover too late casildas wicked plot how could i believe that she would have told me where her brother was gone if i had made the least reflection i might have expected she would deceive me ah credulous wretch that i was i have lost an opportunity i shall never retrieve again just heaven my rival is now safe with leonida and he peaceably enjoys a blessing which belongs to me can i after this survive my shame and despair in short the princes condition was such that nothing could give him relief his complaints were moving and love appeared in all his actions  alphonso who knew by experience the torments that attend transcendent passions extremely pitied this unhappy prince oh love cried he will you never cease persecuting us you alone cause all our misfortunes and never grant a favor that is not preceded by a thousand disappointments ah why have we no fence against your power the prince whilst he was talking continued in a deep silence and alphonso finding he was not disposed to converse with him meditated some time then wrote these verses  love thou dear but cruel tyrant can nothing move thee to be kind hear my sighs and see my torment for only thou can ease my mind   since all are doomed to feel thy darts at least suspend our pains with tender pity bless those hearts that languish in thy chains the prince read these lines and said one could have no room to complain if in love there were an equal mixture of pleasure and pain but alas i have experienced that all its ills are reserved for me which makes me wish a period to my unhappy life ah my lord interrupted alphonso do not harbor a thought so offensive to your courage it is unworthy a soul so great as yours should yield to a passion which will divert you from the performance of great exploits the prince blushed at what alphonso said and looked on this discourse as a reproach made him for the time he had employed in entertaining his amorous sentiments you shall see by my conduct replied he that my soul is still my own i love it is true and cannot flatter myself with ever being disengaged from a passion which has so great an empire over me yet when honor calls me i am ready to attend and if i must give up my life it shall be in so glorious a way as will do honor to my name  here they where both silent some time till the prince urged by disagreeable thoughts broke out into his usual complaints oh alphonso said he which way shall i direct my course to find leonida i cannot hear where she is must i then turn knight errant and run through the world without knowing where to go no i have a nobler resolution i will return to seville and there follow my brothers fortune if we engage the moors i must conquer or bravely die  alphonso overjoyed to hear the prince speak in these terms applauded a design so worthy of him consider my lord said he that all you could do at present for leonida would meet with no return for since she flies you it is proable you are the object of her aversion at least her going off with benavidez is a proof she loves him and is perfidious to you what can you then expect from her rather strive to deface the impression she has made that in time you may even lose the remembrance of having ever known her i ought to take your advice indeed interrupted the prince but alas how is it possible fortune may be inconstant but my heart can never change thus irresolute not knowing what to determine he conjured alphonso not to discover who he was nor acquaint the count of la march with his being at jaen till he had fixed a resolution the chevalier promised him upon honor to keep the secret inviolably and begged he would not be uneasy on that subject  whilst these things passed in relation to the prince of carency the count of la march his brother neglected no opportunity of signalizing himself he had not been long at seville when the moors besieged baeca with seven thousand horse and a hundred thousand foot so formidable an army struck terror throughout andalusia but as the place was well fortified the moors despaired of its reduction when they received advice that the spaniards from all parts were assembled in order to relieve it therefore they suddenly retired loaded with the plunder of the neighboring villages they were not more fortunate at sea where they had considerable losses by the spanish fleet which had engaged theirs and gained a complete victory this advantage gave no small satisfaction to the spaniards who now thought of acting offensively the infanta called a general council of all the officers of the army where it was resolved to besiege zahara the besieged defended the town bravely till the want of necessaries made em capitulate soon after he took another of their strongest places which so exasparated mahomet king of granada that he immediately thought on revenge and in order to carry on his design put himself at the head of six thousand horse and eighty thousand foot dividing them into several bodies which took different routs for their march and all on a sudden besieged jaen whilst they thought him employed elsewhere  his approach surpised the governor who was not prepared for a siege and would have been under greater difficulties were he not assisted by the prince of carency who had not yet left the town and was rejoiced to have so fine an occasion of distinguishing himself he had been presented to alonzo fajardo under the title of count of la vagne and having offered his services to him the other readily accepted of em this young prince put himself at the head of a detachment and by his frequent sallies often broke the enemies measures and repulsed em where ever he appeared carrying death and terror along with him as his neglect of life made him expose himself to the greatest dangers he became dreadful to his enemies who knowing him by his arms chose rather to avoid his blows than resist him the governor of jaen admired his courage and thought heaven had sent him to defend that city against the infidels  the king of the moors enraged at his ill success and attributing the cause to the prince of carency whom they called the knight of the black arms ordered some of the bravest of his army either to kill or take him prisoner so immediately the generals and most of the noblemen made a league to be revenged of this terrible enemy or perish in the attempt a detachment was sent out the next day much superior to that under the princes command nevertherless he attacked them and his courage surpassed all that can be imagined the moors were beginning to repent their rash undertaking when unluckily the princes horse was wounded by an arrow and before he could disengage himself they rushed upon him with a shout and took him prisoner this news ran through the camp and soon found way into the town where it had a different effect mahomet thought now he had conquered and the governor believed himself overcome the barbarians were resolved to make a general assault and the christians were preparing to defend themselves though most of the soldiers were mightily disheartened saying to one another what can we pretend to we have lost the count of la vagne commanded by him we might have defeated our enemies but his misfortune is the presage of ours  at this time the infanta omitted nothing for the succor of jaen he assembled his troops with great diligence and marched toward the town with the count of la march where he surpised the moors who retired with more shame than glory satisfying themselves with burning and pillaging wherever they passed the spaniards pursued them as far as malaga which they besieged in their turn the infanta was informed by don alonso fajardo of the young count of la vagnes being taken prisoner by mahomet as for his friend alphonso he was killed in one of the engagements which was the cause that the count of la march heard nothing of the prince of carencys being there the mighty character of his bravery and the recital of the great actions he had performed gave the infanta a particular concern for his misfortune he sent an officer with proposals for the exchange of prisoners and offered a ransom for the count of la vagne being willing to purchase his liberty at any rate but all he could do to get him out of his enemies power was in vain the moors made answer that the count having bribed his guards had made his escape and that were he still in their hands they would readily send him back to show how desirous they were to oblige the infanta  the king of granada in the mean time was of opinion that he could not too strictly guard a person who had been very troublesome to him during the siege therefore policy and revenge having an equal share in this design he ordered that the prince though dangerously wounded should be conveyed to the castle of solobrena where his brother prince joseph with his two sons mahomet and osmin were kept prisoners so the prince of carency found himself a second time in the power of the infidels but his sentiments were quite different from those he had at nicopolis for that which at another time would have given him much chagrin had now very little effect on him all his thoughts being only employed on leonida and every thing else below his consideration yet it was an unhappy state for a man to love an object whom he thought guilty of the greatest perfidiousness  whilst this was the state of affairs in upper andalusia and murcia celima queen of fez was taking measures to be revenged of abelhamar felicia had but just obliged him to leave her chamber when the queen impatient to have her designs executed caused him to be seized by a captain of her guards who carried him immediately to a tower adjoining the palace and having posted a guard at every gate to hinder people from coming near the queen went to him soon after  abelhamar did not appear the least surpised at his confinement he said to this princess my sentiments madam are not unknown to you since you are informed of the love i have for felicia i have not acted any thing contrary to the allegiance and respect i owe you and though you find me disguised in your palace it would not consist with justice to draw an ill consequence from an action that is only the effect of my passion to which you can impute no other crime but that of indiscretion i know too well your intentions interrupted the queen in a fierce tone to let myself be deceived by your wit or metamorphosis no prince you were here conspiring against me the rebellious principles you were brought up in could never receive a grateful sentiment or teach you what you owe your sovereign have i not preserved your life without regard to the reasons of state which ought to have induced me to sacrifice you yet ungrateful as you are have you lived hitherto with the hopes of making me a victim cruel ismael also seconds your design and has promised you forces in order to dethrone me you prefer a stranger to a queen of your own blood to whom you owe every thing but heaven that protects me has put me in a condition to punish you and be revenged of my enemies satisfy yourself madam replied the prince with a haughty air and dont slight so fine an opportunity of taking away a life which is odious to you paint my innocence in the vilest colors or rather say the legal right i have to the crown you wear is my only crime and that as you have ever born an invincible hatred to the unhappy remainders of my family you have resolved to complete what your unjust father had begun rash man cried celima do you think of what you are saying dare you pronounce these words before the queen your mistress dont you know your death waits my command is it thus you endeavor to justify your self and appease me you dont consider the danger you are in abelhamar made no reply to her threats nor gave the least attention to her whilst she was speaking but rather acted like one who despising mercy did not regret the life he was going to be deprived of which unconcerned behavior surpised the queen who retired full of resentment  celima had already given orders that felicia and inea should be strictly guarded in their chambers and that none of their companions should be admitted to them this new misfortune did not add to felicias concern for every thing was now become so indifferent to her that she did not even enquire into the cause  the queen being returned to the palace called her council and appointed persons to examine the prince because she would show some form in an affair which might draw upon her the aversion of her relations and particularly that of the maliquez alabez who were also descended from the ancient kings of fez and at that time very potent in the kingdom of granada this induced her to give the blackest colors to the crime with which they were going to charge abelhamar and though she took the best measures to conceal the design she had against him yet his faithful mula who was just returned from tunis where he had carried credentials to ismael from the prince used his utmost application to serve him he had to good a correspondence in the palace not to be informed of every thing that passed there in relation to the unfortunate prince and as he perceived the occasion was pressing he would lose no time to give immediate assistance to his master who otherways would fall a sacrifice to celima he went to all abelhamars friends and slaves and prepared them to assemble in order to raise the city in his favor by which means he hoped to restore him to his liberty or put all to fire and sword that would oppose it these were his resolutions till he reflected that the queen had a great many creatures devoted to her service as well as a strong garrison and that the people being used to her government would strive to maintain it therefore he thought it more prudent to return to tunis and apply himself to ismael who would employ his utmost power in this important affair so he set out again from sallee and soon arrived at ismaels court  his grief and affection furnished him with expressions of so great a force that the king of tunis was extremely touched at abelhamars misfortunes and being already exasperated against celima he resolved immediately to assist that prince with this intent he ordered his troops to be drawn out of their garrisons and reviewed then sent an ambassador to the king of morocco to renew his treaty of alliance with him to prevent that prince in his absence from making any irruptions into his territories  after having disposed every thing with as much wisdom as diligence he opened the campaign and mula returned privately to sallee to perform what he had first resolved for the safety of his master  the young prince being examined refused at first to make a reply but when they told him unless he answered to the accusation he should receive sentence the sooner it obliged him to make a defense in expectation of being relieved by ismael and whatever mind the queen had to forward his trial she could not proceed to a condemnation without exposing herself to inevitable dangers the first officers of the crown and lords of the court represented to her that she could not take too much precaution in an affair of this importance and that it would be more to her glory to let clemency take place of justice we believe the prince is culpable said they since he was found disguised in the palace which is a sufficient proof yet without regard to his youth as he is presumptive heir to the crown and of your blood madam he ought to have some respect shown him therefore we beg that your majesty for your own interest will consider these reasons separately and by suspending your resentment show mercy to the prince  the queen was displeased at a request which showed that abelhamar had more friends than she imagined and fearing they should take measures to rescue her prisoner she would no longer consult reason but resolved to do every thing by her own authority without taking any advice of her council so having prevented those appointed to judge the prince she herself pronounced the sentence of his death and to deter seditious persons from caballing against her she ordered that he should be executed on the platform of the court wherein he was confined that every body might see him suffer  in this place they built a scaffold hung with mourning and set round with standards and scutcheons which with other dismal preparations drew numbers of spectators the prince was soon after informed of his fate this news at first very much surpised him his eyes expressed an extraordinary grief and he was some time without speaking at last lifting up his hands oh heaven he cried you know my disguise was not criminal and that this is only a pretext the unjust queen takes to destroy me but since you have decreed my doom i am ready to obey without repining and if celima grants me one favor i shall die with content then turning himself to the captain of the guards he said go tell the queen from me that i beg leave to bid an eternal adieu to charming felicia the minutes i shall pass with her will be too short to retard the inhuman designs of celima  the officer went directly to the queen who was very unwilling to grant the prince his request but her ministers having represented to her in respectful terms how cruel it would be to refuse so small a satisfaction to a person in his condition she at last consented that felicia should be brought to him she was till then a stranger to the princes misfortune being strictly confined with inea and as her confinement did not in the least disturb her she never enquired why they added this new rigor to her captivity her mind was entirely taken up with the count of la vagne and the tears she shed were only for his inconstancy and absence every thing else that happened had no effect on her and she was in this disposition when she was sent for by the queens orders she followed the governess of the slaves without asking any question inea supported her and being very weak after her illness it was with a vast deal of difficulty that she reached the tower  the first object that struck her sight was the scaffold and a number of guards which gave her room to believe that she was going to be a victim to celimas jealousy ineas thoughts were the same which extremely terrified her felicias sentiments were different from hers for though death appeared hard to her yet she had some sort of satisfaction in seeing the approaching end of her misfortunes take courage my dear inea said she embracing her with a great deal of tenderness the danger only regards me and i look upon it with indifferency it is a remedy my preservation commanded me not to seek but since it is my fate i receive it with pleasure i am going to die and shall no longer have a sense of my calamities no lovely felicia cried the prince who was near enough to hear what she said you are not to die this punishment is prepared for unfortune abelhamar who now takes his last leave of you i protest it less concerns me to lose my life in so shameful a manner than to want assurances of your favor ah madam added he with an air full of love and grief can you refuse me a look a sigh or a favorable word you see i perish and my misfortune proceeds from your transcendent charms the desire i had to see you reign made me endeavor to ascend the throne from which my father fell you inspired me with an ambition i should have managed better had i been less in love you are the innocent cause of the disguise i am reproached with which is thought my crime yet i have nothing to repent of since my passion invites me to bear the cruelty of my fate but at least give me leave divine felicia to believe that had my design succeeded my respect and perseverance would have made some impression on you only approve these thoughts and i shall not think much to purchase so dear a profession with the loss of my life  felicia at these words was so disordered that she looked some time at abelhamar without having power to speak she was touched with a sincere compassion and deplored the misfortune of this young prince who was going to be sacrificed so ignominiously she could have wished the queens resentment had fallen on her for the state of her affairs with the count of la vagne was such as had rendered life so insupportable to her that she seemed very willing to resign it at last perceiving abelhamar waited her answer she said is this scene prepared for you my lord alas why cannot i relieve you my tears are the only proofs i can give of my true concern yet be assured i shall never be so ungrateful as to forget your favors this days disaster will ever be before my eyes ah felicia replied the prince i thought your compassion would have inspired me with courage but i find it has a contrary influence oh that i could now live for you the hopes you have given me make me extremely regret leaving you since i must leave you for ever here his breast was oppressed with so deep a sorrow that he could only express it by his repeated sighs the queen who was impatient to have the prince executed had ordered that felicia should be called away from him when of a sudden she was alarmed hearing at the gates of the palace the shouts and cries of people in arms who were commanded by valiant mula and had already charged the soldiers of the guard they demanded the prince and threatened celima with a general revolt unanimously calling abelhamar their king and saying they had cause to fear a queen who was cruel enough to wash her hands in the blood of her nearest relation and that if she denied their request they would deliver her up to the punishment which she had designed for the prince  the queen would not have given much attention to the menaces of these seditious people had she not been informed that there were thick clouds of dust seen toward the road of tunis and that the sentinels who had already heard a confused noise of warlike instruments began to discover from the walls of the town a body of men marching with great precipitation soon after they came to acquaint her that there was a herald at the gate who desired admittance to her majesty in the name of ismael this news struck the queen with terror which she expressed by her emotions being divided between revenge and despair her ministers pressed her to give audience to the king of tituans herald and after being a little composed she consented to see him he brought her a letter which was in these terms  i am come to succor abelhamar who is a prince favored by heaven and our great prophet mahomet therefore you must deliver him up to me consider inhuman queen that you have neither arms nor subjects to support you i am informed of every thing that passes in the palace which i protest i will reduce to ashes unless you immediately restore the prince to his liberty but if you send him to me or hostages for his security i will favor your retreat you may leave the kingdom and take with you such attendance as you shall think necessary  ismael sultan   celimas fortune could hardly receive a greater change she now saw at the gates of her capital an enemy who treated her like a conqueror that was just going to dethrone her the soul of this imperious princess grew so furious at ismaels menaces that instead of thinking of the danger she was in her mind was only taken up with revenge come cried she barbarian come and be witness of my courage and resentment the man you intend to redeem shall be sacrificed before your eyes if heaven and earth should join and the elements return to their first chaos what is it to me i have but a life to lose which has been a burden to me these many years let us go and strike off this rebellious head which is so dear to ismael and send it to him from the height of the tower follow me said she to the herald who waited her answer come and see how i slight the threats of your master you shall witness the death of abelhamar and receive his last sighs ending these words she went hastily toward the place where her commands were only expected for his execution but the mufty the admiral and governor of the town with several of her faithful subjects flung themselves at her feet alas madam said they consider the misfortune which seems to point at you personally are you resolved to bury your self in the ruins of the palace that must certainly be your fate if you irritate a king who is before your walls with a potent army this is no time madam to revenge your self for in putting the prince to death it may raise a mutiny and should ismael take advantage of it you may lose your life or become captive to the conqueror is it not more glorious madam to fly and seek in another country some forces who encouraged by your presence may replace you on your throne  the queens women in tears prostrated themselves at her feet and said all that zeal and fear could inspire at last her imperious heart was touched rather at the danger she exposed so many persons to who depended on her than at what concerned her own person must the queen of fez submit cried she and seek her safety in a shameful flight which will cause her to blush the rest of her days oh heavens was ever destiny so wretched as mine i shall become a fugitive and banished my kingdom be forced to beg refuge of those whom i once could have protected i cannot think i deserve so cruel a fate here she continued her complaints and whilst she yielded to her excessive grief abelhamar was informed of the agreeable change in his fortune  he was entertaining felicia when they came to tell him that ismaels ships and forces were approaching think with what transports he received this news it is now madam said he to her that i can return the goodness you just now expressed your virtues have made a deep impression on me and since i am delivered from death you shall no longer feel the weight of your chains i rejoice my lord replied felicia to see that the danger is past and conjure you not to give your self any uneasiness about me i am born to be unhappy and the rigor of my captivity is nothing when compared to my inward pain farewell my lord you have now affairs of greater importance to employ your thoughts finishing these words she retired and abelhamar remained in the tower by order of the queen who sent hostages to ismael with assurances that the prince should be set at liberty as soon as she had left the city  unfortunate celima was now preparing a fleet and transports to carry away her most valuable goods she gave instructions to those persons whom she could not take along with her and having disposed every thing according to her intention she made all imaginable diligence to depart not depending on ismaels words and fearing the consequences of abelhamars resentment thus the fugitive queen went off by night with her women and slaves and was conducted to the vessel which attended her she ordered immediately to set sail with the rest of the fleet and the wind being fair they soon entered the mediterranean nothing could be equal to the concern celima was in for the loss of her kingdom she fetched deep sighs and in spite of all her pride could not restrain her tears fortune ungrateful fortune said she your capriciousness spares neither king nor subject who can flatter himself with being above your reach you declared your self my enemy from my infancy and pursued me in the remotest countries once taken by a pyrate i fell into the power of bajazet soon after you made use of cupids arrows to pierce my heart alas that wound i never can hope to cure at last to show your self more favorable you placed me on a throne which you now force me to abandon what must i expect from you next why dont you strike me at once with your most poisoned darts that i may not be exposed to new torments oh deplorable fate shall i thus be for ever persecuted and you felicia continued she casting her melancholy eyes on leonida who was near her you are the author of my last misfortune it is your fatal beauty that has been the occasion of this revolution ah how can you evince me that you are innocent alas madam replied felicia i had no hand in the princes criminal designs for if it be true that he had a passion for me it was contrary to my inclination i knew nothing of his disguise nor did i ever flatter him with any hopes on the contrary my aversion was the only return i made to his addresses and from the first hour he declared his sentiments for me i resolved never to change i was informed said celima that the count of la vagne who came to fetch away olympia had given you much uneasiness without doubt he is the person you love but you are convinced he has no longer a passion for you and since he has no regard to your affection you ought to disdain him these words put felicia into some confusion who blushing cast down her eyes without being able to utter one word and her beauteous cheeks moistened with tears sufficiently expressed the state of her anxious soul you make me no answer said celima fetching a sigh ah i am better able to answer for you i was willing to see whether your tongue could betray your heart or disown a distemper you cannot cure alas felicia i know too well by fatal experience the irresistible power of love which unhappily surpised me before i could suppress its first motions or even think how dangerous they might prove  if there are torments in love madam said felicia they ought not to affect a sovereign whom nature has graced with such transcendent perfections nothing but death or absence can deprive you of the object that is dear to you inconstancy which surpasses either in cruelty can never make you feel the tormenting effects of it ah felicia replied celima there is no pain like that which is occasioned by absence since it keeps us in continual fears both of death and infidelity at least madam said felicia there is one comfort in it which is that having but an uncertain knowledge of the truth we are generally inclined to believe what we most wish no continued celima it is not as you imagine uncertainty in love is a martyrdom which adds to all the pains we can endure alas madam replied felicia i should now look on that uncertain state as a happy one since i might derive from it the pleasing hopes which my present condition entirely destroys  the sovereign and her charming slave were entertaining each other with discourses of this quality and though celimas familiarity was very great yet felicia was ever mindful of the respect due to her night was far advanced before they took any rest but at last their eyes yielded to what nature required and celima had been asleep some hours when she was awaked by the noise of seamen and soldiers the former were preparing against a storm which threatened em and the latter for an engagement with abelhamar whose ships they had just discovered  you must know that as soon as the queen of fez had set out for the kingdom of granada the gates of sallee and the palace were opened to the king of tituan who immediately went to the tower where the young prince was prisoner but the latter being already set at liberty he came to meet the king with the greatest marks of joy and gratitude for his happy deliverance after abelhamar had employed some time in giving the king as obliging a reception as that juncture would permit he could not forbear going to the apartment which belonged to the queens slaves thinking to find felicia there for those who guarded him in his confinement had not informed him of her being embarked with celima  but you may imagine how great was his surprise not to meet any women there and to see every thing in disorder this giving him some suspicion he proceeded to the queens apartments which were open and quite empty so that he had no longer room to doubt of the loss of his felicia he ran up and down like a distracted man and expressed his excessive grief in such terms as extremely moved all that were with him have i then lost you felicia cried he my charming felicia have i lost you at a time that i was flattered with the hopes of a perfect felicity the compassion you showed for me when i was expecting immediate death was an evincement of the disposition you were in to do me justice and had you not been compelled to fly me i am inclined to believe you would no longer refuse me your affection but oh my felicia they have snatched you from me and my raging passion is the only thing i have left in your cruel absence go mula continued he go tell the king he has done nothing for me i am ready to give him up that life which he has preserved and i conjure him to take it from me or restore me my mistress but what do i say she is not in his power then let him give me his ships to pursue her  mula obeyed his commands and went to ismael whilst some persons who remained with the prince were giving him an account with how much precipitation the queen went off and that she had set sail for the kingdom of granada abelhamar whose impatience was great would not wait mulas return but ran to ismael who readily granted him all he desired so having chosen some of the kings best ships and swiftest sailers he pursued celima whose fleet he knew was neither considerable in strength or number though he did not reflect that his squadron was still inferior having put to sea he stood on the quarter deck endeavoring to discover some of the queens ships when he spied a vessel not very distant he gave orders they should make all sail which being executed and the wind fair it was not long before he came up with her  the first object that presented it self to him was the count of la vagne for his and olympias sailing had been prevented by stormy weather which forced em back so they chose to stay on shipboard and remain in the harbor where they waited a fair opportunity of going on their voyage as soon as abelhamar perceived it was the count whether he looked on him as a rival who was the occasion that his passion for felicia had not met with an obliging return or that he considered him as an enemy to that lovely captive having behaved himself toward her in an ungrateful and perfidious manner he could not help conceiving so immoderate an aversion for him that he instantly commanded mula to take the barge and go to the count of la vagne tell him said the prince that i look on him as a traitor who deserves death and if he has a mind to save those who are with him and have nothing to interpose in our quarrel he may come to me or give me his word of honor and i will go and decide the affair with him  mula went on board the count of la vagnes ship and though he was not acquainted with abelhamar whom he was sure had no reasonable motive to quarrel with him yet he was so offended to see himself suspected being a traitor that without entering into a detail which might have made up the difference he leaped into mulas boat i will go said he to him with an air full of pride and anger your master shall see that such a man as i is not to be insulted unrevenged thus without reflecting on the danger to which he exposed himself and even forgetting his dear mistress he ordered them to row him to abelhamars ship  the boat had already made some way when olympias woman awaked her and gave her an account of what was passing her surprise was so great that she just gave her self time to take her nightgown then ran upon deck from whence she perceived her lover at a great distance do you abandon me then my dear count cried she and are you going to expose a life which is mine what have you to say to cruel abelhamar oh dont leave me so but come back to your dear olympia or take me along with you that i may undergo the same fate whilst she was uttering these words the count had reached abelhamars ship olympia seeing this desired the captain of that she was in to let her take his barge which being granted she bad them pull up with all speed toward the princes ship but she unfortunately arrived there too late the count was already engaged with abelhamar and though he fought with all the courage and dexterity imaginable he was forced at length to yield having received a mortal wound  as he was making his last efforts to defend himself against abelhamars reiterated blows the unhappy olympia came up and perceiving at a small distance that her lover was covered with blood and hardly able to support himself she cried out in a loud voice hold barbarous prince hold what have i done to you that should provoke you to deprive me of my life dont you know that the count of la vagne is to be mine give some intermission to your rage cruel as you are or if nothing but a sacrifice will satisfy you i am here ready to receive the blow come and pierce my heart but spare oh spare the man i love  the accent of a voice so dear to the count reached him just as he fell at abelhamars feet he strove to raise his head and turning his eyes toward olympias barge he saw his divine mistress despairing who with much ado got on board the ship and was no sooner there but fell in a swoon near the count and remained speechless a long while after she was a little recovered all she could do was to lay her dying lovers head on her knees and bath his wounds with her tears thus oppressed with mortal grief she sat down without being able to complain  the count endeavored to speak to her and taking her by the hand said i die my dear olympia i die entirely yours and regret departing from life only for your sake with these words his soul took its flight and left his body in the arms of his deplorable mistress who said such moving things and acted so much despair that even abelhamar was inconsolable for being the author of her affliction he sent her half dead on board the ship she was in before and ordered the count of la vagnes corpse to be also transported olympia instead of going to genoa sailed for sardinia in order to retire to her aunts monastry where having erected a magnificent tomb for her lover she continued the rest of her days lamenting the irreparable loss she had made thus we are often deceived when in the greatest hopes of an approaching happiness which fortune changes into the cruelest torments  abelhamar would not have left olympia in this desolate condition had not his passion invited him elsewhere he impatiently desired to overtake the queen being resolved to force his felicia from her and he was not long in his pursuit before they came to tell him that they had discovered celimas ships one may judge how extremely overjoyed he was at this news he immediately gave orders to make all sail then employing his wishes for success and a fair wind prepared himself for an engagement with the queens squadron who were also doing the same  this unfortunate princess knowing the danger which threatened her encouraged her people and having sent to all the captains to come on board her ship she called a council then orders were given and each officer thought of nothing but doing his duty the trumpets began to sound and the cannons roared whilst on each side they were endeavoring to gain the advantage of the wind with a resolution not to show any favor thus ready for a fight celima said to her soldiers observe that dangerous serpent pointing at abelhamar who was in armor walking on his quarter deck see that ungrateful man whom i brought up with so much care he is now meditating my ruin did i not spare his life though it ever endangered mine yet he is not satisfied with my quitting my kingdom to expose myself on this dangerous element he even pursues me and so greedily thirsts after blood that nothing can please him but my death help me ye brave and loyal subjects to punish this rebel and let us by destroying him afford an example for other traitors in ages to come  the queen was thus animating her soldiers whilst felicia and inea were indulging their melancholy see my dear said felicia see these dreadful preparations what can be the fatal consequence of this engagement i fear we shall once more be the victims of fortune oh heaven cried she rather let me die than fall into the hands of abelhamar since no greater disaster can ever happen to me  inea endeavored to comfort and give her hopes saying why do you thus afflict your self since nothing is yet decided we are all preparing for a vigorous resistance and the weather begins to be so stormy that one would almost believe it impossible for the two fleets to approach she was still speaking when on a sudden there arose such a boisterous wind with thunder and lightning that on each side instead of continuing their preparation for a fight they were forced to employ all hands to save themselves from greater dangers  thus the fleets were dispersed without knowing which way to steer their course the raging wind rent the sails and split the masts and the artless pilot with death in his looks was torn from his helm the impetuous waves tossed the ships here and there till at last unable to withstand their resistless fury some were dashed against the rocks others wrecked on the shore and few escaped this terrible tempest  abelhamar having lost sight of the ship wherein he thought felicia and despairing of ever seeing her more looked on the danger he was in with some kind of satisfaction no said he to mula who made unsuccesful efforts to console his master no should i escape death which now threatens me you must not think that i can ever enjoy any pleasure or happiness without the possession of felicia my passion for her increases more and more by the many difficulties i meet with and though i see the fatal powers which oppose me yet nothing shall make me change the design i have of pursuing her  by this time the weather grew more calm and day being far advanced the prince was consulting mula which way he should steer his course to find his mistress he had already passed the streights of gibraltar in order to go to carthagena or porto real not doubting but the queen had reached one of those harbors to shelter herself from the storm he therefore resolved for the coast of andalusia but they who accompanied him disapproved his design consider my lord said they that this is the only ship left of several which ismael lent you and that your pursuing celima may prove of a fatal consequence her sex her beauty and misfortunes will plead for her and what will the king of granada think to see you come into his dominions in pursuit of an unhappy princess who has abandoned here is and left you master of them he may detain you as an hostage till he has made advantageous conditions in her favor with the king of tituan and it is not to be expected that this monarch will continue your friend whilst you act contrary to his interest for should his generous disposition happen to change he might take possession himself of what he has just acquired for you let us return to sallee my lord continued they if the kingdom of fez remains in your hands you may soon be in a condition to ask what you please of the king of granada who will deliver up felicia to you rather than have any difference with you about a christian slave  abelhamar was mortally displeased to see that the present conjuncture obliged him to return to fez and what added to his affliction in his way thither was to meet on every side the dismal fragments of shipwracks which covered the surface of the sea and made him but too sensible that he had lost the greatest part of his fleet  the queen on her side had not been exposed to lesser dangers for all her fleet was dispersed and as the wind drove her into the port of carthagena the stern of her ship struck so fiercely against another that they both had like to have sunk which accident shattered what the storm had spared but several boats and barges came immediately to the queens assistance and landed her safe with her women and equipage  she had hardly stepped out of her barge but was informed of the great alterations which had happened in the kingdom of granada by the death of mahomet who being poisoned by the means of a gown which was sent to him as a present had left the crown to his brother joseph whom he had detained prisoner many years in the castle of salobrena celima sent an officer of her guards to congratulate this prince on his happy and unexpected accession to the throne desiring him at the same time to take compassion on her she sent also to some of her near relations who held the lighest rank in that court  the governor of carthagena hearing that the queen of fez was landed went to meet her with all the marks of honor and respect that were due to her quality she had an apartment prepared for her in the castle where she remained two days to repose her self after the danger and fatigue she had undergone and from thence set out for granada where they were already informed of her landing and were prepared to receive her being willing to give a sanctuary to that unfortunate queen  joseph king of granada immediately ordered his two sons mahomet and osmin to go and meet celima with assurances of his concern for her misfortunes and how desirous he was to serve her in all that lay in his power these princes were perfectly accomplished and as the prince of carency had been confined by the late kings orders in the castle of salobrena whilst they were prisoners there they had conceived so entire a friendship for him that they resolved to set him at liberty if ever their condition should change but the king their father being desirous to make peace with the spaniards and knowing that the infanta don fernand had offered mahomet a considerable ranson for the count of la vagne for he continued calling himself by that title thought that in detaining him it might be a more effectual means to obtain what he so earnestly wished nevertheless as he had a particular esteem for the prince he asked him if he would give him his honor not to go away without his consent which the other having readily promised the king took him along with him to granada  the day he made his entry he sent the prince of carency a magnificent dress with a rich turbant and a scymiter embellished with jewels which showed it was the kings pleasure he should dress himself after the moorish manner in order to accompany him to all the solemnities of his coronation  but the king who had found in the prince a great resemblance of the brave assimir who was a grandee of the house of abanserages much considered in that kingdom and had been lately killed used often to give the prince that name out of a mark of favor who equally received it as such and as he was unwilling to be known he chose rather to be called by that name than any other  though time had not been able to diminish the princes passion or alleviate his grief yet in spite of his excessive melancholy every body distinguished him as one of the finest gentlemen that was ever known amongst all those who showed him the greatest marks of esteem the princes mahomet and osmin particularly expressed themselves his friends mahomet had eminent qualities but was so presumptuous that he would have sacrificed any thing to gratify his desires his younger brother osmin was as fine a prince and had nobler inclinations which made the king have a greater affection for him than for the rest of his children  as soon as news was brought of celimas being near granada these two princes by the king their fathers order at the head of the noblemen of that court went out of town to meet the queen the prince of carency was one of those who accompanied them in this cavalcade and each cavalier had a motto painted on his shield the prince caused an apollo pursuing daphne to be drawn on his with these words round it written in spanish quiero y busco quien me aborece y me fuyo that is i love and pursue one who hates and flies me this thought expressed in a gallant manner his disappointed passion the princes understood it immediately for whilst they were in confinement together he told em part of his adventures and made a secret only of his and his mistresss true name which he concealed for several political reasons especially on his brother and don john of velascos account who had both fought against the moors and defeated them in several engagements  so many historians have informed the world how highly the moors in those days distinguished themselves above other nations by their gallantry and magnificence that i shall decline extending that subject and only say that the unfortunate but beauteous queen of fez elected that court for her refuge where she appeared with such attractives as inspired love in all who beheld her  mahomet and his brother accompanied by the prince of carency in his moorish dress which admirably became him met the queen at a small distance from granada she sat alone in a fine open chariot and all her women followed her in chaises felicia and inea were together in one and had drawn the curtains to have an opportunity of entertaining each other more conveniently ought we to look on our being near spain said felicia to her friend as a favorable change toward our better fortune i think replied inea that the circumstances can no ways prove to our disadvantage alas as for my part interrupted felicia i have so little hopes of happiness in this life that i could now leave the world with pleasure inea did not omit any thing which could divert her from these melancholy reflections though she herself had cause enough to be uneasy not having heard from her dear don ramire whilst they were talking the princes alighted and saluted the queen with many assurances in the name of the king their father then took horse again and rode by the side of her chariot entertaining her majesty with what was most suitable to the occasion of her voyage but celima became of a sudden so pensive that she could hardly make em any answer her eyes were entirely fixed on the prince of carency and she had not power to turn them on any other object her joy and surprise were equally extraordinary and what added to both was seeing him in a moorish dress which gave her a curiosity to ask his name of one of the guards that was near her who not knowing that the prince was a prisoner of war but had only seen him with the king in his journey from salobrena to granada told the queen he was called assimir  she immediately conjectured he had some important reasons which obliged him to assume that name and disguise so did not ask any other questions relating to him yet what gave her some uneasiness was to find that he did not take any particular notice of her she was a good while in expectation he would have spoken to her at last seeing he continued silent she addressed her discourse to him and for a pretense asked him the signification of the motto which she had perceived on his shield he told her the meaning and added that he was the unhappiest man in the world the queen imagined that by the apollo he meant himself and daphne to be her which filled her mind with such ideas as were too pleasing to be expressed i have sometimes had a prophetic spirit said she to him smiling and have foretold things without knowing their true cause methinks i have a great disposition to do you the same favor assimir your daphne neither flies nor hates you and you shall soon have the satisfaction of seeing her ah madam cried the prince transported what do you tell me is it possible that the cruel fair one who is the object of my sufferings will at last vouchsafe to make me happy yes replied celima with a gracious air she is as willing as you to put a period to your torments and i promise you that as soon as i am a little at leisure i will tell you more of the matter alas madam replied he i do not deserve that so great a queen should be concerned in my fortune which hitherto has proved very fatal and i dare hardly hope a better one for the future celima said no more to him at that time fearing the particular distinction she had shown him might be taken notice of which undoubtedly would have disobliged mahomet who had already found so many charms in the queen that he could not sufficiently deplore her misfortunes and whilst he was thus offering her his pity a more powerful passion made way to his heart  the nearer celima approached granada the more she admired the beauty of that famous city which is situated in a plain at the extremity whereof is a snowy hill from whence spring two rivers the daro and genil the one often produces golddust mixed with the sand and the other pure silver the air of that climate is sweet and refined and there seldom appears any winter the spring and autumn united afford flowers and fruit without being at the trouble of cultivating the earth there are whole forests of orange myrtle and pomgranate trees and as nature had taken care to embellish the country so no art had been spared to beautify the city which was encompassed with a strong wall and twelve hundred towers the palace of alhambro which the kings had chosen for their court was so magnificent that nothing but the castle of abbaycin could be equal to it which on every side shined with gold and azure supported by marble and porphyry besides the moors observed an admirable order in architecture which highly recommended their buildings and as for their gardens walks and fountains they were so wonderfully well contrived that nothing could be added to their beauty and agreeableness  the queen arrived at the gates of the town where the people assembled in great multitudes but the prince of carency to avoid the crowd took another way which insensibly led him to the side of the river daro whence he continued till he came to a fountain whose water was as clear as crystal the deep silence which reigned in that place and the inclination he had to meditate on what the queen of fez had said to him invited him to alight he tied his horse to a tree and lay down on the grass then calling to mind what celima had told him by what chance thought he did this princess who never saw me before single me out to acquaint me that leonida still loves me and that i shall soon see her has any one informed her of my sentiments methinks it does not well become one of her rank to rally an unfortunate man who cannot even flatter himself with hopes much less with the real enjoyment of so unexpected a blessing  he was drowned in reflections of this nature when the voice of a man who spoke the arabic tongue interrupted him asking whether the queen of fez was yet arrived at granada the prince knew very well that the person who was coming up to him was a stranger and that he only spoke arabic to him because of his dress supposing him to be some grandee in alliance with the moors he fixed his eyes on this foreigner but heavens how great was their surprise when they knew each other benavidez for it was he could not help turning pale at the thoughts of his perfidiousness and the prince swelling with anger said to him from whence come you unworthy wretch that you are what doemon has conveyed you here to receive the punishment of of your treacheries finishing these words he drew his sword and used it with such fierceness that the spaniard notwithstanding his bravery was daunted and seized with terror till at last calling despair to his succor and seeing the inevitable danger he was in he fought rather like a desperate man than one who had a mind to save his life the prince resolving not to spare him reiterated his blows with such vigor that he soon gave benavidez a mortal wound which made him fall at his feet ah my lord said he to the prince with a feeble and incoherent accent it is but just i should die by your hand after all the injuries i have done you did i deserve such usage traitor replied the prince since you can deceive me no longer where have you left perfidious leonida now is the time to convince me that you are yet capable of repenting a base action i am willing to obey you answered benavidez stretching out his hand upon condition that you will forgive me speak and i will even forget all said the prince tell me what is become of my leonida i declare to you replied benavidez whose face showed the symptoms of an approaching death that leonida never ceased loving you she no ways consented to her flight but almost consumed with grief loaded me with the cruellest reproaches and her utmost aversion was the only return she made my passion yet in spite of her tears and resistance i took her with me on board a ship and was promising myself a happy voyage when we were met by some of the enemys ships who engaged and took ours i was so dangerously wounded that  farewell my lord i can say no more i am dying his eyes instantly closed and his soul made its exit whilst he was lying in the princes arms  benavidezs death touched the prince of carencys generous soul who forgetting all his ingratitude began to pity him saying that he would never have been guilty of the crimes he had committed could he have defended his heart from leonidas charms and looking on him as an unhappy rival and a reconciled enemy his compassion took place of his resentment he reflected on what benavidez had just told him relating to his dear leonida but he was perfectly inconsolable not knowing the enemies who had taken her fatal death cried he thou have snatched away the life of a man who was going to inform me of a circumstance which is of the greatest importance to me where must i fly to seek the object of my love and how can i tell into whose hands she is fallen oh heavens am i not more unfortunate than ever the thoughts of her being inconstant gave some intermission to my passion for which i was endeavoring to find a cure but now the case is changed i am concerned for a mistress to whom i am contracted she has ever been true to me and perhaps has found a lover and a master in the man who has her now in his possession oh unparalled fatality how tormenting will these apprehensions be to my afflicted soul which way shall i go to find her the prince was so deeply involved in these anxious reflections that he did not immediately perceive a wound he had received in his arm but finding himself grow weak by the great loss of blood he thought fit to retire  just as he entered the town he met zulema who was a moor of the family of abenserages to whose guard he had been committed by orders of the late king whilst he was prisoner in the castle of salobrena the prince having a confidence in this moor thought he could not choose any one more capable of ordering benavidezs burial therefore he desired zulema to oblige him in this occasion who without delay though the night was far spent took some slaves with him and went to the fountain in order to execute the princes commands  as he came near the place he heard a person lamenting grievously which at first surpised him not distinguishing what he said but having alighted from his horse he perceived a man who was embracing beavidezs body and bemoaning his misfortune in the spanish tongue ah my dear benavidez said he how unlucky it is that i was not here to defend you against the traitors who have murdered you alas my uneasiness and fears had already foretold your death here zulema interrupted this stranger and being compassionate told him benavidez had not been killed by any treacherous means and that he who fought him was so generous an enemy that he had even desired him to come and see the corpse interred the spaniard who was very young expressed his concern by his tears and said oh sir nothing can alleviate my affliction since i have lost all in losing my dear master zulema endeavored to comfort him then ordered his people to take the corpse and bury it in a little wood not far from the fountain  this being performed zulema who was naturally generous and then moved with pity at the repeated complaints of this servant of benavidez asked him if he would go along with him to granada you shall be safe in my house said he which is a favor your countrymen cannot well expect in this kingdom don sanche for that was the spaniards name hesitated some time before he made an answer but at last whether fear or prudence prevailed with him he told zulema that since he was pleased to offer him his house for a sanctuary he was very willing to wait on him zulema who was uneasy about the princes wound went directly to see him and the mean while sent the spaniard to his house to wait his return  the prince was in bed and the surgeon who had dressed his wound found it somewhat dangerous which soon occasioned a report in the town that he had had a rencounter though the particulars were not known and when zulema entered the princes chamber he found the kings two sons sitting by him who were much concerned at this accident mahomet thus continued the discourse he had already begun i must tell you it is unkind to make a mystery to us of your enemys name i owe you my lord replied the prince too much gratitude and affection ever to do that which might deserve a reproach from you i should be very willing to tell you who was my enemy if there were cause to apprehend any farther consequences but i am entirely easy on that score besides i am obliged to keep a secret which i was sworn to before i thought you would have asked me the detail of this affair so beg leave to be silent  osmin fearing this conversation might create some uneasiness in the prince obligingly waved the discourse and said to him you have lost very much by not attending the queen of fez for laying aside the honorable reception the king my father gave her and the extraordinary luster which the ladies of our court appeared in she commanded all her slaves to pull off their veils and i must confess we were both astonished and charmed to see so many beautiful creatures their praise was the chief entertainment of the court and i am persuaded they will cause many a lover to be guilty of infidelity that is already your case brother replied mahomet smiling and you cannot deny but the eyes of that felicia whose name you were so desirous to know have made such an impression as may endanger your liberty i own to you said osmin that i prefer her to all the rest her beauty is not to be paralleled and i am surpised brother that you escaped falling her captive no answered mahomet my heart is not so easily wounded alas my lord interrupted the prince of carency perhaps your time is not come but you will find your self as sensible as any of us when you meet with the object whom destiny has decreed to inspire you as for my part i dread that fatal moment as much as a pilot does a rock in a storm why dont you bestow your inclinations on a slave like felicia replied osmin at least you would be free from any cruel torments who can tell my lord said the prince whether that slave will like the man who has a passion for her love is capricious and ever guided by fancy therefore a slave may look with indifference on the greatest monarch in the world how can you thus oppose my satisfaction with your reflections cried osmin would you have me cease loving felicia out of groundless apprehensions indeed brother replied mahomet it is strange you should say you love a person whom you hardly know nay you may style it as you please said osmin but what i can affirm is that the perfections of this young captive have already engaged me nothing in nature can be more beautiful no nor even comparable to this lovely creature and i impatiently wish assimirs recovery that he may be able to make his court to the queen of fez he will then be judge of what i advance  it will not be so easy to see her as you imagine my lord interrupted zulema who had been silent all this while i have been at salee where i stayed a considerable time and the negotiations i was employed in by the late king gave me frequent opportunities of having both private and public audiences with the queen yet whenever i was admitted i found her surrounded with the oldest and ugliest women in the world she used to set a strict watch on all her pretty slaves and keep em so concealed that unless her humor be much altered i am sure you will find some difficulty in paying your courtship to felicia that sex is very unjust cried osmin i suppose celima will not let her slaves be seen for fear they should eclipse her charms it is you that are unjust replied mahomet why should you attribute to any other cause a custom which has been long established only for the safety of slaves every one must agree that celima is endowed with too many excellencies to apprehend any thing from other beauties ha brother said osmin you were boasting a while ago of your insensibility but i find by the passionate air with which you express yourself in the queens defense that you are not so very indifferent as you would make us believe mahomet who had no mind to satisfy his brother on that subject made no reply but rising up addressed himself to assimir meaning the prince of carency whom he embraced and after having desired him to take care of his health he and his brother took their leave of him zulema retired at the same time without acquainting him that he had met benavidezs servant the prince on the other hand was impatient to entertain him but there was no possibility of doing it till the next day  one may imagine the prince passed but a very ill night what the queen and benavidez had said to him strangely perplexed his mind which being added to the pain he suffered by his wound threw him before morning into a violent fever zulema who had a particular concern for the prince rose early and went to enquire after his health they told him he had not reposed all night and if he pleased might go into his chamber as soon as the prince perceived him ah my dear zulema said he i was wishing to see you all that passed yesterday has put me into such a disorder as i shall not be able to overcome without your assistance the queen of fez spoke to me as if she knew me and i remarked in her air and eyes something more obliging than is usually expressed for a person one has never seen besides she assures me that my mistress neither flies nor hates me and that i shall have the pleasure of seeing her soon who could have informed her of a thing so positive i should be inclined to think that chance was the only cause why she entertained me so agreeably were it not for the rencounter i had yesterday near the fountain he whom i fought was my rival the same benavidez who carried off my felicia he told me with his last breath she had ever loved me and that her sentiments for me were still the same it is not probable he would have uttered an untruth in so dismal a condition but just as he was going to tell me where he had left her he was deprived both of his speech and life you cannot imagine how this grieves my soul felicia loves me can any happiness be greater yet alas i have lost her and know not where to enquire after her what misfortune can be equal to mine here he was some time silent  zulema told him that a more favorable fortune would certainly disclose a secret on which depended his felicity and that he did not doubt but he might receive some information from a young man he found weeping near benavidezs body whom he had detained at his house for that purpose oh i conjure you send for him immediately cried the prince i remember his master in approaching me asked whether the queen of fez was yet arrived at granada perhaps she knew him and that in relating his adventures to her he mentioned something concerning mine i ought not to neglect any means in my present circumstances for if that young man was with benavidez when he ran away with my mistress and can tell me what is become of her i shall be blessed above mankind  i perceive so great an emotion in you my lord replied zulema that i am sorry for having acquainted you with a particular which may be prejudicial to your health no said the prince do not fear any thing but if you have either love or pity relieve me in this urgent occasion shall i tell you then what i was thinking answered zulema osmin spoke to you yesterday very much in praise of one felicia who is a slave of celimas it is probable she may be the person you love i began to suspect the same interrupted the prince but was not willing to harbor such a thought for there are many felicias in spain and after the adventure i had at jaen with don alonso by a mistake which that name occasioned i have room to fear the like disappointment i only beg you will send for the young man you spoke of  zulema commanded one of his slaves in whom he confided to give a moorish dress to the spaniard and bring him immediately along with him this was the precaution he used to prevent his being taken at granada for a sranger don sanche was a little unwilling at first to go out of zulemas house not knowing where they intended to carry him but the slave having told him they were going to an intimate friend of his masters whose name was assimir he readily followed him believing assimir was a moor and he continued in the same opinion even when he entered the prince of carencys chamber who was in bed and the windows closed come nearer don sanche said zulema to him and tell us sincerely what you know concerning felicia of leon  this unexpected question surpised the spaniard who was some time without making any answer what said the prince do you hesitate tell me immediately what is become of her were you not with your master when he carried her away heavens what new astonishment did this voice create don sanche or to explain myself in a clearer manner casilda sister to benavidez for it was she who was thus disguised was suddenly struck with such a violent trembling that had not the chamber been very dark it would have been impossible to conceal her disorder her eyes were endeavoring to see the person whom her heart already knew whilst the prince on his side was in the utmost impatience to be informed of his mistresss fate what said she to her self shall my rival for ever be adored and could her absence no ways extinguish the princes passion was ever misfortune equal to mine then resolving at once not to mention any thing which might discover leonidas being with the queen of fez it is true my lord said she i was with don fernand benavidez when he ran away with the fair lady you named and we should have had a prosperous voyage were it not for the fatal rencounter of two turkish ships who engaged ours and took it my master being the only man that resisted with undaunted courage the captains of these ships were so charmed with felicias beauty which had received no
