injury from her affliction that they resolved to carry her to constantinople in order to present her to the grand seignior therefore having given her a very rich dress they brought her to that emperor who was so mightily taken with her that he immediately placed her in his seraglio as for my master and i good fortune would have it that we were sold to the bashaw of morea who knew don fernand benavidez to whom he was indebted for some considerable service he had rendered him in spain this bashaw was a famous renegado which was his only crime for he was very generous and so grateful that he restored us to our liberty without requiring any ransom thus we returned to andalusia where we were just landed when my master heard that the queen of fez was coming to granada which determined him to come hither in order to pay his court to her  the prince during casildas relation was seized with an unspeakable affliction when he heard that felicia was among the grand seigniors women the anxiety of such a cruel thought overpowered his senses and his wound opening so great a quantity of blood gushed out that it flung him into a swoon  zulema surpised at the princes silence spoke to him but as he made no reply he took his hand which was in a cold sweat this startled him and calling for a light he saw the picture of despair painted on the face of this unfortunate prince who was without motion and his paleness would have persuaded one that his soul had already left his body but how shall i represent here the deplorable condition of casilda whose passion was raised to such a transcendency that having no regard to her honor she framed a false story to destroy the princes hopes of ever seeing his divine mistress at another time she would have sacrificed a thousand lives to have saved his but at this juncture had he died one might have accused her with being the cause of his death  had not zulemas concern been so great he would have easily discovered that of the counterfeit don sanche who without restraint shed a deluge of tears and expressed a more than ordinary care in assisting the prince who at last receiving a little strength from the cordials they gave him opened his weak eyes which he fixed languishingly on his friend and don sanche whose face he thought he knew yet did not take much notice of him then turning to zulema ah pity me cried he since my misfortunes can never be greater they are come to their last period i had lost my felicia and thought her false which in some measure suppressed my tormenting passion but now i am informed she is living and that her affection for me is still the same had that tyrant death shatchd her from me i should doubtless have been inconsolable for her loss yet methinks i should be free from those tumultuous fears which now rack my mind oh what dismal objects appear to my distracted imagination felicia in the seraglio and beloved by the grand seignior heavens what greater cruelty can ever be inflicted on a man so passionately in love i have lost her and shall never see her more i am even jealous and i fear her heart will at last yield to the barbarous laws which ill fortune has imposed on her here his disturbed thoughts interrupted his discourse whilst zulema was using all his endeavors to mitigate so violent a grief felicia had too sincere a passion for you said he ever to change in favor of a prince who is no ways agreeable and is too proud to give himself the least trouble toward obtaining the favors of a lady he thinks all must submit to his authority and i am persuaded that as she will neither relish his addresses nor make any return her resistance and coldness will soon render her indifferent to the emperor suppose i were free from these apprehensions interrupted the prince by what means shall i hear from her is she not in the grand seigniors seraglio and absolutely lost for me oh it is too true i cannot flatter myself no not even wish to see her more which misfortune compleats my despair  casilda was in no small confusion when she heard him speak in such passionate terms she was several times tempted to make herself known that she might address herself to him in the tenderest expressions love could inspire but calling to mind what passed between em when she acquainted him with leonidas flight it made her apprehend that if she spoke to him at this juncture it would be as ill timed therefore thought proper to wait another opportunity in the mean time she affected an extraordinary concern for the prince who remarked it and was not slow in showing his acknowledgments for he told her thinking he was speaking to a man that although his present fortune being then a prisoner did not permit him to bestow great favors on those who were in his service yet if he was willing to stay with him till he could be better provided for he would take care of him assimir little knew the effect this proposal created in our disguised lady who immediately accepted it with all imaginable marks of joy and respect assuring him that no body would serve him with more zeal and fidelity but before we see how strict she was to her promise let us be informed by what chance she came to granada  abelhamar and the admiral of fez having taken the ship leonida was in it was thought benavidez could not recover of the wounds he had received in his vigorous resistance so was left for dead but after leonida had been conducted on board the admiral they found in benavidez some symptoms of life which made em take care of him till they were landed at sallee where he continued a long time extremely ill leonida knew nothing of it being strictly guarded in the palace but as soon as he was recovered he resolved either pay her ransom or carry her off by stratagem with this design he wrote to casilda who having received his letter lost no time in preparing for that voyage and as her passion for the prince of carency had met with no return but disdain she was meditating on some desperate enterprise in order to act a vengeance proportionable to the injury she thought this might be a favorable opportunity therefore taking her jewels with a considerable sum of money she disguised herself in mans apparel to prevent her being known and embarked for sallee where she arrived soon after with the resolution of taking away leonidas life and to succeed in her wicked design she had brought with her a box of the subtilest poison  benavidez was not a little overjoyed at casildas arrival and after he had paid his ransom to the admiral he only thought of recovering leonida but the queen having an extraordinary friendship for her hardly suffered her to be out of her sight which made him fear his attempt would be in vain this was the state of his affairs when the king of tunis invaded the kingdom of fez which obliged celima to abandon sallee and at the same time that she embarked benavidez and his sister in disguise took their passage in one of the ships which were bound for granada during their voyage they often saw leonida aboard the queens ship whose sight only inflamed benavidezs heart with love and casildas with rage but the dreadful storm which arose dispersing the fleet their ship was driven some leagues beyond carthagena where they landed and set out immediately on horseback for granada casilda who was of a weak constitution and already very much fatigued with her voyage was left a great way behind which was the occasion of her not arriving till after her brothers rencounter with the prince of carency which was then too late  i have already told you with what marks of honor and distinction the queen of fez was received at her arrival at the court of granada but i did not mention the magnificent entertainment the king gave her at the palace of alhambro after which the princes and most part of the noblemen conducted her to the castle of the abbaicyn which was prepared for her and there took leave of her majesty  as soon as she was at liberty to give some time to reflection she went to take the air on a terrace walk adjoining her apartment which had a prospect over the river daro there a thousand hurrying thoughts started from her mind what course shall i take said she to herself and whom shall i trust with my secret must i once more to the shame of my sex and glory make my weakness known to this lovely stranger heaven has sent him to me again and i am inclined to believe he is thinking on me yes certainly the apollo pursuing daphne which was painted on his shield with his motto nay more than that his languishing looks and distractions in short every thing persuades me he is in love yet if it were with me ought not he to be inspired with some motions of sympathy which would have told him that his unknown of nicopolis and the queen of fez were the same why does he not discover as many charms in my person as he did in my wit and generosity alas he was then too young to feel the effects of love gratitude was the only thing that moved him to make a return and i now fear some softer care imploys his thoughts but continued she i cannot persuade myself that fortune has brought him once more in my way only to add fresh afflictions to those i have already undergone i am rather disposed to look on this as the beginning of a happiness which will end by the destruction of my enemies this prince is nearly related to the king of france i will make myself a christian and in giving him my hand present him with my crown he may head an army and invade the kingdom of fez which he soon will be master of the people by my example will submit to his laws and after being an unhappy fugitive destitute of all hopes i shall see myself crowned with unspeakable felicity celima thus indulged her imagination till it grew so late that she thought fit to retire to her apartment where she passed the night betwixt soft repose and a thousand agreeable ideas which made her appear the next day in all her charms  but before the queen would admit of any visit she sent for felicia to whom she spoke in these terms i am desirous to know whether your sentiments for the count of la vagne are still the same therefore felicia confess ingenuously the truth has not his perfidiousness been capable to extinguish the affection you had for him when you were persuaded of his constancy search well into your heart for i have some reason to enquire about it and whatever answer you make me i shall not love you the less these questions caused some surprise in felicia who at first had a mind to disguise her sentiments but having considered that she had not long before confessed her weakness to the queen she was of opinion it was better to speak her thoughts without any dissimulation madam replied she since they are your majestys commands i cannot refuse obeying i own with the utmost confusion that till now it has not been in my power to banish from my heart the fatal idea of the count of la vagne i daily entertain myself with the cause i have to hate him as the cruellest of my enemies yet alas it is past my skill and i dare not even hope that time it self will ever be able to effect my cure you do love him then interrupted the queen if love consists in often thinking of a person replied felicia i am convinced i still have an affection for him i may now confide in you replied the queen therefore hear me and be secret  i was hardly out of my infancy when my unlucky stars decreed i should fall into the hands bajazet whose passion for me only increased my aversion to him and i thought nothing could be more deplorable than my destiny  these were my sentiments when he went into missia and compelled me to go along with him where after a victory over the christians he was desirous to see the prisoners of distinction who had been taken and as out of a politic motive he endeavored to inspire me with cruelty and inure me to tragic scenes he ordered i should be placed at a window which was grated and looked over the court where the christians were to suffer death and several noblemen of france had already been executed when i saw a young prince appear whose beauty surpassed that which we attribute to the god of love he seemed to be about fifteen or sixteen years of age he was tall wellshapd and had fair hair which hung in fine curls on his shoulders and in spite of his careless air he had something so great and noble in his mien that the other princes were not to be compared to him oh felicia could you but imagine what i felt in that moment a quick emotion seized all my soul i was troubled without knowing the cause and in a word had like to have died for fear bajazet should have taken away a life which was already dearer to me than my own i began to think what i could do to deliver this lovely prince from the immediate danger which threatened him whether to fling myself at bajazets feet and beg his life or to offer myself a victim in his room for i could have done any thing to save him but whilst a thousand such thoughts were torturing my mind the emperor resolved on accepting his ransom which news so transported me that my joy was inexpressible  this young prince was prisoner in the tower of nicopolis and as my apartment had a prospect of it i used to pass whole days at my closet window in fruitless sighs and wishes but one evening as i was endeavoring with the help of a telescope to discover the object i so dearly loved i perceived him walking on the leads of the tower and he appeared to me so melancholy that it threw me into the deepest concern i immediately resolved on writing to him notwithstanding the danger to which i exposed myself if bajazet had known it but love is often more lucky than wise and chance on that occasion is a much better servant than reason when i had ended my letter i confided it to an eunuch who had attended me a long time and showed a particular affection for my service what did i not say to persuade him to be faithful which having promised me even at the hazard of his life he conveyed my letter to the top of the tower by means of an arrow and the prince having received it sent me an answer which entirely vanquished me i was informed that his ransom was not come and the more i considered how dear he daily grew to me the greater cause i had to fear equally for him and myself i was perfectly acquainted with bajazets inhuman temper and too sensible of my own weakness to believe that it would be in my power to fly a prince who so entirely possessed my thoughts these considerations obliged me to take measures for his immediate departure but alas what torments did not i endure through the necessity of so cruel a resolution  to this effect i was forced once more to confide in my eunuch who bribed one of the princes guards by whose means a strong box was conveyed into his chamber wherein i sent him a considerable sum to pay his ransom and a letter which was the last i wrote to him being bereft of the hopes of ever seeing him more imagine felicia how many anxious hours i have passed since that unlucky day  soon after bajazets fortune met with an unhappy change for tamerlane having engaged him gained a complete victory and took him prisoner it was with no small difficulty i made my escape and returned to my fathers dominions where i was no sooner arrived but several kings and princes made their addresses to me some out of ambition and others out of a sincere love for my person but i was so entirely prepossessed with the idea of him who had charmed me at nicopolis that nothing at sallee was capable of making an impression on me so in spite of myself i was in love without hopes of a return this was the state of my mind at my arrival here but how can i express the surprise and agitation i was in when amongst the noblemen who came to receive me out of the gates of the town i perceived the man i love this christian prince under the name and dress of a moor appeared to me as charming as ever no it is impossible for you to comprehend what i felt at so unexpected a rencounter my heart was seized with so many different motions that i was not able to speak and whilst i was endeavoring to recover myself assimir for that is the name he goes by at this court approached and gave me an occasion to see the motto that was painted on his shield which persuaded me the memory of his unknown of nicopolis was dear to him i must confess i was equally surpised and overjoyed for i could not flatter myself with being still in the thoughts of that young prince who had not the same motives to inspire him i had seen him and was informed of his name and birth but he had neither seen me nor knew who i was therefore what had touched him was either gratitude or the obliging expressions of my letters which i must say are no small attractives to a generous soul  in short felicia i have a mind that you should talk with him and endeavor to discover his sentiments the management of this affair which i entrust you with is of a nice quality but as you are very discreet i cannot employ any one who will give me less suspicion though i must own my weakness to you i am naturally of a jealous temper and a confidant so beautiful as you with assimirs merit might give me some apprehension were it not that you are entirely prepossessed in favor of the count of la vagne felicia threw her self at the queens feet and kissing her hand with great respect said to her i have so true a sense madam of the honor you do me when you are pleased to confide in me that i cannot easily express my acknowledgments for so high a favor but whatever ambition i have to serve your majesty i am strangely diffident of my capacity for i know that in so important an affair one cannot act too prudently which makes me fear i shall not answer the good opinion you have conceived of me what replied the queen would you yield to another the advantage of doing me a piece of service is not your affection for me great enough to prevent you from acting those faults you foresee felicia understood by what the queen said to her that her majesty would be highly disobliged should she neglect so fair an opportunity of serving her therefore considering the unhappy state of her captivity she made no other reply but that she was ready to obey her commands you must then write to assimir said the queen and desire him to meet you on the terrace adjoining my apartment where you shall entertain him with some particulars relating to me  felicia immediately retired in order to write to assimir and finding inea in her chamber she gave her an account what had passed between the queen and her then wrote her letter in these terms  though i am unknown to you my lord and you also a stranger to me i have a mighty desire to entertain you which perhaps you may think very extraordinary if you will be pleased to meet me this evening on the terrace walk next to the queen of fez s apartment i shall there explain my self more at large  felicia   this letter felicia showed to the queen who called for one of her pages and charged him to go and deliver it to assimir who as i told you before was extremely afflicted at what casilda under the disguise of don sanche had spitefully intimated concerning felicia the mean while zulema who had stayed by the prince was saying all he could to soften his distress and as he was talking to him they came to tell assimir that one of the queen of fezs pages had a letter to deliver to him this caused some emotion in the prince who looking at his friend can you conceive said he what may be the meaning of this letter if i may believe my thoughts replied zulema they persuade me some agreeable news is coming to you my lord whatever it be said the prince i desire you will speak to the page i am unwilling to see him for fear he should discover the disorder i am in  zulema readily satisfied the princes impatience he took the letter and brought it to him which he no sooner opened but knew the name and writing heavens how great was his surprise he could not conceal his transports but giving the letter back to zulema said am i in a dream or must i believe what i see is my felicia in granada whilst i am bemoaning her absence and bereft of all hopes of ever seeing her more zulema my dear zulema how can i outlive so unexpected a felicity indeed my lord replied his friend i am sensibly touched at your good fortune and heartily congratulate you but am afraid you will go to the palace of abbaicyn before your wound is healed which may prove very dangerous to you were i to hazard my life answered the prince i would not defer the pleasure of seeing her and as i am not able to write i desire you would do it for me i am assured said zulema that she does not know the condition you are in otherwise she would be very much concerned at the little care you take of a life which ought to be dear to her but i am ready to do any thing my lord to oblige you so the prince dictated these lines  you are not so great a stranger to me as you imagine adorable felicia i do not doubt but you will be convinced of it as soon as i have the pleasure of saluting you i have had the misfortune of receiving a wound which very much discomposes me yet nothing shall prevent me attending your commands   whilst the passionate prince was abandoning himself to a thousand transports of joy and impatience the page delivered his letter to the queen who having read it was seized with the deepest chagrin was any fatality like this cried she assimir is acquainted with felicia and says he will attend her though he is wounded what accident could have happened to him since yesterday sure there must needs be an intimate understanding between felicia and him though she has concealed it from me i thought her sentiments for the count of la vagne would have left me no room to apprehend any thing from her but alas how deceived have i been well i am resolved she shall neither see him nor speak to him as celima was thus reasoning with herself felicia entered her chamber assimir said the queen to her has received your letter and is very much indisposed therefore could not write to you felicia seemed concerned at his illness thinking by that means to pay her court to the queen but she could not have taken a more indirect step toward it for celima was so prepossessed with the opinion of felicias having a correspondence with the prince that the most innocent actions of this young slave in her eyes appeared criminal  the king of granada being now indisposed sent his two sons to visit celima whom they invited to take the air in the forest this queen accepted the invitation and as assimir illness had been confirmed to her by the princes mahomet and osmin she did not in the least imagine that he would venture to go abroad besides celima had observed that osmin was mightily taken with felicia which extremely pleased her for she would not have cared had all the monarchs of the universe adored that lovely captive so the prince of carency had but looked on her indifference  thus the court set out from the palace of abbaicyn followed by a great number of musical instruments all the ladies were seated in little open chariots each of them having a cavalier to drive them mahomet drove the queen of fezs chariot and osmin felicias as they were going by the palace of alhambro the queen desired she might stop a little to enquire after the kings health  zulema hearing that celima was coming to the palace told the prince she should pass under his windows and that if he was able to rise perhaps he might see felicia heavens cried the prince what would not i do for so dear a satisfaction with that he leaped out of bed and having put on some clothes went and sat in one of the balconies of his apartment where soon after he saw celima and felicia attending her osmin perceiving the prince desired this beauteous lady to take notice of him but how shall i express the motions which seized her soul when she knew him to be her lover the prince of carency on the other side was so transported that he was just going to speak to her had not zulema persuaded him to the contrary  felicia was in such a disorder that at first she knew not what to say but being extremely desirous to be informed by what chance her false lover happened to be in granada for she took him for the count of la vagne she recovered herself a little and told osmin that the person he had shown her appeared to be a stranger you judge right madam replied he for he is a genouese of the noble house of fiesques the late king having besieged jean took him prisoner and sent him to the castle of salobrena where my father my bother and i were confined there i contracted an intimate friendship with the count of la vagne that is his title and after mahomets death my father coming to the throne conceived so particular an esteem for this illustrious count that he gave him his liberty upon condition that he would not part from granada without his consent therefore he still remains with us and we are daily charmed with his noble and polite behavior  these encomiums which osmin gave to the count were very acceptable to felicia notwithstanding the reasons she had to be dissatisfied with his conduct she then asked him when the count had been taken prisoner but nothing could astonish her more than what osmin told her on that subject for either the scene which passed at sallee between olympia the count and her was a vision which she had no room to believe or what osmin was saying to her could not be sincere this made her impatient to be with inea to entertain her with this surprising adventure and she grew of a sudden so pensive that she could not make any reply to the obliging terms in which osmin addressed her what is it that troubles you divine felicia said he to her you seem very melancholy do but confide in me and i will use my best endeavors to deserve so great a favor alas my lord replied felicia with a dejected air what secret could i impart to you i am an unfortunate captive and perhaps i repine at the cruelty of that destiny from whence flows the sorrow which you perceive vouchsafe madam said osmin to accept of my service i may procure you your liberty and soon remove the cause of your uneasiness but you must at least give me leave to pay homage to your transcendent charms since they have inspired me with such sentiments as do not merit a disobliging return i conjure you amiable felicia to be favorable to me and let me feed my passion with the hopes of your affection i cannot answer your request my lord interrupted felicia i have too great a regard for you and as an evincement of it i declare that i am neither desirous to be beloved nor disposed to receive an impression it is a resolution i have made which nothing shall induce me to change therefore i entreat you my lord never to think on me more this confession extremely surpised osmin who would rather have met with more dissimulation and less cruelty but as love is always deluding he did not doubt but in time he should conquer an indifference which he thought unreasonable  the court being returned from the forest celima whose thoughts were entirely employed on her rendezvous with the prince of carency retired to her palace and felicia went to her chamber where she found inea whom she embraced tenderly and said how shall i express to you my dear the agitation of my mind the count of la vagne is here i have just seen him in the palace of alhambro it is no imagination for he saluted me so respectfully that i could not help returning the civility and i am even ashamed of having discovered my weakness to a man who has deserved my aversion but alas when love commands reason must obey i have something yet more surprising to tell you continued she i am informed he has been some months in andalusia and by the relation i have heard i find he was taken prisoner about the time that i had a dream at sallee which represented him to me engaged with the moors and vanquished osmin told me the count had been ever since in the castle of salobrena or at granada but i fancy he desired him to speak to me in that manner with a design to screen his offense for who knows whether he does not repent his unworthy behavior toward me moreover i am surpised not to see olympia here which makes me believe the moors took the count at sea and that he has not been long in these dominions it is very probable interrupted inea for what passed at sallee is not to be contradicted and perhaps he is now sorry for having disobliged you therefore you must resolve to pardon him no my dear inea replied felicia i shall never forget his ingratitude he is still dear to me i confess yet i hope in time to banish him from my heart oh heavens added she weeping what a series of misfortunes attend me i must tell you something more young osmin has declared himself my votary and you may judge how favorably i received his addresses  whilst felicia and inea were discoursing together the queen of fez sent for the governess of the slaves who as i told you before was an ugly old woman and commanded her to wrap herself in her veil and wait on the terrace for the prince of carencys arrival she charged her at the same time not to discover herself but to appear overjoyed at seeing him in case he took her for felicia it was a moonlight night and the amorous prince leaning on casilda whom he took for a young man was making as much haste toward the place appointed as his strength would permit him and perceiving at a distance a tall person walking on the terrace he did not doubt but it was his charming felicia therefore approaching her he said ah madam has fortune brought you to me again after having so long bemoaned your absence and spent days and nights endeavoring to find you i can hardly believe my eyes is it you yourself my divine mistress here transported with love and joy he went to throw off this womans veil who not being quick enough to take hold of it let it fall on the ground and discovered a face which was as ugly as felicias was beautiful  his astonishment was so great that he could not help crying out aloud and any one might have perceived by his emotion the strange disorder he was in the queen being in a closet that looked on the terrace walk easily saw the princes action and knew his voice which made her guess what had passed therefore approaching him with a majestic air i am come to your assistance prince said she taking his hand and smiling follow me i have something to tell you which is of too great a consequence to be concealed from you any longer  the queen went in first but casilda being obliged to wait without was mighty uneasy concerning what might pass between celima and the prince this inquisitive creature stayed till the governess of the slaves was retired then placed herself near the closet where she could easily hear their conversation the queen looking at the prince who was not well recovered from his surprise i have been employing my skill for you my lord said she and by the help of my books and the figures i have cast am already acquainted with some of your adventures moreover i can assure you that i interest myself very much in what concerns you and if you will be sincere with me i do not in the least doubt but i shall be able by the assistance of my powerful art to put you in a way of overcoming your ill fortune i am persuaded madam replied the prince that a sovereign who has so great an influence as your majesty may easily change my destiny without consulting the stars yet i cannot flatter myself with deserving so extraordinary a favor as an evincement of the progress i have already made said celima i know assimir is not your name and that by your birth you are nearly related to a great king  the prince of carency was amazed to hear the queen express herself in these terms and before he could make her any answer nay continued she you will own my knowledge is no fiction when i tell you that you was in misia and taken prisoner by bajazet besides whilst you were in the tower of nicopolis did not you receive very passionate letters and a considerable supply from a lady who to this hour is unknown to you the prince sighed and seeing celima waited an answer it is as your majesty says replied he and since you are so well informed of what has happened to me i beg madam you will tell me who was that charming unknown this request extremely pleased the queen who concealing her satisfaction said to him out of what motive do you desire to know this lady perhaps you may never see her that is a misfortune i fear madam interrupted the prince yet i often flatter myself that some lucky chance will convey me were she is but added the queen in an accent which discovered part of her sentiments is it possible that the memory of a person can be still dear to you who had no other attractive to engage you but her writing a few obliging letters and sending you a sum of money to pay your ransom ah madam replied he there are impressions which never can be effaced and could you conceive the torments i have endured for that unknown you would soon be convinced that one may feel the sharpest darts of love without seeing the influencing object is it then really true said the queen that you are impatient to see her and that she often imploys your thoughts i declare it is sincerely so madam answered the prince and there is nothing i wish more ardently than an opportunity of making my retributions to a lady who has conferred so high an obligation on me well prince said celima smiling i will consult with some favorable genius in order to complete your desire come to me to morrow at the same hour and you shall be farther informed of this subject the prince returned his acknowledgments to her in a most grateful manner and retired to the palace of alhambro with the disguised casilda who was waiting on the terrace  zulema impatient to know what had passed at the abbaicyn repaired soon after to the princes apartment and casilda who perceived they had some matter of importance to communicate to one another feigning to withdraw went and hid herself in a place where she could hear their conversation you think perhaps said the prince to zulema that i have seen felicia and am going to inform you of the particulars of an agreeable rendezvous but instead of that my dear friend i must tell you some demon appeared to me in the shape of an ugly old creature and that i was in the greatest astonishment when the queen of fez came upon the terrace and desired me to follow her into her closet where i no sooner entered but she endeavored to persuade me that she had acquired an extraordinary knowledge by corresponding with good and evil geniuss and in reality she told me every thing relating to my adventure at nicopolis which very much surpised me for she certainly must have been informed of it by the unknown herself whom i believe is now amongst her slaves and i cannot put it out of my head but felicia wrote to me by the queens orders  here the prince was some time silent and zulema spoke to him in these terms i begin to have a thought which appears to me very probable and you may judge of it your self my lord when i have informed you that celima herself was at nicopolis at the time that the christians were defeated by bajazet as you were of the number of the prisoners it is likely she saw you and received an impression besides if you consider the present which was sent you in the tower it could not come from a person of an inferior rank and  you give me such a light into the matter interrupted the prince as opens my eyes at once i cannot call to mind what the queen said to me the day of her arrival and the conversation we have just had together without being convinced that she is my unknown of nicopolis alas into what a labyrinth am i fallen felicia is with her and if she discovers my passion for that lovely creature i fear she will make her feel the effects of her revenge ah cruel destiny cried he am i born only to pass my days in a continual series of woes and have you decreed that i shall never be happy here the tormenting thoughts of his past disappointment came fresh to his mind and interrupting his discourse threw him into so deep a melancholy that even his friend zulema endeavored unsuccessfully to divert it therefore as it was late he took his leave of the prince though extremely concerned at not having it in his power to give him some relief  whilst the prince and zulema were entertaining each other casilda heard their whole conversation and finding she had no hopes left of ever touching the heart of a prince for whom she had already acted many extravagances she resolved on some desperate undertaking her revenge against her rival was more predominant than either the passion she had for the prince or her own honor so that nothing less than the death of the unhappy leonida could satisfy her raging spirit  the queen of fez extremely overjoyed at what the prince of carency had said to her was forming a thousand agreeable projects not doubting but his passion for his unknown of nicopolis was very sincere and that he would be equally transported to find she was the person yet as her jealousy of felicia gave her much uneasiness she thought it prudent first to clear her suspicions on that subject for said she if the prince has seen that beautiful captive he must needs love her therefore i will contrive they shall meet in a place where i may hear their discourse which will give me some insight into the matter  celima immediately sent for felicia and being alone with her i command you said she to be sincere with me consider you are my slave and that your destiny is in my power i can make you happy if you will confess the truth read this continued she showing her the letter which the prince of carency had desired zulema to write do you know the writing felicia read it and having examined it some time told the queen she sincerely could not tell whose hand it was which in some measure satisfied celima yet to be thoroughly convinced in an affair that so nearly concerned her tell me said she have you ever heard of the house of bourbon related to the kings of france felicia at this question did not doubt but the queen knew her and without being any ways out of countenance replied that the name of so illustrious a family was not unknown to her and are you acquainted with any one of that name said celima did not you see the count of la march or the prince of carency when you were in spain no madam answered she i never saw those princes they are entire strangers to me know then felicia interrupted the queen of fez that the person i spoke of and who appeared so charming to me is of the house of bourbon and is called the prince of carency i have a mind you should talk with him and endeavor to penetrate into his sentiments he came here last night when i ordered the governess of the slaves to entertain him but she managed the matter so very ill that i must wholly depend upon you had the queens thoughts been less prepossessed with her project she might have discovered felicias surprise when she heard the prince of carency was the person whom the queen loved and that he was actually in granada but her mind being otherways employed this young slave had time to recover from her disorder and said to celima your pleasure madam is so dear to me that i fear i shall not be able to effect your majestys commands with success for i have but very little experience and should i miscarry in an affair which requires so much prudence i could never forgive myself no replied the queen do not let that give you the least uneasiness i know you better than you know yourself and am persuaded you cannot do any thing amiss but as the moon shines very bright i do not think it proper you should meet the prince on the terrace because i saw many people walking there last night and it would not be convenient i should be seen with him therefore i will give orders that he may be conveyed to the grotto in the wood where you may entertain him till i come to you  felicia having received her instructions retired to her chamber very much troubled which inea peceiving lovely felicia said she do not conceal your thoughts but tell me the cause of your pain ah my dear inea cried felicia nothing but fresh afflictions attend me the prince of carency is in granada and goes by the name of assimir it is he whom the queen loves and by her command i am to have an interview with him this evening what interrupted inea can that give you any uneasiness do you consider that heaven has sent him here to put a period to your miseries he will procure you your liberty and carry you back to your native land where all your wishes will be crowned with felicity whilst unfortunate inea absent from her dear don ramire must pass the remainder of her life in tears and captivity you bewail your destiny replied felicia and you think that my being united to the prince of carency will make mine happier alas you are very much deceived for we have conceived a secret antipathy for each other and must never expect a perfect satisfaction in our alliance besides do you imagine that i can so easily banish the count of la vagne from my thoughts in spite of his infidelity he is still dear to me and it is probable he is now sorry for having offended me at least his eyes tell me so and his repentance may deserve pardon in short inea i believe he loves me but let it be as it will the prince shall not know who i am as he has seen my picture he may call to mind its resemblance therefore i will hid my face so well that he shall not see it inea finding felicia was fixed on that resolution would not any ways oppose it though she was of a contrary opinion  the prince of carency was now thinking on means to convey a letter to felicia in order to know how he might have an opportunity of entertaining her he told his design to zulema who advised him not to write for fear his letter should fall into the hands of the queen of fez but promised him he would contrive some way to speak to her by this time the hour of the princes appointment was near yet he made no great haste to go to the palace for he began to reflect that a second interview with celima would only puzzle him because he believed she was his unknown of nicopolis and that were she informed of his passion for felicia it might prove of a fatal consequence  zulema put him in mind to repair to his rendezvous at last taking the supposed don sanche with him he went with some reluctance to the abbaicyn where he found a mute waiting on the terrace who conveyed him to the grotto felicia came soon after so entirely hidden from head to foot in a large white veil that it was impossible to know her the prince did not doubt in seeing her but it was the same old woman he had met the night before which made him resolve not to have any discourse with her felicia on the other side who felt strange emotions finding her self at that instant with the prince of carency was some time without speaking but she had scarcely broke silence when the prince knowing the voice of his lovely mistress went and flung himself at her feet leonida charming leonida said he what a blessing is this have i found you at last and have you still the same obliging sentiments for me which you had when i was in the house of the traitor benavidez leonida calling to mind what had passed at sallee was grieved at this discourse go said she breaking out into a passion go ungrateful man have you forgot the cause you have given me to upbraid you the prince thinking she was angry that he had concealed his name from her i am guilty madam i confess replied he for not having confided in you i ought to have told you that i was the prince of carency and not have appeared under an other title but the cruel designs of leonora by whose orders i was pursued when i parted from villareal and wounded in the forest where you found me was the occasion i changed my name and took that of the count of la vagne whom i very much resembled this is my only crime divine leonida sure it is not so enormous as to be unpardonable whilst the prince was talking in this manner leonida whose surprise was great had a thousand different imaginations and could not tell what judgment to make at last the prince impatient to hear her speak ah madam said he how much do i dread that you are no more the same for me here you see me at your feet in transports of inexpressible joy whilst you my beauteous mistress are indifferent and melancholy what disobliging sentiments have you received for a man who adores you and whom destiny has decreed to be yours do you consider that i am going to offer up to you the remainder of my life and that from the fatal moment i lost you no torment could be equal to that i endured be assured madam that the prince of carency has a passion for you no ways inferior to that which you found in the count of la vagne i must own to you my lord replied leonida that i cannot believe what i hear for when you were at sallee you even treated me with disdain what greater offense could you give me than to abandon me as you did and go away with olympia doria whom you passionately loved do you think my senses could deceive me or that i am not capable of resenting the perfidy i cannot tell to this hour whether you are the prince of carency or the count of la vagne but what i am certain of is that you are the person who has highly injured me and it would be a shameful weakness in me to pardon you these words strangely confounded the prince who believed his dear leonidas mind was discomposed and what confirmed this opinion was his being persuaded that the count of la vagne perished at sea in his return from nicopolis and that olympia doria died in her fathers house at genoa these were circumstances he could no ways doubt of and as for his voyage to sallee he had never been there so that he looked on all her reproaches as visionary which threw him into a despairing condition yet he would not let her perceive the trouble he was in nor what occasioned it but continued speaking to her in a very obliging manner you do me a great deal of wrong charming leonida said he to her sighing and i should not find it a very hard task to justify myself though i fancy i have the most cause to complain what must i judge of the letter you writ to casilda when you and benavidez contrived your going off which was a thing i could never have believed you guilty of and what shall i conjecture from your being at constantinople and the grand seigniors passion for you leonida heard the prince with astonishment and thought likewise he knew not what he said she could not imagine how a man of so good sense could talk after such an extravagant manner and as her affection was more predominant than her resentment she was sensibly grieved at his misfortune who i my lord cried she did i write to casilda or give my consent to benavidezs insolent behavior and was i ever in turkey these things are so new to me and so far from being true that i cannot bear to hear em how long have you entertained these chimeras here she took the princes hand and could not restrain her tears which proof of her tenderness with the other circumstances so thoroughly touched him that he was soon convinced of her sincerity let us do justice to each other most amiable leonida said the prince printing an ardent kiss on her fair hand be assured i never was false to you i should be willing to satisfy you interrupted leonida could i forget the adventure which happened to me lately at sallee she then recited to him her whole story with so much wit and coherence that he perceived what he had taken for an effect of lunacy was supported by solid appearances therefore having explained matters they came to a right understanding which created unspeakable transports in these two lovers  one may easily imagine the consternation of casilda who had heard their whole discourse and was distracted to see so perfect a sympathy between leonida and the prince all her perifidiousness as well as her brothers was laid open and seeing herself frustrated of those hopes which had flattered her till then she had like in her excessive despair to have entered the grotto with a full design to stab leonida but as she considered that the prince would prevent the blow and disappoint her revengful attempt she deferred her wicked action till she found a fairer opportunity of executing it  after leonida and the prince of carency had given each other reciprocal assurances of their joy and affection they consulted how they should behave themselves toward the queen of fez till they could find an opportunity of going off while they were on this subject the queen came to the grotto but i must tell you what prevented her from repairing thither sooner  as celima was coming out of her apartment they told her that mahomet was in the palace and had something of the highest importance to communicate to her she had given orders that no body should be admitted that evening yet as that princes visit seemed to import some weighty matter she would not refuse seeing him mahomet addressing the queen told her that mula favorite to abelhamar was just arrived from fez with a letter to her from his master and that being a particular acquaintance of his he had applied to him for a private audience which if she was pleased to grant he would immediately send for him though celima was very impatient to be at her rendezvous with the prince of carency yet on this occasion she was forced to yield to her politics fearing that if she should defer this affair till the next day mahomet might suspect she was employed in some more agreeable occupation therefore having assented to mulas admittance he came and threw himself at the queens feet and presented her with a letter from the prince his master which was written in these terms  though i have an indisputable right to the kingdom of fez and am now in the possession of it yet i am willing madam to yield up one half of it to you upon condition that you will give me felicia before i had seen her nothing could be equal to my ambition but now her charms have made so deep an impression in my heart that all other passions have submitted to my transcendent love i can never be happy without her and if i am indebted to you for the possession of that lovely creature half my kingdom will be too small a return for so high an obligation therefore grant me but your slave and i will acknowledge you for my sovereign  abelhamar   celima having read this letter in the presence of mahomet they both admired abelhamars passion for felicia and as mahomets vows were already dedicated to the queen of fez he was overjoyed to find that this occasion afforded her sure means of recovering at least one part of her dominions he joined with mula in his proposals and offered to go himself with felicia to sallee in order to bring back with him such hostages from abelhamar as should warrant the performance of the treaty celima with a gracious air returned mahomet thanks and assured him she should never forget the generous manner in which he espoused her interest but as abelhamars proposals required some consideration she desired her answer might be suspended till the next day then mula withdrew and left the prince there who took so great a pleasure in entertaining the queen that he did not retire till it was late which gave time to the prince of carency and his mistress to take some measures relating to their particular affairs  mahomet having taken leave of the queen she immediately went to the grotto where being entered leonida out of respect retired and left her alone with the prince of carency this lovely captive was walking in the wood with her thoughts entirely employed on the happiness she proposed to herself through the means of her faithful lover but alas fate was preparing a new tragedy casilda still under a mans disguise distracted with jealousy at what she had just heard and seeing her rival walking alone thought she might easily pierce her heart before any one could come to her assistance so running up to her like a fury she drew out her poinard and plunged it into leonidas breast who fell with the blow crying out for help and calling the prince of carency at which name casilda was possessed with such inhuman rage that she repeated her blows the grotto not being distant the prince was struck at the mournful accents of his wounded mistress and leaving the queen suddenly he made haste toward the place where he heard leonidas voice he saw her lying on the ground bathed in blood and perceived don sanche running away which convinced him that he was the murderer he immediately pursued him and with his sword run him through after he had thus revenged unfortunate leonida he came up to her but oh what a lamentable condition did he find her in she expressed herself with painful sighs and had searce strength enough to take her lovers hand which made him fear her beauteous eyes were going to yield up all their charms to that universal conqueror death  how shall i here paint the disconsolate state of our unhappy prince he was resolved not to survive so great a misfortune and had already turned the point of his sword to his breast when the queen who had followed him out of the grotto interposed and prevented him from acting his own death she repeated her shrieks in so pressing a manner that the guards immediately came up to her and soon after most of her attendants with a great number of flambeaux which showed all the horror of this tragic scene it was not long before they were informed of it at the palace of alhambro the two princes mahomet and osmin came to the abbaicyn with mula and another gentleman who had accompanied him in his voyage from sallee in short the wood was full of people who were in a strange consternation leonida wounded lying in the arms of a despairing prince who was near losing his mistress moved all hearts with compassion  on the other hand casilda that wretched creature was tearing open her wounds to hasten her deserved death zulema approached her and still thinking she was a man ah barbarous villain that you are cried he to her what demon urged you to commit a crime so black tell me what had innocent felicia done to you and how came you to murder her in this cruel manner i am casilda replied she with a furious air and she was my rival go to your friend and he will tell you the rest these were the last and only words she pronounced with her expiring breath  though leonidas life was despaired of yet the surgeons were sent for who used all their skill to stop the bleeding of her wounds which they dressed and having assisted her with proper remedies her spirits began to revive she opened her weak eyes then fixed them on the prince who held her in his arms and appeared in as great want of relief as his dying mistress at last they took her from him and carried her by the queens order to her chamber where she was laid in bed and inea who had a tender affection for leonida staid by her almost inconsolable for the unlucky accident which had happened to her illustrious companion she was so sensibly touched at it that even the presence of don ramire could not mitigate her excessive grief he was just arrived from fez where he had been in expectation of finding his dear inea who had sent him a letter whilst he was at morocco to acquaint him with her captivity but before he could reach sallee the queen was embarked which obliged him to wait there for a favorable opportunity of coming over to granada and as about this time mula was setting out for that kingdom he took his passage in the same ship  osmin who had a real passion for leonida was thoroughly concerned at her misfortune and as for the queen of fez she could not help being moved at this dismal adventure though she prudently concealed her thoughts the prince of carencys mournful complaints too well confirmed her suspicions in relation to his sentiments for leonida and she saw him possessed with so violent a despair that she had no room left for any hopes no not even to come to an agreement with abelhamar for in the first place she was convinced that should leonida die of her wounds her death would render his proposals of no effect and on the other hand she foresaw that if she recovered the prince would claim her as one perhaps he had loved a long time and whom he intended to marry  as for mula he was so amazed that he could scarcely believe his own eyes for though he was present when his master fought the brave count of la vagne and killed him and that he saw him give up his last breath in olympias arms yet he could not be persuaded but the prince of carency was that same count so great was their resemblance  the prince all this while was like a man whose senses had abandoned him and in that condition the queen of fez gave orders that he should be carried into one of the apartments of the abbaicyn where being laid on a bed his wound opened afresh and there gushed from it a great quantity of blood which alarmed all his friends particularly osmin who looked on him as his rival and notwithstanding showed a sincere trouble for his misfortune as well as his generous friend zulema  no body could now tell who was in the greatest danger the prince of carency or leonida they both continued extremely ill his excessive grief for the condition of his beloved mistress retarded his recovery till they assured him there was hopes of her life which agreeable news caused so wonderful an effect in him that his wound was soon healed and in a few days he was able to visit her who was also in no small concern for the state of her lovers health the presence of this lovely prince had so great an influence on her that it contributed likewise to her speedy recovery his daily attendance and tender care gave her more relief than all the remedies which the surgeons applied to her wounds and it may be said that as love was the author of the pains and disasters of these constant lovers he was also their physician and comfort no satisfaction could be equal to theirs not is it possible to conceive the endearing expressions they mutually exchanged during their illness  by this time it was known through the means of inea that leonida was daughter to don john of velasco and zulema having mentioned casildas name she also informed the court of her being of the family of the benavidezs and related to them the whole story as she had heard it from leonida  as to the prince of carencys name it was not long kept a secret celima told the king of granada who he was which added so much to the esteem he had already acquired through his personal merit that he received all possible marks of honor from the king who went often to see him after this unhappy adventure and endeavoring to console the prince amongst other obliging expressions he told him he restored him to his liberty for which he desired no other ransom than his friendship and that had he known sooner of his being of the house of bourbon he would have shown him all the distinction that was due to so illustrious a family  the prince who now saw leonida out of danger was very willing to retrieve his liberty at any rate he readily accepted of the king of granadas generous offer and returned him thanks for that and the many other favors he had conferred on him since the time he was taken prisoner  celima notwithstanding leonida was her rival extremely pitied her and ordered that all the attendance imaginable should be given her she also visited the prince who laying aside the respect due to her rank received her with so much indifferency that she resolved never more to speak to him of his unknown of nicopolis  the mean while the king of granada who was desirous to complete the prince of carencys good fortune and had a design at the same time to oblige the spaniards thought on means to procure leonida her liberty he therefore addressed himself to the queen of fez offering her whatever sum she would please to demand for the ransom of that young lady but celima whose greatness of spirit was equal to her passion resolved no sovereign should surpass her in generosity the prince of carency being a christian and in love with her slave was enough to make her determine never to think of him more she told the king of granada that far from requiring any ransom for leonida she desired he would accept and dispose of her as he thought fit and that not only leonida but all the rest of her slaves were at his command if agreeable to him the king heard with pleasure celimas answer and in his turn gallantly presented leonida to the prince of carency who received her with inexpressible marks of joy and gratitude but could not find words to make a retribution suitable to the present  the chief and only care of these happy lovers consisted now in giving each other daily proofs of their tender affection their long and cruel disappointments made their felicity the greater and though they were not as yet perfectly recovered they were proposing means to leave granada in order to perform the promise which their parents had made for them in their infant years the prince wrote to don john of velasco at villareal acquainting him with the particulars of his and leonidas fortune and withal that he hoped soon to be the happiest of mankind  mula seeing his masters designs were rendered impracticable through this adventure between the prince of carency and leonida went back to sallee and gave abelhamar an account of what had passed which news so cruelly affected him that the loss of his mistress had like to have made him act his own death but as an evincement of the greatness of his passion he took a resolution proportionable to it for having renounced to the crown of fez he retired to a castle on the seaside where he consecrated the remainder of his life to the dear memory of his felicia celima soon received advice of this unexpected change and as mahomet was extremely sollicitous to serve her in so favorable a conjuncture he entreated the king of granada his father to give him a fleet and some forces in order to reinstate the queen of fez which being granted he took the command entirely upon himself and convoyed her to sallee where far from meeting with any opposition she found all things in a perfect tranquillity by this time her mind was more at ease for having considered that she could no longer hope to receive an obliging return to the passion she had for the prince of carency she thought nothing would sooner effect it is cure than approving mahomets vows therefore being of too haughty a temper to bear with the disdain of the one and gratitude pleading in behalf of the other she at once resolved to give her hand and all her affection to mahomet who by this alliance saw his love and ambition satisfied  celima before she parted from granada restored inea to her liberty and don ramire took her with him to toledo where these two lovers by a happy union received the reward of their constancy  what i have farther to add relating to the prince of carency and leonida is that as soon as they were in a condition to set out on their journey they took leave of the king of granada who made them considerable presents and ordered several noblemen with a strong detachment of his guards to conduct them as far as the frontiers of spain whence they proceeded to villa real where they were received with a satisfaction equal to the occasion their long sufferings entitled them to such blessings as hardly any who wore the chains of love could expect leonida in whom so many perfections were assembled was too great a prize for an indifferent hero and the prince of carency whose accomplishments rendered him one of the finest gentlemen of his time might justly claim a place in her affection in short where so much virtue and merit was united love must be triumphant then let us leave the prince and leonida to the bounteous care of hymen whose soft endearments could only recompense their past misfortunes and crown their days with true felicity  finis
